crsnk10{_}85{_}FOR PUBLIC DOMAIN ETEXTS*Ver.04.29.93*END*     THE CRUISE OF THE "SNARK"     CHAPTER I--FOREWORD    It began in the swimming pool at Glen Ellen.
crsnk10{_}86{_}Between swims it was our wont to come out and lie in the sand and let our skins breathe the warm air and soak in the sunshine.
crsnk10{_}87{_}Roscoe was a yachtsman.
crsnk10{_}88{_}I had followed the sea a bit.
crsnk10{_}89{_}It was inevitable that we should talk about boats.
crsnk10{_}90{_}We talked about small boats, and the seaworthiness of small boats.
crsnk10{_}91{_}We instanced Captain Slocum and his three years' voyage around the world in the Spray.
crsnk10{_}92{_}We asserted that we were not afraid to go around the world in a small boat, say forty feet long.
crsnk10{_}93{_}We asserted furthermore that we would like to do it.
crsnk10{_}94{_}We asserted finally that there was nothing in this world we'd like better than a chance to do it.
crsnk10{_}95{_}"Let us do it," we said .
crsnk10{_}96{_}.
crsnk10{_}97{_}.
crsnk10{_}98{_}in fun.
crsnk10{_}99{_}Then I asked Charmian privily if she'd really care to do it, and she said that it was too good to be true.
crsnk10{_}100{_}The next time we breathed our skins in the sand by the swimming pool I said to Roscoe, "Let us do it."
crsnk10{_}101{_}I was in earnest, and so was he, for he said:  "When shall we start?"
crsnk10{_}102{_}I had a house to build on the ranch, also an orchard, a vineyard, and several hedges to plant, and a number of other things to do.
crsnk10{_}103{_}We thought we would start in four or five years.
crsnk10{_}104{_}Then the lure of the adventure began to grip us.
crsnk10{_}105{_}Why not start at once?
crsnk10{_}106{_}We'd never be younger, any of us.
crsnk10{_}107{_}Let the orchard, vineyard, and hedges be growing up while we were away.
crsnk10{_}108{_}When we came back, they would be ready for us, and we could live in the barn while we built the house.
crsnk10{_}109{_}So the trip was decided upon, and the building of the Snark began.
crsnk10{_}110{_}We named her the Snark because we could not think of any other name- -this information is given for the benefit of those who otherwise might think there is something occult in the name.
crsnk10{_}111{_}Our friends cannot understand why we make this voyage.
crsnk10{_}112{_}They shudder, and moan, and raise their hands.
crsnk10{_}113{_}No amount of explanation can make them comprehend that we are moving along the line of least resistance; that it is easier for us to go down to the sea in a small ship than to remain on dry land, just as it is easier for them to remain on dry land than to go down to the sea in the small ship.
crsnk10{_}114{_}This state of mind comes of an undue prominence of the ego.
crsnk10{_}115{_}They cannot get away from themselves.
crsnk10{_}116{_}They cannot come out of themselves long enough to see that their line of least resistance is not necessarily everybody else's line of least resistance.
crsnk10{_}117{_}They make of their own bundle of desires, likes, and dislikes a yardstick wherewith to measure the desires, likes, and dislikes of all creatures.
crsnk10{_}118{_}This is unfair.
crsnk10{_}119{_}I tell them so.
crsnk10{_}120{_}But they cannot get away from their own miserable egos long enough to hear me.
crsnk10{_}121{_}They think I am crazy.
crsnk10{_}122{_}In return, I am sympathetic.
crsnk10{_}123{_}It is a state of mind familiar to me.
crsnk10{_}124{_}We are all prone to think there is something wrong with the mental processes of the man who disagrees with us.
crsnk10{_}125{_}The ultimate word is I LIKE.
crsnk10{_}126{_}It lies beneath philosophy, and is twined about the heart of life.
crsnk10{_}127{_}When philosophy has maundered ponderously for a month, telling the individual what he must do, the individual says, in an instant, "I LIKE," and does something else, and philosophy goes glimmering.
crsnk10{_}128{_}It is I LIKE that makes the drunkard drink and the martyr wear a hair shirt; that makes one man a reveller and another man an anchorite; that makes one man pursue fame, another gold, another love, and another God.
crsnk10{_}129{_}Philosophy is very often a man's way of explaining his own I LIKE.
crsnk10{_}130{_}But to return to the Snark, and why I, for one, want to journey in her around the world.
crsnk10{_}131{_}The things I like constitute my set of values.
crsnk10{_}132{_}The thing I like most of all is personal achievement--not achievement for the world's applause, but achievement for my own delight.
crsnk10{_}133{_}It is the old "I did it!
crsnk10{_}134{_}I did it!
crsnk10{_}135{_}With my own hands I did it!"
crsnk10{_}136{_}But personal achievement, with me, must be concrete.
crsnk10{_}137{_}I'd rather win a water-fight in the swimming pool, or remain astride a horse that is trying to get out from under me, than write the great American novel.
crsnk10{_}138{_}Each man to his liking.
crsnk10{_}139{_}Some other fellow would prefer writing the great American novel to winning the water-fight or mastering the horse.
crsnk10{_}140{_}Possibly the proudest achievement of my life, my moment of highest living, occurred when I was seventeen.
crsnk10{_}141{_}I was in a three-masted schooner off the coast of Japan.
crsnk10{_}142{_}We were in a typhoon.
crsnk10{_}143{_}All hands had been on deck most of the night.
crsnk10{_}144{_}I was called from my bunk at seven in the morning to take the wheel.
crsnk10{_}145{_}Not a stitch of canvas was set.
crsnk10{_}146{_}We were running before it under bare poles, yet the schooner fairly tore along.
crsnk10{_}147{_}The seas were all of an eighth of a mile apart, and the wind snatched the whitecaps from their summits, filling.
crsnk10{_}148{_}The air so thick with driving spray that it was impossible to see more than two waves at a time.
crsnk10{_}149{_}The schooner was almost unmanageable, rolling her rail under to starboard and to port, veering and yawing anywhere between south-east and south-west, and threatening, when the huge seas lifted under her quarter, to broach to.
crsnk10{_}150{_}Had she broached to, she would ultimately have been reported lost with all hands and no tidings.
crsnk10{_}151{_}I took the wheel.
crsnk10{_}152{_}The sailing-master watched me for a space.
crsnk10{_}153{_}He was afraid of my youth, feared that I lacked the strength and the nerve.
crsnk10{_}154{_}But when he saw me successfully wrestle the schooner through several bouts, he went below to breakfast.
crsnk10{_}155{_}Fore and aft, all hands were below at breakfast.
crsnk10{_}156{_}Had she broached to, not one of them would ever have reached the deck.
crsnk10{_}157{_}For forty minutes I stood there alone at the wheel, in my grasp the wildly careering schooner and the lives of twenty-two men.
crsnk10{_}158{_}Once we were pooped.
crsnk10{_}159{_}I saw it coming, and, half-drowned, with tons of water crushing me, I checked the schooner's rush to broach to.
crsnk10{_}160{_}At the end of the hour, sweating and played out, I was relieved.
crsnk10{_}161{_}But I had done it!
crsnk10{_}162{_}With my own hands I had done my trick at the wheel and guided a hundred tons of wood and iron through a few million tons of wind and waves.
crsnk10{_}163{_}My delight was in that I had done it--not in the fact that twenty- two men knew I had done it.
crsnk10{_}164{_}Within the year over half of them were dead and gone, yet my pride in the thing performed was not diminished by half.
crsnk10{_}165{_}I am willing to confess, however, that I do like a small audience.
crsnk10{_}166{_}But it must be a very small audience, composed of those who love me and whom I love.
crsnk10{_}167{_}When I then accomplish personal achievement, I have a feeling that I am justifying their love for me.
crsnk10{_}168{_}But this is quite apart from the delight of the achievement itself.
crsnk10{_}169{_}This delight is peculiarly my own and does not depend upon witnesses.
crsnk10{_}170{_}When I have done some such thing, I am exalted.
crsnk10{_}171{_}I glow all over.
crsnk10{_}172{_}I am aware of a pride in myself that is mine, and mine alone.
crsnk10{_}173{_}It is organic.
crsnk10{_}174{_}Every fibre of me is thrilling with it.
crsnk10{_}175{_}It is very natural.
crsnk10{_}176{_}It is a mere matter of satisfaction at adjustment to environment.
crsnk10{_}177{_}It is success.
crsnk10{_}178{_}Life that lives is life successful, and success is the breath of its nostrils.
crsnk10{_}179{_}The achievement of a difficult feat is successful adjustment to a sternly exacting environment.
crsnk10{_}180{_}The more difficult the feat, the greater the satisfaction at its accomplishment.
crsnk10{_}181{_}Thus it is with the man who leaps forward from the springboard, out over the swimming pool, and with a backward half-revolution of the body, enters the water head first.
crsnk10{_}182{_}Once he leaves the springboard his environment becomes immediately savage, and savage the penalty it will exact should he fail and strike the water flat.
crsnk10{_}183{_}Of course, the man does not have to run the risk of the penalty.
crsnk10{_}184{_}He could remain on the bank in a sweet and placid environment of summer air, sunshine, and stability.
crsnk10{_}185{_}Only he is not made that way.
crsnk10{_}186{_}In that swift mid-air moment he lives as he could never live on the bank.
crsnk10{_}187{_}As for myself, I'd rather be that man than the fellows who sit on the bank and watch him.
crsnk10{_}188{_}That is why I am building the Snark.
crsnk10{_}189{_}I am so made.
crsnk10{_}190{_}I like, that is all.
crsnk10{_}191{_}The trip around the world means big moments of living.
crsnk10{_}192{_}Bear with me a moment and look at it.
crsnk10{_}193{_}Here am I, a little animal called a man--a bit of vitalized matter, one hundred and sixty-five pounds of meat and blood, nerve, sinew, bones, and brain,--all of it soft and tender, susceptible to hurt, fallible, and frail.
crsnk10{_}194{_}I strike a light back-handed blow on the nose of an obstreperous horse, and a bone in my hand is broken.
crsnk10{_}195{_}I put my head under the water for five minutes, and I am drowned.
crsnk10{_}196{_}I fall twenty feet through the air, and I am smashed.
crsnk10{_}197{_}I am a creature of temperature.
crsnk10{_}198{_}A few degrees one way, and my fingers and ears and toes blacken and drop off.
crsnk10{_}199{_}A few degrees the other way, and my skin blisters and shrivels away from the raw, quivering flesh.
crsnk10{_}200{_}A few additional degrees either way, and the life and the light in me go out.
crsnk10{_}201{_}A drop of poison injected into my body from a snake, and I cease to move--for ever I cease to move.
crsnk10{_}202{_}A splinter of lead from a rifle enters my head, and I am wrapped around in the eternal blackness.
crsnk10{_}203{_}Fallible and frail, a bit of pulsating, jelly-like life--it is all I am.
crsnk10{_}204{_}About me are the great natural forces--colossal menaces, Titans of destruction, unsentimental monsters that have less concern for me than I have for the grain of sand I crush under my foot.
crsnk10{_}205{_}They have no concern at all for me.
crsnk10{_}206{_}They do not know me.
crsnk10{_}207{_}They are unconscious, unmerciful, and unmoral.
crsnk10{_}208{_}They are the cyclones and tornadoes, lightning flashes and cloud-bursts, tide-rips and tidal waves, undertows and waterspouts, great whirls and sucks and eddies, earthquakes and volcanoes, surfs that thunder on rock-ribbed coasts and seas that leap aboard the largest crafts that float, crushing humans to pulp or licking them off into the sea and to death--and these insensate monsters do not know that tiny sensitive creature, all nerves and weaknesses, whom men call Jack London, and who himself thinks he is all right and quite a superior being.
crsnk10{_}209{_}In the maze and chaos of the conflict of these vast and draughty Titans, it is for me to thread my precarious way.
crsnk10{_}210{_}The bit of life that is I will exult over them.
crsnk10{_}211{_}The bit of life that is I, in so far as it succeeds in baffling them or in bitting them to its service, will imagine that it is godlike.
crsnk10{_}212{_}It is good to ride the tempest and feel godlike.
crsnk10{_}213{_}I dare to assert that for a finite speck of pulsating jelly to feel godlike is a far more glorious feeling than for a god to feel godlike.
crsnk10{_}214{_}Here is the sea, the wind, and the wave.
crsnk10{_}215{_}Here are the seas, the winds, and the waves of all the world.
crsnk10{_}216{_}Here is ferocious environment.
crsnk10{_}217{_}And here is difficult adjustment, the achievement of which is delight to the small quivering vanity that is I.  I like.
crsnk10{_}218{_}I am so made.
crsnk10{_}219{_}It is my own particular form of vanity, that is all.
crsnk10{_}220{_}There is also another side to the voyage of the Snark.
crsnk10{_}221{_}Being alive, I want to see, and all the world is a bigger thing to see than one small town or valley.
crsnk10{_}222{_}We have done little outlining of the voyage.
crsnk10{_}223{_}Only one thing is definite, and that is that our first port of call will be Honolulu.
crsnk10{_}224{_}Beyond a few general ideas, we have no thought of our next port after Hawaii.
crsnk10{_}225{_}We shall make up our minds as we get nearer, in a general way we know that we shall wander through the South Seas, take in Samoa, New Zealand, Tasmania, Australia, New Guinea, Borneo, and Sumatra, and go on up through the Philippines to Japan.
crsnk10{_}226{_}Then will come Korea, China, India, the Red Sea, and the Mediterranean.
crsnk10{_}227{_}After that the voyage becomes too vague to describe, though we know a number of things we shall surely do, and we expect to spend from one to several months in every country in Europe.
crsnk10{_}228{_}The Snark is to be sailed.
crsnk10{_}229{_}There will be a gasolene engine on board, but it will be used only in case of emergency, such as in bad water among reefs and shoals, where a sudden calm in a swift current leaves a sailing-boat helpless.
crsnk10{_}230{_}The rig of the Snark is to be what is called the "ketch."
crsnk10{_}231{_}The ketch rig is a compromise between the yawl and the schooner.
crsnk10{_}232{_}Of late years the yawl rig has proved the best for cruising.
crsnk10{_}233{_}The ketch retains the cruising virtues of the yawl, and in addition manages to embrace a few of the sailing virtues of the schooner.
crsnk10{_}234{_}The foregoing must be taken with a pinch of salt.
crsnk10{_}235{_}It is all theory in my head.
crsnk10{_}236{_}I've never sailed a ketch, nor even seen one.
crsnk10{_}237{_}The theory commends itself to me.
crsnk10{_}238{_}Wait till I get out on the ocean, then I'll be able to tell more about the cruising and sailing qualities of the ketch.
crsnk10{_}239{_}As originally planned, the Snark was to be forty feet long on the water-line.
crsnk10{_}240{_}But we discovered there was no space for a bath-room, and for that reason we have increased her length to forty-five feet.
crsnk10{_}241{_}Her greatest beam is fifteen feet.
crsnk10{_}242{_}She has no house and no hold.
crsnk10{_}243{_}There is six feet of headroom, and the deck is unbroken save for two companionways and a hatch for'ard.
crsnk10{_}244{_}The fact that there is no house to break the strength of the deck will make us feel safer in case great seas thunder their tons of water down on board.
crsnk10{_}245{_}A large and roomy cockpit, sunk beneath the deck, with high rail and self- bailing, will make our rough-weather days and nights more comfortable.
crsnk10{_}246{_}There will be no crew.
crsnk10{_}247{_}Or, rather, Charmian, Roscoe, and I are the crew.
crsnk10{_}248{_}We are going to do the thing with our own hands.
crsnk10{_}249{_}With our own hands we're going to circumnavigate the globe.
crsnk10{_}250{_}Sail her or sink her, with our own hands we'll do it.
crsnk10{_}251{_}Of course there will be a cook and a cabin-boy.
crsnk10{_}252{_}Why should we stew over a stove, wash dishes, and set the table?
crsnk10{_}253{_}We could stay on land if we wanted to do those things.
crsnk10{_}254{_}Besides, we've got to stand watch and work the ship.
crsnk10{_}255{_}And also, I've got to work at my trade of writing in order to feed us and to get new sails and tackle and keep the Snark in efficient working order.
crsnk10{_}256{_}And then there's the ranch; I've got to keep the vineyard, orchard, and hedges growing.
crsnk10{_}257{_}When we increased the length of the Snark in order to get space for a bath-room, we found that all the space was not required by the bath-room.
crsnk10{_}258{_}Because of this, we increased the size of the engine.
crsnk10{_}259{_}Seventy horse-power our engine is, and since we expect it to drive us along at a nine-knot clip, we do not know the name of a river with a current swift enough to defy us.
crsnk10{_}260{_}We expect to do a lot of inland work.
crsnk10{_}261{_}The smallness of the Snark makes this possible.
crsnk10{_}262{_}When we enter the land, out go the masts and on goes the engine.
crsnk10{_}263{_}There are the canals of China, and the Yang-tse River.
crsnk10{_}264{_}We shall spend months on them if we can get permission from the government.
crsnk10{_}265{_}That will be the one obstacle to our inland voyaging--governmental permission.
crsnk10{_}266{_}But if we can get that permission, there is scarcely a limit to the inland voyaging we can do.
crsnk10{_}267{_}When we come to the Nile, why we can go up the Nile.
crsnk10{_}268{_}We can go up the Danube to Vienna, up the Thames to London, and we can go up the Seine to Paris and moor opposite the Latin Quarter with a bow-line out to Notre Dame and a stern-line fast to the Morgue.
crsnk10{_}269{_}We can leave the Mediterranean and go up the Rhone to Lyons, there enter the Saone, cross from the Saone to the Maine through the Canal de Bourgogne, and from the Marne enter the Seine and go out the Seine at Havre.
crsnk10{_}270{_}When we cross the Atlantic to the United States, we can go up the Hudson, pass through the Erie Canal, cross the Great Lakes, leave Lake Michigan at Chicago, gain the Mississippi by way of the Illinois River and the connecting canal, and go down the Mississippi to the Gulf of Mexico.
crsnk10{_}271{_}And then there are the great rivers of South America.
crsnk10{_}272{_}We'll know something about geography when we get back to California.
crsnk10{_}273{_}People that build houses are often sore perplexed; but if they enjoy the strain of it, I'll advise them to build a boat like the Snark.
crsnk10{_}274{_}Just consider, for a moment, the strain of detail.
crsnk10{_}275{_}Take the engine.
crsnk10{_}276{_}What is the best kind of engine--the two cycle?
crsnk10{_}277{_}three cycle?
crsnk10{_}278{_}four cycle?
crsnk10{_}279{_}My lips are mutilated with all kinds of strange jargon, my mind is mutilated with still stranger ideas and is foot-sore and weary from travelling in new and rocky realms of thought.--Ignition methods; shall it be make-and-break or jump-spark?
crsnk10{_}280{_}Shall dry cells or storage batteries be used?
crsnk10{_}281{_}A storage battery commends itself, but it requires a dynamo.
crsnk10{_}282{_}How powerful a dynamo?
crsnk10{_}283{_}And when we have installed a dynamo and a storage battery, it is simply ridiculous not to light the boat with electricity.
crsnk10{_}284{_}Then comes the discussion of how many lights and how many candle-power.
crsnk10{_}285{_}It is a splendid idea.
crsnk10{_}286{_}But electric lights will demand a more powerful storage battery, which, in turn, demands a more powerful dynamo.
crsnk10{_}287{_}And now that we've gone in for it, why not have a searchlight?
crsnk10{_}288{_}It would be tremendously useful.
crsnk10{_}289{_}But the searchlight needs so much electricity that when it runs it will put all the other lights out of commission.
crsnk10{_}290{_}Again we travel the weary road in the quest after more power for storage battery and dynamo.
crsnk10{_}291{_}And then, when it is finally solved, some one asks, "What if the engine breaks down?"
crsnk10{_}292{_}And we collapse.
crsnk10{_}293{_}There are the sidelights, the binnacle light, and the anchor light.
crsnk10{_}294{_}Our very lives depend upon them.
crsnk10{_}295{_}So we have to fit the boat throughout with oil lamps as well.
crsnk10{_}296{_}But we are not done with that engine yet.
crsnk10{_}297{_}The engine is powerful.
crsnk10{_}298{_}We are two small men and a small woman.
crsnk10{_}299{_}It will break our hearts and our backs to hoist anchor by hand.
crsnk10{_}300{_}Let the engine do it.
crsnk10{_}301{_}And then comes the problem of how to convey power for'ard from the engine to the winch.
crsnk10{_}302{_}And by the time all this is settled, we redistribute the allotments of space to the engine-room, galley, bath-room, state-rooms, and cabin, and begin all over again.
crsnk10{_}303{_}And when we have shifted the engine, I send off a telegram of gibberish to its makers at New York, something like this:  Toggle-joint abandoned change thrust-bearing accordingly distance from forward side of flywheel to face of stern post sixteen feet six inches.
crsnk10{_}304{_}Just potter around in quest of the best steering gear, or try to decide whether you will set up your rigging with old-fashioned lanyards or with turnbuckles, if you want strain of detail.
crsnk10{_}305{_}Shall the binnacle be located in front of the wheel in the centre of the beam, or shall it be located to one side in front of the wheel?-- there's room right there for a library of sea-dog controversy.
crsnk10{_}306{_}Then there's the problem of gasolene, fifteen hundred gallons of it--what are the safest ways to tank it and pipe it?
crsnk10{_}307{_}and which is the best fire-extinguisher for a gasolene fire?
crsnk10{_}308{_}Then there is the pretty problem of the life-boat and the stowage of the same.
crsnk10{_}309{_}And when that is finished, come the cook and cabin-boy to confront one with nightmare possibilities.
crsnk10{_}310{_}It is a small boat, and we'll be packed close together.
crsnk10{_}311{_}The servant-girl problem of landsmen pales to insignificance.
crsnk10{_}312{_}We did select one cabin-boy, and by that much were our troubles eased.
crsnk10{_}313{_}And then the cabin-boy fell in love and resigned.
crsnk10{_}314{_}And in the meanwhile how is a fellow to find time to study navigation--when he is divided between these problems and the earning of the money wherewith to settle the problems?
crsnk10{_}315{_}Neither Roscoe nor I know anything about navigation, and the summer is gone, and we are about to start, and the problems are thicker than ever, and the treasury is stuffed with emptiness.
crsnk10{_}316{_}Well, anyway, it takes years to learn seamanship, and both of us are seamen.
crsnk10{_}317{_}If we don't find the time, we'll lay in the books and instruments and teach ourselves navigation on the ocean between San Francisco and Hawaii.
crsnk10{_}318{_}There is one unfortunate and perplexing phase of the voyage of the Snark.
crsnk10{_}319{_}Roscoe, who is to be my co-navigator, is a follower of one, Cyrus R. Teed.
crsnk10{_}320{_}Now Cyrus R. Teed has a different cosmology from the one generally accepted, and Roscoe shares his views.
crsnk10{_}321{_}Wherefore Roscoe believes that the surface of the earth is concave and that we live on the inside of a hollow sphere.
crsnk10{_}322{_}Thus, though we shall sail on the one boat, the Snark, Roscoe will journey around the world on the inside, while I shall journey around on the outside.
crsnk10{_}323{_}But of this, more anon.
crsnk10{_}324{_}We threaten to be of the one mind before the voyage is completed.
crsnk10{_}325{_}I am confident that I shall convert him into making the journey on the outside, while he is equally confident that before we arrive back in San Francisco I shall be on the inside of the earth.
crsnk10{_}326{_}How he is going to get me through the crust I don't know, but Roscoe is ay a masterful man.
crsnk10{_}327{_}P.S.--That engine!
crsnk10{_}328{_}While we've got it, and the dynamo, and the storage battery, why not have an ice-machine?
crsnk10{_}329{_}Ice in the tropics!
crsnk10{_}330{_}It is more necessary than bread.
crsnk10{_}331{_}Here goes for the ice-machine!
crsnk10{_}332{_}Now I am plunged into chemistry, and my lips hurt, and my mind hurts, and how am I ever to find the time to study navigation?
crsnk10{_}333{_}CHAPTER II--THE INCONCEIVABLE AND MONSTROUS    "Spare no money," I said to Roscoe.
crsnk10{_}334{_}"Let everything on the Snark be of the best.
crsnk10{_}335{_}And never mind decoration.
crsnk10{_}336{_}Plain pine boards is good enough finishing for me.
crsnk10{_}337{_}But put the money into the construction.
crsnk10{_}338{_}Let the Snark be as staunch and strong as any boat afloat.
crsnk10{_}339{_}Never mind what it costs to make her staunch and strong; you see that she is made staunch and strong, and I'll go on writing and earning the money to pay for it."
crsnk10{_}340{_}And I did .
crsnk10{_}341{_}.
crsnk10{_}342{_}.
crsnk10{_}343{_}as well as I could; for the Snark ate up money faster than I could earn it.
crsnk10{_}344{_}In fact, every little while I had to borrow money with which to supplement my earnings.
crsnk10{_}345{_}Now I borrowed one thousand dollars, now I borrowed two thousand dollars, and now I borrowed five thousand dollars.
crsnk10{_}346{_}And all the time I went on working every day and sinking the earnings in the venture.
crsnk10{_}347{_}I worked Sundays as well, and I took no holidays.
crsnk10{_}348{_}But it was worth it.
crsnk10{_}349{_}Every time I thought of the Snark I knew she was worth it.
crsnk10{_}350{_}For know, gentle reader, the staunchness of the Snark.
crsnk10{_}351{_}She is forty-five feet long on the waterline.
crsnk10{_}352{_}Her garboard strake is three inches thick; her planking two and one-half inches thick; her deck- planking two inches thick and in all her planking there are no butts.
crsnk10{_}353{_}I know, for I ordered that planking especially from Puget Sound.
crsnk10{_}354{_}Then the Snark has four water-tight compartments, which is to say that her length is broken by three water-tight bulkheads.
crsnk10{_}355{_}Thus, no matter how large a leak the Snark may spring, Only one compartment can fill with water.
crsnk10{_}356{_}The other three compartments will keep her afloat, anyway, and, besides, will enable us to mend the leak.
crsnk10{_}357{_}There is another virtue in these bulkheads.
crsnk10{_}358{_}The last compartment of all, in the very stern, contains six tanks that carry over one thousand gallons of gasolene.
crsnk10{_}359{_}Now gasolene is a very dangerous article to carry in bulk on a small craft far out on the wide ocean.
crsnk10{_}360{_}But when the six tanks that do not leak are themselves contained in a compartment hermetically sealed off from the rest of the boat, the danger will be seen to be very small indeed.
crsnk10{_}361{_}The Snark is a sail-boat.
crsnk10{_}362{_}She was built primarily to sail.
crsnk10{_}363{_}But incidentally, as an auxiliary, a seventy-horse-power engine was installed.
crsnk10{_}364{_}This is a good, strong engine.
crsnk10{_}365{_}I ought to know.
crsnk10{_}366{_}I paid for it to come out all the way from New York City.
crsnk10{_}367{_}Then, on deck, above the engine, is a windlass.
crsnk10{_}368{_}It is a magnificent affair.
crsnk10{_}369{_}It weighs several hundred pounds and takes up no end of deck-room.
crsnk10{_}370{_}You see, it is ridiculous to hoist up anchor by hand-power when there is a seventy-horse-power engine on board.
crsnk10{_}371{_}So we installed the windlass, transmitting power to it from the engine by means of a gear and castings specially made in a San Francisco foundry.
crsnk10{_}372{_}The Snark was made for comfort, and no expense was spared in this regard.
crsnk10{_}373{_}There is the bath-room, for instance, small and compact, it is true, but containing all the conveniences of any bath-room upon land.
crsnk10{_}374{_}The bath-room is a beautiful dream of schemes and devices, pumps, and levers, and sea-valves.
crsnk10{_}375{_}Why, in the course of its building, I used to lie awake nights thinking about that bath-room.
crsnk10{_}376{_}And next to the bathroom come the life-boat and the launch.
crsnk10{_}377{_}They are carried on deck, and they take up what little space might have been left us for exercise.
crsnk10{_}378{_}But then, they beat life insurance; and the prudent man, even if he has built as staunch and strong a craft as the Snark, will see to it that he has a good life-boat as well.
crsnk10{_}379{_}And ours is a good one.
crsnk10{_}380{_}It is a dandy.
crsnk10{_}381{_}It was stipulated to cost one hundred and fifty dollars, and when I came to pay the bill, it turned out to be three hundred and ninety-five dollars.
crsnk10{_}382{_}That shows how good a life-boat it is.
crsnk10{_}383{_}I could go on at great length relating the various virtues and excellences of the Snark, but I refrain.
crsnk10{_}384{_}I have bragged enough as it is, and I have bragged to a purpose, as will be seen before my tale is ended.
crsnk10{_}385{_}And please remember its title, "The Inconceivable and Monstrous."
crsnk10{_}386{_}It was planned that the Snark should sail on October 1, 1906.
crsnk10{_}387{_}That she did not so sail was inconceivable and monstrous.
crsnk10{_}388{_}There was no valid reason for not sailing except that she was not ready to sail, and there was no conceivable reason why she was not ready.
crsnk10{_}389{_}She was promised on November first, on November fifteenth, on December first; and yet she was never ready.
crsnk10{_}390{_}On December first Charmian and I left the sweet, clean Sonoma country and came down to live in the stifling city--but not for long, oh, no, only for two weeks, for we would sail on December fifteenth.
crsnk10{_}391{_}And I guess we ought to know, for Roscoe said so, and it was on his advice that we came to the city to stay two weeks.
crsnk10{_}392{_}Alas, the two weeks went by, four weeks went by, six weeks went by, eight weeks went by, and we were farther away from sailing than ever.
crsnk10{_}393{_}Explain it?
crsnk10{_}394{_}Who?--me?
crsnk10{_}395{_}I can't.
crsnk10{_}396{_}It is the one thing in all my life that I have backed down on.
crsnk10{_}397{_}There is no explaining it; if there were, I'd do it.
crsnk10{_}398{_}I, who am an artisan of speech, confess my inability to explain why the Snark was not ready.
crsnk10{_}399{_}As I have said, and as I must repeat, it was inconceivable and monstrous.
crsnk10{_}400{_}The eight weeks became sixteen weeks, and then, one day, Roscoe cheered us up by saying:  "If we don't sail before April first, you can use my head for a football."
crsnk10{_}401{_}Two weeks later he said, "I'm getting my head in training for that match."
crsnk10{_}402{_}"Never mind," Charmian and I said to each other; "think of the wonderful boat it is going to be when it is completed."
crsnk10{_}403{_}Whereat we would rehearse for our mutual encouragement the manifold virtues and excellences of the Snark.
crsnk10{_}404{_}Also, I would borrow more money, and I would get down closer to my desk and write harder, and I refused heroically to take a Sunday off and go out into the hills with my friends.
crsnk10{_}405{_}I was building a boat, and by the eternal it was going to be a boat, and a boat spelled out all in capitals--B--O--A- -T; and no matter what it cost I didn't care.
crsnk10{_}406{_}So long as it was a BOAT.
crsnk10{_}407{_}And, oh, there is one other excellence of the Snark, upon which I must brag, namely, her bow.
crsnk10{_}408{_}No sea could ever come over it.
crsnk10{_}409{_}It laughs at the sea, that bow does; it challenges the sea; it snorts defiance at the sea.
crsnk10{_}410{_}And withal it is a beautiful bow; the lines of it are dreamlike; I doubt if ever a boat was blessed with a more beautiful and at the same time a more capable bow.
crsnk10{_}411{_}It was made to punch storms.
crsnk10{_}412{_}To touch that bow is to rest one's hand on the cosmic nose of things.
crsnk10{_}413{_}To look at it is to realize that expense cut no figure where it was concerned.
crsnk10{_}414{_}And every time our sailing was delayed, or a new expense was tacked on, we thought of that wonderful bow and were content.
crsnk10{_}415{_}The Snark is a small boat.
crsnk10{_}416{_}When I figured seven thousand dollars as her generous cost, I was both generous and correct.
crsnk10{_}417{_}I have built barns and houses, and I know the peculiar trait such things have of running past their estimated cost.
crsnk10{_}418{_}This knowledge was mine, was already mine, when I estimated the probable cost of the building of the Snark at seven thousand dollars.
crsnk10{_}419{_}Well, she cost thirty thousand.
crsnk10{_}420{_}Now don't ask me, please.
crsnk10{_}421{_}It is the truth.
crsnk10{_}422{_}I signed the cheques and I raised the money.
crsnk10{_}423{_}Of course there is no explaining it, inconceivable and monstrous is what it is, as you will agree, I know, ere my tale is done.
crsnk10{_}424{_}Then there was the matter of delay.
crsnk10{_}425{_}I dealt with forty-seven different kinds of union men and with one hundred and fifteen different firms.
crsnk10{_}426{_}And not one union man and not one firm of all the union men and all the firms ever delivered anything at the time agreed upon, nor ever was on time for anything except pay-day and bill-collection.
crsnk10{_}427{_}Men pledged me their immortal souls that they would deliver a certain thing on a certain date; as a rule, after such pledging, they rarely exceeded being three months late in delivery.
crsnk10{_}428{_}And so it went, and Charmian and I consoled each other by saying what a splendid boat the Snark was, so staunch and strong; also, we would get into the small boat and row around the Snark, and gloat over her unbelievably wonderful bow.
crsnk10{_}429{_}"Think," I would say to Charmian, "of a gale off the China coast, and of the Snark hove to, that splendid bow of hers driving into the storm.
crsnk10{_}430{_}Not a drop will come over that bow.
crsnk10{_}431{_}She'll be as dry as a feather, and we'll be all below playing whist while the gale howls."
crsnk10{_}432{_}And Charmian would press my hand enthusiastically and exclaim: "It's worth every bit of it--the delay, and expense, and worry, and all the rest.
crsnk10{_}433{_}Oh, what a truly wonderful boat!"
crsnk10{_}434{_}Whenever I looked at the bow of the Snark or thought of her water- tight compartments, I was encouraged.
crsnk10{_}435{_}Nobody else, however, was encouraged.
crsnk10{_}436{_}My friends began to make bets against the various sailing dates of the Snark.
crsnk10{_}437{_}Mr. Wiget, who was left behind in charge of our Sonoma ranch was the first to cash his bet.
crsnk10{_}438{_}He collected on New Year's Day, 1907.
crsnk10{_}439{_}After that the bets came fast and furious.
crsnk10{_}440{_}My friends surrounded me like a gang of harpies, making bets against every sailing date I set.
crsnk10{_}441{_}I was rash, and I was stubborn.
crsnk10{_}442{_}I bet, and I bet, and I continued to bet; and I paid them all.
crsnk10{_}443{_}Why, the women-kind of my friends grew so brave that those among them who never bet before began to bet with me.
crsnk10{_}444{_}And I paid them, too.
crsnk10{_}445{_}"Never mind," said Charmian to me; "just think of that bow and of being hove to on the China Seas."
crsnk10{_}446{_}"You see," I said to my friends, when I paid the latest bunch of wagers, "neither trouble nor cash is being spared in making the Snark the most seaworthy craft that ever sailed out through the Golden Gate--that is what causes all the delay."
crsnk10{_}447{_}In the meantime editors and publishers with whom I had contracts pestered me with demands for explanations.
crsnk10{_}448{_}But how could I explain to them, when I was unable to explain to myself, or when there was nobody, not even Roscoe, to explain to me?
crsnk10{_}449{_}The newspapers began to laugh at me, and to publish rhymes anent the Snark's departure with refrains like, "Not yet, but soon."
crsnk10{_}450{_}And Charmian cheered me up by reminding me of the bow, and I went to a banker and borrowed five thousand more.
crsnk10{_}451{_}There was one recompense for the delay, however.
crsnk10{_}452{_}A friend of mine, who happens to be a critic, wrote a roast of me, of all I had done, and of all I ever was going to do; and he planned to have it published after I was out on the ocean.
crsnk10{_}453{_}I was still on shore when it came out, and he has been busy explaining ever since.
crsnk10{_}454{_}And the time continued to go by.
crsnk10{_}455{_}One thing was becoming apparent, namely, that it was impossible to finish the Snark in San Francisco.
crsnk10{_}456{_}She had been so long in the building that she was beginning to break down and wear out.
crsnk10{_}457{_}In fact, she had reached the stage where she was breaking down faster than she could be repaired.
crsnk10{_}458{_}She had become a joke.
crsnk10{_}459{_}Nobody took her seriously; least of all the men who worked on her.
crsnk10{_}460{_}I said we would sail just as she was and finish building her in Honolulu.
crsnk10{_}461{_}Promptly she sprang a leak that had to be attended to before we could sail.
crsnk10{_}462{_}I started her for the boat-ways.
crsnk10{_}463{_}Before she got to them she was caught between two huge barges and received a vigorous crushing.
crsnk10{_}464{_}We got her on the ways, and, part way along, the ways spread and dropped her through, stern-first, into the mud.
crsnk10{_}465{_}It was a pretty tangle, a job for wreckers, not boat-builders.
crsnk10{_}466{_}There are two high tides every twenty-four hours, and at every high tide, night and day, for a week, there were two steam tugs pulling and hauling on the Snark.
crsnk10{_}467{_}There she was, stuck, fallen between the ways and standing on her stern.
crsnk10{_}468{_}Next, and while still in that predicament, we started to use the gears and castings made in the local foundry whereby power was conveyed from the engine to the windlass.
crsnk10{_}469{_}It was the first time we ever tried to use that windlass.
crsnk10{_}470{_}The castings had flaws; they shattered asunder, the gears ground together, and the windlass was out of commission.
crsnk10{_}471{_}Following upon that, the seventy-horse-power engine went out of commission.
crsnk10{_}472{_}This engine came from New York; so did its bed-plate; there was a flaw in the bed-plate; there were a lot of flaws in the bed-plate; and the seventy-horse-power engine broke away from its shattered foundations, reared up in the air, smashed all connections and fastenings, and fell over on its side.
crsnk10{_}473{_}And the Snark continued to stick between the spread ways, and the two tugs continued to haul vainly upon her.
crsnk10{_}474{_}"Never mind," said Charmian, "think of what a staunch, strong boat she is."
crsnk10{_}475{_}"Yes," said I, "and of that beautiful bow."
crsnk10{_}476{_}So we took heart and went at it again.
crsnk10{_}477{_}The ruined engine was lashed down on its rotten foundation; the smashed castings and cogs of the power transmission were taken down and stored away--all for the purpose of taking them to Honolulu where repairs and new castings could be made.
crsnk10{_}478{_}Somewhere in the dim past the Snark had received on the outside one coat of white paint.
crsnk10{_}479{_}The intention of the colour was still evident, however, when one got it in the right light.
crsnk10{_}480{_}The Snark had never received any paint on the inside.
crsnk10{_}481{_}On the contrary, she was coated inches thick with the grease and tobacco-juice of the multitudinous mechanics who had toiled upon her.
crsnk10{_}482{_}Never mind, we said; the grease and filth could be planed off, and later, when we fetched Honolulu, the Snark could be painted at the same time as she was being rebuilt.
crsnk10{_}483{_}By main strength and sweat we dragged the Snark off from the wrecked ways and laid her alongside the Oakland City Wharf.
crsnk10{_}484{_}The drays brought all the outfit from home, the books and blankets and personal luggage.
crsnk10{_}485{_}Along with this, everything else came on board in a torrent of confusion--wood and coal, water and water-tanks, vegetables, provisions, oil, the life-boat and the launch, all our friends, all the friends of our friends and those who claimed to be their friends, to say nothing of some of the friends of the friends of the friends of our crew.
crsnk10{_}486{_}Also there were reporters, and photographers, and strangers, and cranks, and finally, and over all, clouds of coal-dust from the wharf.
crsnk10{_}487{_}We were to sail Sunday at eleven, and Saturday afternoon had arrived.
crsnk10{_}488{_}The crowd on the wharf and the coal-dust were thicker than ever.
crsnk10{_}489{_}In one pocket I carried a cheque-book, a fountain-pen, a dater, and a blotter; in another pocket I carried between one and two thousand dollars in paper money and gold.
crsnk10{_}490{_}I was ready for the creditors, cash for the small ones and cheques for the large ones, and was waiting only for Roscoe to arrive with the balances of the accounts of the hundred and fifteen firms who had delayed me so many months.
crsnk10{_}491{_}And then -  And then the inconceivable and monstrous happened once more.
crsnk10{_}492{_}Before Roscoe could arrive there arrived another man.
crsnk10{_}493{_}He was a United States marshal.
crsnk10{_}494{_}He tacked a notice on the Snark's brave mast so that all on the wharf could read that the Snark had been libelled for debt.
crsnk10{_}495{_}The marshal left a little old man in charge of the Snark, and himself went away.
crsnk10{_}496{_}I had no longer any control of the Snark, nor of her wonderful bow.
crsnk10{_}497{_}The little old man was now her lord and master, and I learned that I was paying him three dollars a day for being lord and master.
crsnk10{_}498{_}Also, I learned the name of the man who had libelled the Snark.
crsnk10{_}499{_}It was Sellers; the debt was two hundred and thirty-two dollars; and the deed was no more than was to be expected from the possessor of such a name.
crsnk10{_}500{_}Sellers!
crsnk10{_}501{_}Ye gods!
crsnk10{_}502{_}Sellers!
crsnk10{_}503{_}But who under the sun was Sellers?
crsnk10{_}504{_}I looked in my cheque-book and saw that two weeks before I had made him out a cheque for five hundred dollars.
crsnk10{_}505{_}Other cheque-books showed me that during the many months of the building of the Snark I had paid him several thousand dollars.
crsnk10{_}506{_}Then why in the name of common decency hadn't he tried to collect his miserable little balance instead of libelling the Snark?
crsnk10{_}507{_}I thrust my hands into my pockets, and in one pocket encountered the cheque-hook and the dater and the pen, and in the other pocket the gold money and the paper money.
crsnk10{_}508{_}There was the wherewithal to settle his pitiful account a few score of times and over--why hadn't he given me a chance?
crsnk10{_}509{_}There was no explanation; it was merely the inconceivable and monstrous.
crsnk10{_}510{_}To make the matter worse, the Snark had been libelled late Saturday afternoon; and though I sent lawyers and agents all over Oakland and San Francisco, neither United States judge, nor United States marshal, nor Mr.
crsnk10{_}511{_}Sellers, nor Mr.
crsnk10{_}512{_}Sellers' attorney, nor anybody could be found.
crsnk10{_}513{_}They were all out of town for the weekend.
crsnk10{_}514{_}And so the Snark did not sail Sunday morning at eleven.
crsnk10{_}515{_}The little old man was still in charge, and he said no.
crsnk10{_}516{_}And Charmian and I walked out on an opposite wharf and took consolation in the Snark's wonderful bow and thought of all the gales and typhoons it would proudly punch.
crsnk10{_}517{_}"A bourgeois trick," I said to Charmian, speaking of Mr.
crsnk10{_}518{_}Sellers and his libel; "a petty trader's panic.
crsnk10{_}519{_}But never mind; our troubles will cease when once we are away from this and out on the wide ocean."
crsnk10{_}520{_}And in the end we sailed away, on Tuesday morning, April 23, 1907.
crsnk10{_}521{_}We started rather lame, I confess.
crsnk10{_}522{_}We had to hoist anchor by hand, because the power transmission was a wreck.
crsnk10{_}523{_}Also, what remained of our seventy-horse-power engine was lashed down for ballast on the bottom of the Snark.
crsnk10{_}524{_}But what of such things?
crsnk10{_}525{_}They could be fixed in Honolulu, and in the meantime think of the magnificent rest of the boat!
crsnk10{_}526{_}It is true, the engine in the launch wouldn't run, and the life-boat leaked like a sieve; but then they weren't the Snark; they were mere appurtenances.
crsnk10{_}527{_}The things that counted were the water-tight bulkheads, the solid planking without butts, the bath- room devices--they were the Snark.
crsnk10{_}528{_}And then there was, greatest of all, that noble, wind-punching bow.
crsnk10{_}529{_}We sailed out through the Golden Gate and set our course south toward that part of the Pacific where we could hope to pick up with the north-east trades.
crsnk10{_}530{_}And right away things began to happen.
crsnk10{_}531{_}I had calculated that youth was the stuff for a voyage like that of the Snark, and I had taken three youths--the engineer, the cook, and the cabin-boy.
crsnk10{_}532{_}My calculation was only two-thirds OFF; I had forgotten to calculate on seasick youth, and I had two of them, the cook and the cabin boy.
crsnk10{_}533{_}They immediately took to their bunks, and that was the end of their usefulness for a week to come.
crsnk10{_}534{_}It will be understood, from the foregoing, that we did not have the hot meals we might have had, nor were things kept clean and orderly down below.
crsnk10{_}535{_}But it did not matter very much anyway, for we quickly discovered that our box of oranges had at some time been frozen; that our box of apples was mushy and spoiling; that the crate of cabbages, spoiled before it was ever delivered to us, had to go overboard instanter; that kerosene had been spilled on the carrots, and that the turnips were woody and the beets rotten, while the kindling was dead wood that wouldn't burn, and the coal, delivered in rotten potato-sacks, had spilled all over the deck and was washing through the scuppers.
crsnk10{_}536{_}But what did it matter?
crsnk10{_}537{_}Such things were mere accessories.
crsnk10{_}538{_}There was the boat--she was all right, wasn't she?
crsnk10{_}539{_}I strolled along the deck and in one minute counted fourteen butts in the beautiful planking ordered specially from Puget Sound in order that there should be no butts in it.
crsnk10{_}540{_}Also, that deck leaked, and it leaked badly.
crsnk10{_}541{_}It drowned Roscoe out of his bunk and ruined the tools in the engine-room, to say nothing of the provisions it ruined in the galley.
crsnk10{_}542{_}Also, the sides of the Snark leaked, and the bottom leaked, and we had to pump her every day to keep her afloat.
crsnk10{_}543{_}The floor of the galley is a couple of feet above the inside bottom of the Snark; and yet I have stood on the floor of the galley, trying to snatch a cold bite, and been wet to the knees by the water churning around inside four hours after the last pumping.
crsnk10{_}544{_}Then those magnificent water-tight compartments that cost so much time and money--well, they weren't water-tight after all.
crsnk10{_}545{_}The water moved free as the air from one compartment to another; furthermore, a strong smell of gasolene from the after compartment leads me to suspect that some one or more of the half-dozen tanks there stored have sprung a leak.
crsnk10{_}546{_}The tanks leak, and they are not hermetically sealed in their compartment.
crsnk10{_}547{_}Then there was the bath-room with its pumps and levers and sea-valves--it went out of commission inside the first twenty hours.
crsnk10{_}548{_}Powerful iron levers broke off short in one's hand when one tried to pump with them.
crsnk10{_}549{_}The bathroom was the swiftest wreck of any portion of the Snark.
crsnk10{_}550{_}And the iron-work on the Snark, no matter what its source, proved to be mush.
crsnk10{_}551{_}For instance, the bed-plate of the engine came from New York, and it was mush; so were the casting and gears for the windlass that came from San Francisco.
crsnk10{_}552{_}And finally, there was the wrought iron used in the rigging, that carried away in all directions when the first strains were put upon it.
crsnk10{_}553{_}Wrought iron, mind you, and it snapped like macaroni.
crsnk10{_}554{_}A gooseneck on the gaff of the mainsail broke short off.
crsnk10{_}555{_}We replaced it with the gooseneck from the gaff of the storm trysail, and the second gooseneck broke short off inside fifteen minutes of use, and, mind you, it had been taken from the gaff of the storm trysail, upon which we would have depended in time of storm.
crsnk10{_}556{_}At the present moment the Snark trails her mainsail like a broken wing, the gooseneck being replaced by a rough lashing.
crsnk10{_}557{_}We'll see if we can get honest iron in Honolulu.
crsnk10{_}558{_}Man had betrayed us and sent us to sea in a sieve, but the Lord must have loved us, for we had calm weather in which to learn that we must pump every day in order to keep afloat, and that more trust could be placed in a wooden toothpick than in the most massive piece of iron to be found aboard.
crsnk10{_}559{_}As the staunchness and the strength of the Snark went glimmering, Charmian and I pinned our faith more and more to the Snark's wonderful bow.
crsnk10{_}560{_}There was nothing else left to pin to.
crsnk10{_}561{_}It was all inconceivable and monstrous, we knew, but that bow, at least, was rational.
crsnk10{_}562{_}And then, one evening, we started to heave to.
crsnk10{_}563{_}How shall I describe it?
crsnk10{_}564{_}First of all, for the benefit of the tyro, let me explain that heaving to is that sea manoeuvre which, by means of short and balanced canvas, compels a vessel to ride bow-on to wind and sea.
crsnk10{_}565{_}When the wind is too strong, or the sea is too high, a vessel of the size of the Snark can heave to with ease, whereupon there is no more work to do on deck.
crsnk10{_}566{_}Nobody needs to steer.
crsnk10{_}567{_}The lookout is superfluous.
crsnk10{_}568{_}All hands can go below and sleep or play whist.
crsnk10{_}569{_}Well, it was blowing half of a small summer gale, when I told Roscoe we'd heave to.
crsnk10{_}570{_}Night was coming on.
crsnk10{_}571{_}I had been steering nearly all day, and all hands on deck (Roscoe and Bert and Charmian) were tired, while all hands below were seasick.
crsnk10{_}572{_}It happened that we had already put two reefs in the big mainsail.
crsnk10{_}573{_}The flying-jib and the jib were taken in, and a reef put in the fore-staysail.
crsnk10{_}574{_}The mizzen was also taken in.
crsnk10{_}575{_}About this time the flying jib-boom buried itself in a sea and broke short off.
crsnk10{_}576{_}I started to put the wheel down in order to heave to.
crsnk10{_}577{_}The Snark at the moment was rolling in the trough.
crsnk10{_}578{_}She continued rolling in the trough.
crsnk10{_}579{_}I put the spokes down harder and harder.
crsnk10{_}580{_}She never budged from the trough.
crsnk10{_}581{_}(The trough, gentle reader, is the most dangerous position all in which to lay a vessel.)
crsnk10{_}582{_}I put the wheel hard down, and still the Snark rolled in the trough.
crsnk10{_}583{_}Eight points was the nearest I could get her to the wind.
crsnk10{_}584{_}I had Roscoe and Bert come in on the main-sheet.
crsnk10{_}585{_}The Snark rolled on in the trough, now putting her rail under on one side and now under on the other side.
crsnk10{_}586{_}Again the inconceivable and monstrous was showing its grizzly head.
crsnk10{_}587{_}It was grotesque, impossible.
crsnk10{_}588{_}I refused to believe it.
crsnk10{_}589{_}Under double-reefed mainsail and single-reefed staysail the Snark refused to heave to.
crsnk10{_}590{_}We flattened the mainsail down.
crsnk10{_}591{_}It did not alter the Snark's course a tenth of a degree.
crsnk10{_}592{_}We slacked the mainsail off with no more result.
crsnk10{_}593{_}We set a storm trysail on the mizzen, and took in the mainsail.
crsnk10{_}594{_}No change.
crsnk10{_}595{_}The Snark roiled on in the trough.
crsnk10{_}596{_}That beautiful bow of hers refused to come up and face the wind.
crsnk10{_}597{_}Next we took in the reefed staysail.
crsnk10{_}598{_}Thus, the only bit of canvas left on her was the storm trysail on the mizzen.
crsnk10{_}599{_}If anything would bring her bow up to the wind, that would.
crsnk10{_}600{_}Maybe you won't believe me when I say it failed, but I do say it failed.
crsnk10{_}601{_}And I say it failed because I saw it fail, and not because I believe it failed.
crsnk10{_}602{_}I don't believe it did fail.
crsnk10{_}603{_}It is unbelievable, and I am not telling you what I believe; I am telling you what I saw.
crsnk10{_}604{_}Now, gentle reader, what would you do if you were on a small boat, rolling in the trough of the sea, a trysail on that small boat's stern that was unable to swing the bow up into the wind?
crsnk10{_}605{_}Get out the sea-anchor.
crsnk10{_}606{_}It's just what we did.
crsnk10{_}607{_}We had a patent one, made to order and warranted not to dive.
crsnk10{_}608{_}Imagine a hoop of steel that serves to keep open the mouth of a large, conical, canvas bag, and you have a sea-anchor.
crsnk10{_}609{_}Well, we made a line fast to the sea-anchor and to the bow of the Snark, and then dropped the sea-anchor overboard.
crsnk10{_}610{_}It promptly dived.
crsnk10{_}611{_}We had a tripping line on it, so we tripped the sea-anchor and hauled it in.
crsnk10{_}612{_}We attached a big timber as a float, and dropped the sea-anchor over again.
crsnk10{_}613{_}This time it floated.
crsnk10{_}614{_}The line to the bow grew taut.
crsnk10{_}615{_}The trysail on the mizzen tended to swing the bow into the wind, but, in spite of this tendency, the Snark calmly took that sea-anchor in her teeth, and went on ahead, dragging it after her, still in the trough of the sea.
crsnk10{_}616{_}And there you are.
crsnk10{_}617{_}We even took in the trysail, hoisted the full mizzen in its place, and hauled the full mizzen down flat, and the Snark wallowed in the trough and dragged the sea-anchor behind her.
crsnk10{_}618{_}Don't believe me.
crsnk10{_}619{_}I don't believe it myself.
crsnk10{_}620{_}I am merely telling you what I saw.
crsnk10{_}621{_}Now I leave it to you.
crsnk10{_}622{_}Who ever heard of a sailing-boat that wouldn't heave to?--that wouldn't heave to with a sea-anchor to help it?
crsnk10{_}623{_}Out of my brief experience with boats I know I never did.
crsnk10{_}624{_}And I stood on deck and looked on the naked face of the inconceivable and monstrous--the Snark that wouldn't heave to.
crsnk10{_}625{_}A stormy night with broken moonlight had come on.
crsnk10{_}626{_}There was a splash of wet in the air, and up to windward there was a promise of rain-squalls; and then there was the trough of the sea, cold and cruel in the moonlight, in which the Snark complacently rolled.
crsnk10{_}627{_}And then we took in the sea-anchor and the mizzen, hoisted the reefed staysail, ran the Snark off before it, and went below--not to the hot meal that should have awaited us, but to skate across the slush and slime on the cabin floor, where cook and cabin-boy lay like dead men in their bunks, and to lie down in our own bunks, with our clothes on ready for a call, and to listen to the bilge-water spouting knee-high on the galley floor.
crsnk10{_}628{_}In the Bohemian Club of San Francisco there are some crack sailors.
crsnk10{_}629{_}I know, because I heard them pass judgment on the Snark during the process of her building.
crsnk10{_}630{_}They found only one vital thing the matter with her, and on this they were all agreed, namely, that she could not run.
crsnk10{_}631{_}She was all right in every particular, they said, except that I'd never be able to run her before it in a stiff wind and sea.
crsnk10{_}632{_}"Her lines," they explained enigmatically, "it is the fault of her lines.
crsnk10{_}633{_}She simply cannot be made to run, that is all."
crsnk10{_}634{_}Well, I wish I'd only had those crack sailors of the Bohemian Club on board the Snark the other night for them to see for themselves their one, vital, unanimous judgment absolutely reversed.
crsnk10{_}635{_}Run?
crsnk10{_}636{_}It is the one thing the Snark does to perfection.
crsnk10{_}637{_}Run?
crsnk10{_}638{_}She ran with a sea-anchor fast for'ard and a full mizzen flattened down aft.
crsnk10{_}639{_}Run?
crsnk10{_}640{_}At the present moment, as I write this, we are bowling along before it, at a six-knot clip, in the north-east trades.
crsnk10{_}641{_}Quite a tidy bit of sea is running.
crsnk10{_}642{_}There is nobody at the wheel, the wheel is not even lashed and is set over a half-spoke weather helm.
crsnk10{_}643{_}To be precise, the wind is north-east; the Snark's mizzen is furled, her mainsail is over to starboard, her head-sheets are hauled flat:  and the Snark's course is south-south-west.
crsnk10{_}644{_}And yet there are men who have sailed the seas for forty years and who hold that no boat can run before it without being steered.
crsnk10{_}645{_}They'll call me a liar when they read this; it's what they called Captain Slocum when he said the same of his Spray.
crsnk10{_}646{_}As regards the future of the Snark I'm all at sea.
crsnk10{_}647{_}I don't know.
crsnk10{_}648{_}If I had the money or the credit, I'd build another Snark that WOULD heave to.
crsnk10{_}649{_}But I am at the end of my resources.
crsnk10{_}650{_}I've got to put up with the present Snark or quit--and I can't quit.
crsnk10{_}651{_}So I guess I'll have to try to get along with heaving the Snark to stern first.
crsnk10{_}652{_}I am waiting for the next gale to see how it will work.
crsnk10{_}653{_}I think it can be done.
crsnk10{_}654{_}It all depends on how her stern takes the seas.
crsnk10{_}655{_}And who knows but that some wild morning on the China Sea, some gray- beard skipper will stare, rub his incredulous eyes and stare again, at the spectacle of a weird, small craft very much like the Snark, hove to stern-first and riding out the gale?
crsnk10{_}656{_}P.S.
crsnk10{_}657{_}On my return to California after the voyage, I learned that the Snark was forty-three feet on the water-line instead of forty- five.
crsnk10{_}658{_}This was due to the fact that the builder was not on speaking terms with the tape-line or two-foot rule.
crsnk10{_}659{_}CHAPTER III--ADVENTURE    No, adventure is not dead, and in spite of the steam engine and of Thomas Cook & Son.
crsnk10{_}660{_}When the announcement of the contemplated voyage of the Snark was made, young men of "roving disposition" proved to be legion, and young women as well--to say nothing of the elderly men and women who volunteered for the voyage.
crsnk10{_}661{_}Why, among my personal friends there were at least half a dozen who regretted their recent or imminent marriages; and there was one marriage I know of that almost failed to come off because of the Snark.
crsnk10{_}662{_}Every mail to me was burdened with the letters of applicants who were suffocating in the "man-stifled towns," and it soon dawned upon me that a twentieth century Ulysses required a corps of stenographers to clear his correspondence before setting sail.
crsnk10{_}663{_}No, adventure is certainly not dead--not while one receives letters that begin:  "There is no doubt that when you read this soul-plea from a female stranger in New York City," etc.
crsnk10{_}664{_}; and wherein one learns, a little farther on, that this female stranger weighs only ninety pounds, wants to be cabin-boy, and "yearns to see the countries of the world."
crsnk10{_}665{_}The possession of a "passionate fondness for geography," was the way one applicant expressed the wander-lust that was in him; while another wrote, "I am cursed with an eternal yearning to be always on the move, consequently this letter to you."
crsnk10{_}666{_}But best of all was the fellow who said he wanted to come because his feet itched.
crsnk10{_}667{_}There were a few who wrote anonymously, suggesting names of friends and giving said friends' qualifications; but to me there was a hint of something sinister in such proceedings, and I went no further in the matter.
crsnk10{_}668{_}With two or three exceptions, all the hundreds that volunteered for my crew were very much in earnest.
crsnk10{_}669{_}Many of them sent their photographs.
crsnk10{_}670{_}Ninety per cent.
crsnk10{_}671{_}offered to work in any capacity, and ninety-nine per cent.
crsnk10{_}672{_}offered to work without salary.
crsnk10{_}673{_}"Contemplating your voyage on the Snark," said one, "and notwithstanding its attendant dangers, to accompany you (in any capacity whatever) would be the climax of my ambitions."
crsnk10{_}674{_}Which reminds me of the young fellow who was "seventeen years old and ambicious," and who, at the end of his letter, earnestly requested "but please do not let this git into the papers or magazines."
crsnk10{_}675{_}Quite different was the one who said, "I would be willing to work like hell and not demand pay."
crsnk10{_}676{_}Almost all of them wanted me to telegraph, at their expense, my acceptance of their services; and quite a number offered to put up a bond to guarantee their appearance on sailing date.
crsnk10{_}677{_}Some were rather vague in their own minds concerning the work to be done on the Snark; as, for instance, the one who wrote:  "I am taking the liberty of writing you this note to find out if there would be any possibility of my going with you as one of the crew of your boat to make sketches and illustrations."
crsnk10{_}678{_}Several, unaware of the needful work on a small craft like the Snark, offered to serve, as one of them phrased it, "as assistant in filing materials collected for books and novels."
crsnk10{_}679{_}That's what one gets for being prolific.
crsnk10{_}680{_}"Let me give my qualifications for the job," wrote one.
crsnk10{_}681{_}"I am an orphan living with my uncle, who is a hot revolutionary socialist and who says a man without the red blood of adventure is an animated dish-rag."
crsnk10{_}682{_}Said another:  "I can swim some, though I don't know any of the new strokes.
crsnk10{_}683{_}But what is more important than strokes, the water is a friend of mine."
crsnk10{_}684{_}"If I was put alone in a sail-boat, I could get her anywhere I wanted to go," was the qualification of a third--and a better qualification than the one that follows, "I have also watched the fish-boats unload."
crsnk10{_}685{_}But possibly the prize should go to this one, who very subtly conveys his deep knowledge of the world and life by saying:  "My age, in years, is twenty-two."
crsnk10{_}686{_}Then there were the simple straight-out, homely, and unadorned letters of young boys, lacking in the felicities of expression, it is true, but desiring greatly to make the voyage.
crsnk10{_}687{_}These were the hardest of all to decline, and each time I declined one it seemed as if I had struck Youth a slap in the face.
crsnk10{_}688{_}They were so earnest, these boys, they wanted so much to go.
crsnk10{_}689{_}"I am sixteen but large for my age," said one; and another, "Seventeen but large and healthy."
crsnk10{_}690{_}"I am as strong at least as the average boy of my size," said an evident weakling.
crsnk10{_}691{_}"Not afraid of any kind of work," was what many said, while one in particular, to lure me no doubt by inexpensiveness, wrote:  "I can pay my way to the Pacific coast, so that part would probably be acceptable to you."
crsnk10{_}692{_}"Going around the world is THE ONE THING I want to do," said one, and it seemed to be the one thing that a few hundred wanted to do.
crsnk10{_}693{_}"I have no one who cares whether I go or not," was the pathetic note sounded by another.
crsnk10{_}694{_}One had sent his photograph, and speaking of it, said, "I'm a homely-looking sort of a chap, but looks don't always count."
crsnk10{_}695{_}And I am confident that the lad who wrote the following would have turned out all right:  "My age is 19 years, but I am rather small and consequently won't take up much room, but I'm tough as the devil."
crsnk10{_}696{_}And there was one thirteen-year-old applicant that Charmian and I fell in love with, and it nearly broke our hearts to refuse him.
crsnk10{_}697{_}But it must not be imagined that most of my volunteers were boys; on the contrary, boys constituted a very small proportion.
crsnk10{_}698{_}There were men and women from every walk in life.
crsnk10{_}699{_}Physicians, surgeons, and dentists offered in large numbers to come along, and, like all the professional men, offered to come without pay, to serve in any capacity, and to pay, even, for the privilege of so serving.
crsnk10{_}700{_}There was no end of compositors and reporters who wanted to come, to say nothing of experienced valets, chefs, and stewards.
crsnk10{_}701{_}Civil engineers were keen on the voyage; "lady" companions galore cropped up for Charmian; while I was deluged with the applications of would- be private secretaries.
crsnk10{_}702{_}Many high school and university students yearned for the voyage, and every trade in the working class developed a few applicants, the machinists, electricians, and engineers being especially strong on the trip.
crsnk10{_}703{_}I was surprised at the number, who, in musty law offices, heard the call of adventure; and I was more than surprised by the number of elderly and retired sea captains who were still thralls to the sea.
crsnk10{_}704{_}Several young fellows, with millions coming to them later on, were wild for the adventure, as were also several county superintendents of schools.
crsnk10{_}705{_}Fathers and sons wanted to come, and many men with their wives, to say nothing of the young woman stenographer who wrote:  "Write immediately if you need me.
crsnk10{_}706{_}I shall bring my typewriter on the first train."
crsnk10{_}707{_}But the best of all is the following--observe the delicate way in which he worked in his wife:  "I thought I would drop you a line of inquiry as to the possibility of making the trip with you, am 24 years of age, married and broke, and a trip of that kind would be just what we are looking for."
crsnk10{_}708{_}Come to think of it, for the average man it must be fairly difficult to write an honest letter of self-recommendation.
crsnk10{_}709{_}One of my correspondents was so stumped that he began his letter with the words, "This is a hard task"; and, after vainly trying to describe his good points, he wound up with, "It is a hard job writing about one's self."
crsnk10{_}710{_}Nevertheless, there was one who gave himself a most glowing and lengthy character, and in conclusion stated that he had greatly enjoyed writing it.
crsnk10{_}711{_}"But suppose this:  your cabin-boy could run your engine, could repair it when out of order.
crsnk10{_}712{_}Suppose he could take his turn at the wheel, could do any carpenter or machinist work.
crsnk10{_}713{_}Suppose he is strong, healthy, and willing to work.
crsnk10{_}714{_}Would you not rather have him than a kid that gets seasick and can't do anything but wash dishes?"
crsnk10{_}715{_}It was letters of this sort that I hated to decline.
crsnk10{_}716{_}The writer of it, self-taught in English, had been only two years in the United States, and, as he said, "I am not wishing to go with you to earn my living, but I wish to learn and see."
crsnk10{_}717{_}At the time of writing to me he was a designer for one of the big motor manufacturing companies; he had been to sea quite a bit, and had been used all his life to the handling of small boats.
crsnk10{_}718{_}"I have a good position, but it matters not so with me as I prefer travelling," wrote another.
crsnk10{_}719{_}"As to salary, look at me, and if I am worth a dollar or two, all right, and if I am not, nothing said.
crsnk10{_}720{_}As to my honesty and character, I shall be pleased to show you my employers.
crsnk10{_}721{_}Never drink, no tobacco, but to be honest, I myself, after a little more experience, want to do a little writing."
crsnk10{_}722{_}"I can assure you that I am eminently respectable, but find other respectable people tiresome."
crsnk10{_}723{_}The man who wrote the foregoing certainly had me guessing, and I am still wondering whether or not he'd have found me tiresome, or what the deuce he did mean.
crsnk10{_}724{_}"I have seen better days than what I am passing through to-day," wrote an old salt, "but I have seen them a great deal worse also."
crsnk10{_}725{_}But the willingness to sacrifice on the part of the man who wrote the following was so touching that I could not accept:  "I have a father, a mother, brothers and sisters, dear friends and a lucrative position, and yet I will sacrifice all to become one of your crew."
crsnk10{_}726{_}Another volunteer I could never have accepted was the finicky young fellow who, to show me how necessary it was that I should give him a chance, pointed out that "to go in the ordinary boat, be it schooner or steamer, would be impracticable, for I would have to mix among and live with the ordinary type of seamen, which as a rule is not a clean sort of life."
crsnk10{_}727{_}Then there was the young fellow of twenty-six, who had "run through the gamut of human emotions," and had "done everything from cooking to attending Stanford University," and who, at the present writing, was "A vaquero on a fifty-five-thousand-acre range."
crsnk10{_}728{_}Quite in contrast was the modesty of the one who said, "I am not aware of possessing any particular qualities that would be likely to recommend me to your consideration.
crsnk10{_}729{_}But should you be impressed, you might consider it worth a few minutes' time to answer.
crsnk10{_}730{_}Otherwise, there's always work at the trade.
crsnk10{_}731{_}Not expecting, but hoping, I remain, etc."
crsnk10{_}732{_}But I have held my head in both my hands ever since, trying to figure out the intellectual kinship between myself and the one who wrote:  "Long before I knew of you, I had mixed political economy and history and deducted therefrom many of your conclusions in concrete."
crsnk10{_}733{_}Here, in its way, is one of the best, as it is the briefest, that I received:  "If any of the present company signed on for cruise happens to get cold feet and you need one more who understands boating, engines, etc., would like to hear from you, etc."
crsnk10{_}734{_}Here is another brief one:  "Point blank, would like to have the job of cabin-boy on your trip around the world, or any other job on board.
crsnk10{_}735{_}Am nineteen years old, weigh one hundred and forty pounds, and am an American."
crsnk10{_}736{_}And here is a good one from a man a "little over five feet long": "When I read about your manly plan of sailing around the world in a small boat with Mrs. London, I was so much rejoiced that I felt I was planning it myself, and I thought to write you about filling either position of cook or cabin-boy myself, but for some reason I did not do it, and I came to Denver from Oakland to join my friend's business last month, but everything is worse and unfavourable.
crsnk10{_}737{_}But fortunately you have postponed your departure on account of the great earthquake, so I finally decided to propose you to let me fill either of the positions.
crsnk10{_}738{_}I am not very strong, being a man of a little over five feet long, although I am of sound health and capability."
crsnk10{_}739{_}"I think I can add to your outfit an additional method of utilizing the power of the wind," wrote a well-wisher, "which, while not interfering with ordinary sails in light breezes, will enable you to use the whole force of the wind in its mightiest blows, so that even when its force is so great that you may have to take in every inch of canvas used in the ordinary way, you may carry the fullest spread with my method.
crsnk10{_}740{_}With my attachment your craft could not be UPSET."
crsnk10{_}741{_}The foregoing letter was written in San Francisco under the date of April 16, 1906.
crsnk10{_}742{_}And two days later, on April 18, came the Great Earthquake.
crsnk10{_}743{_}And that's why I've got it in for that earthquake, for it made a refugee out of the man who wrote the letter, and prevented us from ever getting together.
crsnk10{_}744{_}Many of my brother socialists objected to my making the cruise, of which the following is typical:  "The Socialist Cause and the millions of oppressed victims of Capitalism has a right and claim upon your life and services.
crsnk10{_}745{_}If, however, you persist, then, when you swallow the last mouthful of salt chuck you can hold before sinking, remember that we at least protested."
crsnk10{_}746{_}One wanderer over the world who "could, if opportunity afforded, recount many unusual scenes and events," spent several pages ardently trying to get to the point of his letter, and at last achieved the following:  "Still I am neglecting the point I set out to write you about.
crsnk10{_}747{_}So will say at once that it has been stated in print that you and one or two others are going to take a cruize around the world a little fifty- or sixty-foot boat.
crsnk10{_}748{_}I therefore cannot get myself to think that a man of your attainments and experience would attempt such a proceeding, which is nothing less than courting death in that way.
crsnk10{_}749{_}And even if you were to escape for some time, your whole Person, and those with you would be bruised from the ceaseless motion of a craft of the above size, even if she were padded, a thing not usual at sea."
crsnk10{_}750{_}Thank you, kind friend, thank you for that qualification, "a thing not usual at sea."
crsnk10{_}751{_}Nor is this friend ignorant of the sea.
crsnk10{_}752{_}As he says of himself, "I am not a land-lubber, and I have sailed every sea and ocean."
crsnk10{_}753{_}And he winds up his letter with:  "Although not wishing to offend, it would be madness to take any woman outside the bay even, in such a craft."
crsnk10{_}754{_}And yet, at the moment of writing this, Charmian is in her state- room at the typewriter, Martin is cooking dinner, Tochigi is setting the table, Roscoe and Bert are caulking the deck, and the Snark is steering herself some five knots an hour in a rattling good sea--and the Snark is not padded, either.
crsnk10{_}755{_}"Seeing a piece in the paper about your intended trip, would like to know if you would like a good crew, as there is six of us boys all good sailor men, with good discharges from the Navy and Merchant Service, all true Americans, all between the ages of 20 and 22, and at present are employed as riggers at the Union Iron Works, and would like very much to sail with you."
crsnk10{_}756{_}--It was letters like this that made me regret the boat was not larger.
crsnk10{_}757{_}And here writes the one woman in all the world--outside of Charmian- -for the cruise:  "If you have not succeeded in getting a cook I would like very much to take the trip in that capacity.
crsnk10{_}758{_}I am a woman of fifty, healthy and capable, and can do the work for the small company that compose the crew of the Snark.
crsnk10{_}759{_}I am a very good cook and a very good sailor and something of a traveller, and the length of the voyage, if of ten years' duration, would suit me better than one.
crsnk10{_}760{_}References, etc."
crsnk10{_}761{_}Some day, when I have made a lot of money, I'm going to build a big ship, with room in it for a thousand volunteers.
crsnk10{_}762{_}They will have to do all the work of navigating that boat around the world, or they'll stay at home.
crsnk10{_}763{_}I believe that they'll work the boat around the world, for I know that Adventure is not dead.
crsnk10{_}764{_}I know Adventure is not dead because I have had a long and intimate correspondence with Adventure.
crsnk10{_}765{_}CHAPTER IV--FINDING ONE'S WAY ABOUT    "But," our friends objected, "how dare you go to sea without a navigator on board?
crsnk10{_}766{_}You're not a navigator, are you?"
crsnk10{_}767{_}I had to confess that I was not a navigator, that I had never looked through a sextant in my life, and that I doubted if I could tell a sextant from a nautical almanac.
crsnk10{_}768{_}And when they asked if Roscoe was a navigator, I shook my head.
crsnk10{_}769{_}Roscoe resented this.
crsnk10{_}770{_}He had glanced at the "Epitome," bought for our voyage, knew how to use logarithm tables, had seen a sextant at some time, and, what of this and of his seafaring ancestry, he concluded that he did know navigation.
crsnk10{_}771{_}But Roscoe was wrong, I still insist.
crsnk10{_}772{_}When a young boy he came from Maine to California by way of the Isthmus of Panama, and that was the only time in his life that he was out of sight of land.
crsnk10{_}773{_}He had never gone to a school of navigation, nor passed an examination in the same; nor had he sailed the deep sea and learned the art from some other navigator.
crsnk10{_}774{_}He was a San Francisco Bay yachtsman, where land is always only several miles away and the art of navigation is never employed.
crsnk10{_}775{_}So the Snark started on her long voyage without a navigator.
crsnk10{_}776{_}We beat through the Golden Gate on April 23, and headed for the Hawaiian Islands, twenty-one hundred sea-miles away as the gull flies.
crsnk10{_}777{_}And the outcome was our justification.
crsnk10{_}778{_}We arrived.
crsnk10{_}779{_}And we arrived, furthermore, without any trouble, as you shall see; that is, without any trouble to amount to anything.
crsnk10{_}780{_}To begin with, Roscoe tackled the navigating.
crsnk10{_}781{_}He had the theory all right, but it was the first time he had ever applied it, as was evidenced by the erratic behaviour of the Snark.
crsnk10{_}782{_}Not but what the Snark was perfectly steady on the sea; the pranks she cut were on the chart.
crsnk10{_}783{_}On a day with a light breeze she would make a jump on the chart that advertised "a wet sail and a flowing sheet," and on a day when she just raced over the ocean, she scarcely changed her position on the chart.
crsnk10{_}784{_}Now when one's boat has logged six knots for twenty-four consecutive hours, it is incontestable that she has covered one hundred and forty-four miles of ocean.
crsnk10{_}785{_}The ocean was all right, and so was the patent log; as for speed, one saw it with his own eyes.
crsnk10{_}786{_}Therefore the thing that was not all right was the figuring that refused to boost the Snark along over the chart.
crsnk10{_}787{_}Not that this happened every day, but that it did happen.
crsnk10{_}788{_}And it was perfectly proper and no more than was to be expected from a first attempt at applying a theory.
crsnk10{_}789{_}The acquisition of the knowledge of navigation has a strange effect on the minds of men.
crsnk10{_}790{_}The average navigator speaks of navigation with deep respect.
crsnk10{_}791{_}To the layman navigation is a deed and awful mystery, which feeling has been generated in him by the deep and awful respect for navigation that the layman has seen displayed by navigators.
crsnk10{_}792{_}I have known frank, ingenuous, and modest young men, open as the day, to learn navigation and at once betray secretiveness, reserve, and self-importance as if they had achieved some tremendous intellectual attainment.
crsnk10{_}793{_}The average navigator impresses the layman as a priest of some holy rite.
crsnk10{_}794{_}With bated breath, the amateur yachtsman navigator invites one in to look at his chronometer.
