crsnk10{_}795{_}And so it was that our friends suffered such apprehension at our sailing without a navigator.
crsnk10{_}796{_}During the building of the Snark, Roscoe and I had an agreement, something like this:  "I'll furnish the books and instruments," I said, "and do you study up navigation now.
crsnk10{_}797{_}I'll be too busy to do any studying.
crsnk10{_}798{_}Then, when we get to sea, you can teach me what you have learned."
crsnk10{_}799{_}Roscoe was delighted.
crsnk10{_}800{_}Furthermore, Roscoe was as frank and ingenuous and modest as the young men I have described.
crsnk10{_}801{_}But when we got out to sea and he began to practise the holy rite, while I looked on admiringly, a change, subtle and distinctive, marked his bearing.
crsnk10{_}802{_}When he shot the sun at noon, the glow of achievement wrapped him in lambent flame.
crsnk10{_}803{_}When he went below, figured out his observation, and then returned on deck and announced our latitude and longitude, there was an authoritative ring in his voice that was new to all of us.
crsnk10{_}804{_}But that was not the worst of it.
crsnk10{_}805{_}He became filled with incommunicable information.
crsnk10{_}806{_}And the more he discovered the reasons for the erratic jumps of the Snark over the chart, and the less the Snark jumped, the more incommunicable and holy and awful became his information.
crsnk10{_}807{_}My mild suggestions that it was about time that I began to learn, met with no hearty response, with no offers on his part to help me.
crsnk10{_}808{_}He displayed not the slightest intention of living up to our agreement.
crsnk10{_}809{_}Now this was not Roscoe's fault; he could not help it.
crsnk10{_}810{_}He had merely gone the way of all the men who learned navigation before him.
crsnk10{_}811{_}By an understandable and forgivable confusion of values, plus a loss of orientation, he felt weighted by responsibility, and experienced the possession of power that was like unto that of a god.
crsnk10{_}812{_}All his life Roscoe had lived on land, and therefore in sight of land.
crsnk10{_}813{_}Being constantly in sight of land, with landmarks to guide him, he had managed, with occasional difficulties, to steer his body around and about the earth.
crsnk10{_}814{_}Now he found himself on the sea, wide- stretching, bounded only by the eternal circle of the sky.
crsnk10{_}815{_}This circle looked always the same.
crsnk10{_}816{_}There were no landmarks.
crsnk10{_}817{_}The sun rose to the east and set to the west and the stars wheeled through the night.
crsnk10{_}818{_}But who may look at the sun or the stars and say, "My place on the face of the earth at the present moment is four and three-quarter miles to the west of Jones's Cash Store of Smithersville"?
crsnk10{_}819{_}or "I know where I am now, for the Little Dipper informs me that Boston is three miles away on the second turning to the right"?
crsnk10{_}820{_}And yet that was precisely what Roscoe did.
crsnk10{_}821{_}That he was astounded by the achievement, is putting it mildly.
crsnk10{_}822{_}He stood in reverential awe of himself; he had performed a miraculous feat.
crsnk10{_}823{_}The act of finding himself on the face of the waters became a rite, and he felt himself a superior being to the rest of us who knew not this rite and were dependent on him for being shepherded across the heaving and limitless waste, the briny highroad that connects the continents and whereon there are no mile-stones.
crsnk10{_}824{_}So, with the sextant he made obeisance to the sun-god, he consulted ancient tomes and tables of magic characters, muttered prayers in a strange tongue that sounded like INDEXERRORPARALLAXREFRACTION, made cabalistic signs on paper, added and carried one, and then, on a piece of holy script called the Grail--I mean the Chart--he placed his finger on a certain space conspicuous for its blankness and said, "Here we are."
crsnk10{_}825{_}When we looked at the blank space and asked, "And where is that?"
crsnk10{_}826{_}he answered in the cipher-code of the higher priesthood, "31-15-47 north, 133-5-30 west."
crsnk10{_}827{_}And we said "Oh," and felt mighty small.
crsnk10{_}828{_}So I aver, it was not Roscoe's fault.
crsnk10{_}829{_}He was like unto a god, and he carried us in the hollow of his hand across the blank spaces on the chart.
crsnk10{_}830{_}I experienced a great respect for Roscoe; this respect grew so profound that had he commanded, "Kneel down and worship me," I know that I should have flopped down on the deck and yammered.
crsnk10{_}831{_}But, one day, there came a still small thought to me that said: "This is not a god; this is Roscoe, a mere man like myself.
crsnk10{_}832{_}What he has done, I can do.
crsnk10{_}833{_}Who taught him?
crsnk10{_}834{_}Himself.
crsnk10{_}835{_}Go you and do likewise--be your own teacher."
crsnk10{_}836{_}And right there Roscoe crashed, and he was high priest of the Snark no longer.
crsnk10{_}837{_}I invaded the sanctuary and demanded the ancient tomes and magic tables, also the prayer- wheel--the sextant, I mean.
crsnk10{_}838{_}And now, in simple language.
crsnk10{_}839{_}I shall describe how I taught myself navigation.
crsnk10{_}840{_}One whole afternoon I sat in the cockpit, steering with one hand and studying logarithms with the other.
crsnk10{_}841{_}Two afternoons, two hours each, I studied the general theory of navigation and the particular process of taking a meridian altitude.
crsnk10{_}842{_}Then I took the sextant, worked out the index error, and shot the sun.
crsnk10{_}843{_}The figuring from the data of this observation was child's play.
crsnk10{_}844{_}In the "Epitome" and the "Nautical Almanac" were scores of cunning tables, all worked out by mathematicians and astronomers.
crsnk10{_}845{_}It was like using interest tables and lightning-calculator tables such as you all know.
crsnk10{_}846{_}The mystery was mystery no longer.
crsnk10{_}847{_}I put my finger on the chart and announced that that was where we were.
crsnk10{_}848{_}I was right too, or at least I was as right as Roscoe, who selected a spot a quarter of a mile away from mine.
crsnk10{_}849{_}Even he was willing to split the distance with me.
crsnk10{_}850{_}I had exploded the mystery, and yet, such was the miracle of it, I was conscious of new power in me, and I felt the thrill and tickle of pride.
crsnk10{_}851{_}And when Martin asked me, in the same humble and respectful way I had previously asked Roscoe, as to where we were, it was with exaltation and spiritual chest-throwing that I answered in the cipher-code of the higher priesthood and heard Martin's self- abasing and worshipful "Oh."
crsnk10{_}852{_}As for Charmian, I felt that in a new way I had proved my right to her; and I was aware of another feeling, namely, that she was a most fortunate woman to have a man like me.
crsnk10{_}853{_}I couldn't help it.
crsnk10{_}854{_}I tell it as a vindication of Roscoe and all the other navigators.
crsnk10{_}855{_}The poison of power was working in me.
crsnk10{_}856{_}I was not as other men--most other men; I knew what they did not know,-- the mystery of the heavens, that pointed out the way across the deep.
crsnk10{_}857{_}And the taste of power I had received drove me on.
crsnk10{_}858{_}I steered at the wheel long hours with one hand, and studied mystery with the other.
crsnk10{_}859{_}By the end of the week, teaching myself, I was able to do divers things.
crsnk10{_}860{_}For instance, I shot the North Star, at night, of course; got its altitude, corrected for index error, dip, etc., and found our latitude.
crsnk10{_}861{_}And this latitude agreed with the latitude of the previous noon corrected by dead reckoning up to that moment.
crsnk10{_}862{_}Proud?
crsnk10{_}863{_}Well, I was even prouder with my next miracle.
crsnk10{_}864{_}I was going to turn in at nine o'clock.
crsnk10{_}865{_}I worked out the problem, self- instructed, and learned what star of the first magnitude would be passing the meridian around half-past eight.
crsnk10{_}866{_}This star proved to be Alpha Crucis.
crsnk10{_}867{_}I had never heard of the star before.
crsnk10{_}868{_}I looked it up on the star map.
crsnk10{_}869{_}It was one of the stars of the Southern Cross.
crsnk10{_}870{_}What!
crsnk10{_}871{_}thought I; have we been sailing with the Southern Cross in the sky of nights and never known it?
crsnk10{_}872{_}Dolts that we are!
crsnk10{_}873{_}Gudgeons and moles!
crsnk10{_}874{_}I couldn't believe it.
crsnk10{_}875{_}I went over the problem again, and verified it.
crsnk10{_}876{_}Charmian had the wheel from eight till ten that evening.
crsnk10{_}877{_}I told her to keep her eyes open and look due south for the Southern Cross.
crsnk10{_}878{_}And when the stars came out, there shone the Southern Cross low on the horizon.
crsnk10{_}879{_}Proud?
crsnk10{_}880{_}No medicine man nor high priest was ever prouder.
crsnk10{_}881{_}Furthermore, with the prayer-wheel I shot Alpha Crucis and from its altitude worked out our latitude.
crsnk10{_}882{_}And still furthermore, I shot the North Star, too, and it agreed with what had been told me by the Southern Cross.
crsnk10{_}883{_}Proud?
crsnk10{_}884{_}Why, the language of the stars was mine, and I listened and heard them telling me my way over the deep.
crsnk10{_}885{_}Proud?
crsnk10{_}886{_}I was a worker of miracles.
crsnk10{_}887{_}I forgot how easily I had taught myself from the printed page.
crsnk10{_}888{_}I forgot that all the work (and a tremendous work, too) had been done by the masterminds before me, the astronomers and mathematicians, who had discovered and elaborated the whole science of navigation and made the tables in the "Epitome."
crsnk10{_}889{_}I remembered only the everlasting miracle of it-- that I had listened to the voices of the stars and been told my place upon the highway of the sea.
crsnk10{_}890{_}Charmian did not know, Martin did not know, Tochigi, the cabin-boy, did not know.
crsnk10{_}891{_}But I told them.
crsnk10{_}892{_}I was God's messenger.
crsnk10{_}893{_}I stood between them and infinity.
crsnk10{_}894{_}I translated the high celestial speech into terms of their ordinary understanding.
crsnk10{_}895{_}We were heaven-directed, and it was I who could read the sign-post of the sky!--I!
crsnk10{_}896{_}I!
crsnk10{_}897{_}And now, in a cooler moment, I hasten to blab the whole simplicity of it, to blab on Roscoe and the other navigators and the rest of the priesthood, all for fear that I may become even as they, secretive, immodest, and inflated with self-esteem.
crsnk10{_}898{_}And I want to say this now:  any young fellow with ordinary gray matter, ordinary education, and with the slightest trace of the student-mind, can get the books, and charts, and instruments and teach himself navigation.
crsnk10{_}899{_}Now I must not be misunderstood.
crsnk10{_}900{_}Seamanship is an entirely different matter.
crsnk10{_}901{_}It is not learned in a day, nor in many days; it requires years.
crsnk10{_}902{_}Also, navigating by dead reckoning requires long study and practice.
crsnk10{_}903{_}But navigating by observations of the sun, moon, and stars, thanks to the astronomers and mathematicians, is child's play.
crsnk10{_}904{_}Any average young fellow can teach himself in a week.
crsnk10{_}905{_}And yet again I must not be misunderstood.
crsnk10{_}906{_}I do not mean to say that at the end of a week a young fellow could take charge of a fifteen-thousand-ton steamer, driving twenty knots an hour through the brine, racing from land to land, fair weather and foul, clear sky or cloudy, steering by degrees on the compass card and making landfalls with most amazing precision.
crsnk10{_}907{_}But what I do mean is just this:  the average young fellow I have described can get into a staunch sail-boat and put out across the ocean, without knowing anything about navigation, and at the end of the week he will know enough to know where he is on the chart.
crsnk10{_}908{_}He will be able to take a meridian observation with fair accuracy, and from that observation, with ten minutes of figuring, work out his latitude and longitude.
crsnk10{_}909{_}And, carrying neither freight nor passengers, being under no press to reach his destination, he can jog comfortably along, and if at any time he doubts his own navigation and fears an imminent landfall, he can heave to all night and proceed in the morning.
crsnk10{_}910{_}Joshua Slocum sailed around the world a few years ago in a thirty- seven-foot boat all by himself.
crsnk10{_}911{_}I shall never forget, in his narrative of the voyage, where he heartily indorsed the idea of young men, in similar small boats, making similar voyage.
crsnk10{_}912{_}I promptly indorsed his idea, and so heartily that I took my wife along.
crsnk10{_}913{_}While it certainly makes a Cook's tour look like thirty cents, on top of that, amid on top of the fun and pleasure, it is a splendid education for a young man--oh, not a mere education in the things of the world outside, of lands, and peoples, and climates, but an education in the world inside, an education in one's self, a chance to learn one's own self, to get on speaking terms with one's soul.
crsnk10{_}914{_}Then there is the training and the disciplining of it.
crsnk10{_}915{_}First, naturally, the young fellow will learn his limitations; and next, inevitably, he will proceed to press back those limitations.
crsnk10{_}916{_}And he cannot escape returning from such a voyage a bigger and better man.
crsnk10{_}917{_}And as for sport, it is a king's sport, taking one's self around the world, doing it with one's own hands, depending on no one but one's self, and at the end, back at the starting-point, contemplating with inner vision the planet rushing through space, and saying, "I did it; with my own hands I did it.
crsnk10{_}918{_}I went clear around that whirling sphere, and I can travel alone, without any nurse of a sea-captain to guide my steps across the seas.
crsnk10{_}919{_}I may not fly to other stars, but of this star I myself am master."
crsnk10{_}920{_}As I write these lines I lift my eyes and look seaward.
crsnk10{_}921{_}I am on the beach of Waikiki on the island of Oahu.
crsnk10{_}922{_}Far, in the azure sky, the trade-wind clouds drift low over the blue-green turquoise of the deep sea.
crsnk10{_}923{_}Nearer, the sea is emerald and light olive-green.
crsnk10{_}924{_}Then comes the reef, where the water is all slaty purple flecked with red.
crsnk10{_}925{_}Still nearer are brighter greens and tans, lying in alternate stripes and showing where sandbeds lie between the living coral banks.
crsnk10{_}926{_}Through and over and out of these wonderful colours tumbles and thunders a magnificent surf.
crsnk10{_}927{_}As I say, I lift my eyes to all this, and through the white crest of a breaker suddenly appears a dark figure, erect, a man-fish or a sea-god, on the very forward face of the crest where the top falls over and down, driving in toward shore, buried to his loins in smoking spray, caught up by the sea and flung landward, bodily, a quarter of a mile.
crsnk10{_}928{_}It is a Kanaka on a surf-board.
crsnk10{_}929{_}And I know that when I have finished these lines I shall be out in that riot of colour and pounding surf, trying to bit those breakers even as he, and failing as he never failed, but living life as the best of us may live it.
crsnk10{_}930{_}And the picture of that coloured sea and that flying sea-god Kanaka becomes another reason for the young man to go west, and farther west, beyond the Baths of Sunset, and still west till he arrives home again.
crsnk10{_}931{_}But to return.
crsnk10{_}932{_}Please do not think that I already know it all.
crsnk10{_}933{_}I know only the rudiments of navigation.
crsnk10{_}934{_}There is a vast deal yet for me to learn.
crsnk10{_}935{_}On the Snark there is a score of fascinating books on navigation waiting for me.
crsnk10{_}936{_}There is the danger-angle of Lecky, there is the line of Sumner, which, when you know least of all where you are, shows most conclusively where you are, and where you are not.
crsnk10{_}937{_}There are dozens and dozens of methods of finding one's location on the deep, and one can work years before he masters it all in all its fineness.
crsnk10{_}938{_}Even in the little we did learn there were slips that accounted for the apparently antic behaviour of the Snark.
crsnk10{_}939{_}On Thursday, May 16, for instance, the trade wind failed us.
crsnk10{_}940{_}During the twenty-four hours that ended Friday at noon, by dead reckoning we had not sailed twenty miles.
crsnk10{_}941{_}Yet here are our positions, at noon, for the two days, worked out from our observations:  Thursday  20 degrees 57 minutes  9 seconds N          152 degrees 40 minutes 30 seconds W Friday    21 degrees 15 minutes 33 seconds N          154 degrees 12 minutes            W  The difference between the two positions was something like eighty miles.
crsnk10{_}942{_}Yet we knew we had not travelled twenty miles.
crsnk10{_}943{_}Now our figuring was all right.
crsnk10{_}944{_}We went over it several times.
crsnk10{_}945{_}What was wrong was the observations we had taken.
crsnk10{_}946{_}To take a correct observation requires practice and skill, and especially so on a small craft like the Snark.
crsnk10{_}947{_}The violently moving boat and the closeness of the observer's eye to the surface of the water are to blame.
crsnk10{_}948{_}A big wave that lifts up a mile off is liable to steal the horizon away.
crsnk10{_}949{_}But in our particular case there was another perturbing factor.
crsnk10{_}950{_}The sun, in its annual march north through the heavens, was increasing its declination.
crsnk10{_}951{_}On the 19th parallel of north latitude in the middle of May the sun is nearly overhead.
crsnk10{_}952{_}The angle of arc was between eighty-eight and eighty-nine degrees.
crsnk10{_}953{_}Had it been ninety degrees it would have been straight overhead.
crsnk10{_}954{_}It was on another day that we learned a few things about taking the altitude of the almost perpendicular sun.
crsnk10{_}955{_}Roscoe started in drawing the sun down to the eastern horizon, and he stayed by that point of the compass despite the fact that the sun would pass the meridian to the south.
crsnk10{_}956{_}I, on the other hand, started in to draw the sun down to south-east and strayed away to the south-west.
crsnk10{_}957{_}You see, we were teaching ourselves.
crsnk10{_}958{_}As a result, at twenty-five minutes past twelve by the ship's time, I called twelve o'clock by the sun.
crsnk10{_}959{_}Now this signified that we had changed our location on the face of the world by twenty- five minutes, which was equal to something like six degrees of longitude, or three hundred and fifty miles.
crsnk10{_}960{_}This showed the Snark had travelled fifteen knots per hour for twenty-four consecutive hours--and we had never noticed it!
crsnk10{_}961{_}It was absurd and grotesque.
crsnk10{_}962{_}But Roscoe, still looking east, averred that it was not yet twelve o'clock.
crsnk10{_}963{_}He was bent on giving us a twenty-knot clip.
crsnk10{_}964{_}Then we began to train our sextants rather wildly all around the horizon, and wherever we looked, there was the sun, puzzlingly close to the sky-line, sometimes above it and sometimes below it.
crsnk10{_}965{_}In one direction the sun was proclaiming morning, in another direction it was proclaiming afternoon.
crsnk10{_}966{_}The sun was all right--we knew that; therefore we were all wrong.
crsnk10{_}967{_}And the rest of the afternoon we spent in the cockpit reading up the matter in the books and finding out what was wrong.
crsnk10{_}968{_}We missed the observation that day, but we didn't the next.
crsnk10{_}969{_}We had learned.
crsnk10{_}970{_}And we learned well, better than for a while we thought we had.
crsnk10{_}971{_}At the beginning of the second dog-watch one evening, Charmian and I sat down on the forecastle-head for a rubber of cribbage.
crsnk10{_}972{_}Chancing to glance ahead, I saw cloud-capped mountains rising from the sea.
crsnk10{_}973{_}We were rejoiced at the sight of land, but I was in despair over our navigation.
crsnk10{_}974{_}I thought we had learned something, yet our position at noon, plus what we had run since, did not put us within a hundred miles of land.
crsnk10{_}975{_}But there was the land, fading away before our eyes in the fires of sunset.
crsnk10{_}976{_}The land was all right.
crsnk10{_}977{_}There was no disputing it.
crsnk10{_}978{_}Therefore our navigation was all wrong.
crsnk10{_}979{_}But it wasn't.
crsnk10{_}980{_}That land we saw was the summit of Haleakala, the House of the Sun, the greatest extinct volcano in the world.
crsnk10{_}981{_}It towered ten thousand feet above the sea, and it was all of a hundred miles away.
crsnk10{_}982{_}We sailed all night at a seven-knot clip, and in the morning the House of the Sun was still before us, and it took a few more hours of sailing to bring it abreast of us.
crsnk10{_}983{_}"That island is Maui," we said, verifying by the chart.
crsnk10{_}984{_}"That next island sticking out is Molokai, where the lepers are.
crsnk10{_}985{_}And the island next to that is Oahu.
crsnk10{_}986{_}There is Makapuu Head now.
crsnk10{_}987{_}We'll be in Honolulu to-morrow.
crsnk10{_}988{_}Our navigation is all right."
crsnk10{_}989{_}CHAPTER V--THE FIRST LANDFALL    "It will not be so monotonous at sea," I promised my fellow-voyagers on the Snark.
crsnk10{_}990{_}"The sea is filled with life.
crsnk10{_}991{_}It is so populous that every day something new is happening.
crsnk10{_}992{_}Almost as soon as we pass through the Golden Gate and head south we'll pick up with the flying fish.
crsnk10{_}993{_}We'll be having them fried for breakfast.
crsnk10{_}994{_}We'll be catching bonita and dolphin, and spearing porpoises from the bowsprit.
crsnk10{_}995{_}And then there are the sharks--sharks without end."
crsnk10{_}996{_}We passed through the Golden Gate and headed south.
crsnk10{_}997{_}We dropped the mountains of California beneath the horizon, and daily the surf grew warmer.
crsnk10{_}998{_}But there were no flying fish, no bonita and dolphin.
crsnk10{_}999{_}The ocean was bereft of life.
crsnk10{_}1000{_}Never had I sailed on so forsaken a sea.
crsnk10{_}1001{_}Always, before, in the same latitudes, had I encountered flying fish.
crsnk10{_}1002{_}"Never mind," I said.
crsnk10{_}1003{_}"Wait till we get off the coast of Southern California.
crsnk10{_}1004{_}Then we'll pick up the flying fish."
crsnk10{_}1005{_}We came abreast of Southern California, abreast of the Peninsula of Lower California, abreast of the coast of Mexico; and there were no flying fish.
crsnk10{_}1006{_}Nor was there anything else.
crsnk10{_}1007{_}No life moved.
crsnk10{_}1008{_}As the days went by the absence of life became almost uncanny.
crsnk10{_}1009{_}"Never mind," I said.
crsnk10{_}1010{_}"When we do pick up with the flying fish we'll pick up with everything else.
crsnk10{_}1011{_}The flying fish is the staff of life for all the other breeds.
crsnk10{_}1012{_}Everything will come in a bunch when we find the flying fish."
crsnk10{_}1013{_}When I should have headed the Snark south-west for Hawaii, I still held her south.
crsnk10{_}1014{_}I was going to find those flying fish.
crsnk10{_}1015{_}Finally the time came when, if I wanted to go to Honolulu, I should have headed the Snark due west, instead of which I kept her south.
crsnk10{_}1016{_}Not until latitude 19 degrees did we encounter the first flying fish.
crsnk10{_}1017{_}He was very much alone.
crsnk10{_}1018{_}I saw him.
crsnk10{_}1019{_}Five other pairs of eager eyes scanned the sea all day, but never saw another.
crsnk10{_}1020{_}So sparse were the flying fish that nearly a week more elapsed before the last one on board saw his first flying fish.
crsnk10{_}1021{_}As for the dolphin, bonita, porpoise, and all the other hordes of life--there weren't any.
crsnk10{_}1022{_}Not even a shark broke surface with his ominous dorsal fin.
crsnk10{_}1023{_}Bert took a dip daily under the bowsprit, hanging on to the stays and dragging his body through the water.
crsnk10{_}1024{_}And daily he canvassed the project of letting go and having a decent swim.
crsnk10{_}1025{_}I did my best to dissuade him.
crsnk10{_}1026{_}But with him I had lost all standing as an authority on sea life.
crsnk10{_}1027{_}"If there are sharks," he demanded, "why don't they show up?"
crsnk10{_}1028{_}I assured him that if he really did let go and have a swim the sharks would promptly appear.
crsnk10{_}1029{_}This was a bluff on my part.
crsnk10{_}1030{_}I didn't believe it.
crsnk10{_}1031{_}It lasted as a deterrent for two days.
crsnk10{_}1032{_}The third day the wind fell calm, and it was pretty hot.
crsnk10{_}1033{_}The Snark was moving a knot an hour.
crsnk10{_}1034{_}Bert dropped down under the bowsprit and let go.
crsnk10{_}1035{_}And now behold the perversity of things.
crsnk10{_}1036{_}We had sailed across two thousand miles and more of ocean and had met with no sharks.
crsnk10{_}1037{_}Within five minutes after Bert finished his swim, the fin of a shark was cutting the surface in circles around the Snark.
crsnk10{_}1038{_}There was something wrong about that shark.
crsnk10{_}1039{_}It bothered me.
crsnk10{_}1040{_}It had no right to be there in that deserted ocean.
crsnk10{_}1041{_}The more I thought about it, the more incomprehensible it became.
crsnk10{_}1042{_}But two hours later we sighted land and the mystery was cleared up.
crsnk10{_}1043{_}He had come to us from the land, and not from the uninhabited deep.
crsnk10{_}1044{_}He had presaged the landfall.
crsnk10{_}1045{_}He was the messenger of the land.
crsnk10{_}1046{_}Twenty-seven days out from San Francisco we arrived at the island of Oahu, Territory of Hawaii.
crsnk10{_}1047{_}In the early morning we drifted around Diamond Head into full view of Honolulu; and then the ocean burst suddenly into life.
crsnk10{_}1048{_}Flying fish cleaved the air in glittering squadrons.
crsnk10{_}1049{_}In five minutes we saw more of them than during the whole voyage.
crsnk10{_}1050{_}Other fish, large ones, of various sorts, leaped into the air.
crsnk10{_}1051{_}There was life everywhere, on sea and shore.
crsnk10{_}1052{_}We could see the masts and funnels of the shipping in the harbour, the hotels and bathers along the beach at Waikiki, the smoke rising from the dwelling-houses high up on the volcanic slopes of the Punch Bowl and Tantalus.
crsnk10{_}1053{_}The custom-house tug was racing toward us and a big school of porpoises got under our bow and began cutting the most ridiculous capers.
crsnk10{_}1054{_}The port doctor's launch came charging out at us, and a big sea turtle broke the surface with his back and took a look at us.
crsnk10{_}1055{_}Never was there such a burgeoning of life.
crsnk10{_}1056{_}Strange faces were on our decks, strange voices were speaking, and copies of that very morning's newspaper, with cable reports from all the world, were thrust before our eyes.
crsnk10{_}1057{_}Incidentally, we read that the Snark and all hands had been lost at sea, and that she had been a very unseaworthy craft anyway.
crsnk10{_}1058{_}And while we read this information a wireless message was being received by the congressional party on the summit of Haleakala announcing the safe arrival of the Snark.
crsnk10{_}1059{_}It was the Snark's first landfall--and such a landfall!
crsnk10{_}1060{_}For twenty- seven days we had been on the deserted deep, and it was pretty hard to realize that there was so much life in the world.
crsnk10{_}1061{_}We were made dizzy by it.
crsnk10{_}1062{_}We could not take it all in at once.
crsnk10{_}1063{_}We were like awakened Rip Van Winkles, and it seemed to us that we were dreaming.
crsnk10{_}1064{_}On one side the azure sea lapped across the horizon into the azure sky; on the other side the sea lifted itself into great breakers of emerald that fell in a snowy smother upon a white coral beach.
crsnk10{_}1065{_}Beyond the beach, green plantations of sugar-cane undulated gently upward to steeper slopes, which, in turn, became jagged volcanic crests, drenched with tropic showers and capped by stupendous masses of trade-wind clouds.
crsnk10{_}1066{_}At any rate, it was a most beautiful dream.
crsnk10{_}1067{_}The Snark turned and headed directly in toward the emerald surf, till it lifted and thundered on either hand; and on either hand, scarce a biscuit-toss away, the reef showed its long teeth, pale green and menacing.
crsnk10{_}1068{_}Abruptly the land itself, in a riot of olive-greens of a thousand hues, reached out its arms and folded the Snark in.
crsnk10{_}1069{_}There was no perilous passage through the reef, no emerald surf and azure sea-- nothing but a warm soft land, a motionless lagoon, and tiny beaches on which swam dark-skinned tropic children.
crsnk10{_}1070{_}The sea had disappeared.
crsnk10{_}1071{_}The Snark's anchor rumbled the chain through the hawse-pipe, and we lay without movement on a "lineless, level floor."
crsnk10{_}1072{_}It was all so beautiful and strange that we could not accept it as real.
crsnk10{_}1073{_}On the chart this place was called Pearl Harbour, but we called it Dream Harbour.
crsnk10{_}1074{_}A launch came off to us; in it were members of the Hawaiian Yacht Club, come to greet us and make us welcome, with true Hawaiian hospitality, to all they had.
crsnk10{_}1075{_}They were ordinary men, flesh and blood and all the rest; but they did not tend to break our dreaming.
crsnk10{_}1076{_}Our last memories of men were of United States marshals and of panicky little merchants with rusty dollars for souls, who, in a reeking atmosphere of soot and coal-dust, laid grimy hands upon the Snark and held her back from her world adventure.
crsnk10{_}1077{_}But these men who came to meet us were clean men.
crsnk10{_}1078{_}A healthy tan was on their cheeks, and their eyes were not dazzled and bespectacled from gazing overmuch at glittering dollar-heaps.
crsnk10{_}1079{_}No, they merely verified the dream.
crsnk10{_}1080{_}They clinched it with their unsmirched souls.
crsnk10{_}1081{_}So we went ashore with them across a level flashing sea to the wonderful green land.
crsnk10{_}1082{_}We landed on a tiny wharf, and the dream became more insistent; for know that for twenty-seven days we had been rocking across the ocean on the tiny Snark.
crsnk10{_}1083{_}Not once in all those twenty-seven days had we known a moment's rest, a moment's cessation from movement.
crsnk10{_}1084{_}This ceaseless movement had become ingrained.
crsnk10{_}1085{_}Body and brain we had rocked and rolled so long that when we climbed out on the tiny wharf kept on rocking and rolling.
crsnk10{_}1086{_}This, naturally, we attributed to the wharf.
crsnk10{_}1087{_}It was projected psychology.
crsnk10{_}1088{_}I spraddled along the wharf and nearly fell into the water.
crsnk10{_}1089{_}I glanced at Charmian, and the way she walked made me sad.
crsnk10{_}1090{_}The wharf had all the seeming of a ship's deck.
crsnk10{_}1091{_}It lifted, tilted, heaved and sank; and since there were no handrails on it, it kept Charmian and me busy avoiding falling in.
crsnk10{_}1092{_}I never saw such a preposterous little wharf.
crsnk10{_}1093{_}Whenever I watched it closely, it refused to roll; but as soon as I took my attention off from it, away it went, just like the Snark.
crsnk10{_}1094{_}Once, I caught it in the act, just as it upended, and I looked down the length of it for two hundred feet, and for all the world it was like the deck of a ship ducking into a huge head-sea.
crsnk10{_}1095{_}At last, however, supported by our hosts, we negotiated the wharf and gained the land.
crsnk10{_}1096{_}But the land was no better.
crsnk10{_}1097{_}The very first thing it did was to tilt up on one side, and far as the eye could see I watched it tilt, clear to its jagged, volcanic backbone, and I saw the clouds above tilt, too.
crsnk10{_}1098{_}This was no stable, firm-founded land, else it would not cut such capers.
crsnk10{_}1099{_}It was like all the rest of our landfall, unreal.
crsnk10{_}1100{_}It was a dream.
crsnk10{_}1101{_}At any moment, like shifting vapour, it might dissolve away.
crsnk10{_}1102{_}The thought entered my head that perhaps it was my fault, that my head was swimming or that something I had eaten had disagreed with me.
crsnk10{_}1103{_}But I glanced at Charmian and her sad walk, and even as I glanced I saw her stagger and bump into the yachtsman by whose side she walked.
crsnk10{_}1104{_}I spoke to her, and she complained about the antic behaviour of the land.
crsnk10{_}1105{_}We walked across a spacious, wonderful lawn and down an avenue of royal palms, and across more wonderful lawn in the gracious shade of stately trees.
crsnk10{_}1106{_}The air was filled with the songs of birds and was heavy with rich warm fragrances--wafture from great lilies, and blazing blossoms of hibiscus, and other strange gorgeous tropic flowers.
crsnk10{_}1107{_}The dream was becoming almost impossibly beautiful to us who for so long had seen naught but the restless, salty sea.
crsnk10{_}1108{_}Charmian reached out her hand and clung to me--for support against the ineffable beauty of it, thought I.
crsnk10{_}1109{_}But no.
crsnk10{_}1110{_}As I supported her I braced my legs, while the flowers and lawns reeled and swung around me.
crsnk10{_}1111{_}It was like an earthquake, only it quickly passed without doing any harm.
crsnk10{_}1112{_}It was fairly difficult to catch the land playing these tricks.
crsnk10{_}1113{_}As long as I kept my mind on it, nothing happened.
crsnk10{_}1114{_}But as soon as my attention was distracted, away it went, the whole panorama, swinging and heaving and tilting at all sorts of angles.
crsnk10{_}1115{_}Once, however, I turned my head suddenly and caught that stately line of royal palms swinging in a great arc across the sky.
crsnk10{_}1116{_}But it stopped, just as soon as I caught it, and became a placid dream again.
crsnk10{_}1117{_}Next we came to a house of coolness, with great sweeping veranda, where lotus-eaters might dwell.
crsnk10{_}1118{_}Windows and doors were wide open to the breeze, and the songs and fragrances blew lazily in and out.
crsnk10{_}1119{_}The walls were hung with tapa-cloths.
crsnk10{_}1120{_}Couches with grass-woven covers invited everywhere, and there was a grand piano, that played, I was sure, nothing more exciting than lullabies.
crsnk10{_}1121{_}Servants-- Japanese maids in native costume--drifted around and about, noiselessly, like butterflies.
crsnk10{_}1122{_}Everything was preternaturally cool.
crsnk10{_}1123{_}Here was no blazing down of a tropic sun upon an unshrinking sea.
crsnk10{_}1124{_}It was too good to be true.
crsnk10{_}1125{_}But it was not real.
crsnk10{_}1126{_}It was a dream- dwelling.
crsnk10{_}1127{_}I knew, for I turned suddenly and caught the grand piano cavorting in a spacious corner of the room.
crsnk10{_}1128{_}I did not say anything, for just then we were being received by a gracious woman, a beautiful Madonna, clad in flowing white and shod with sandals, who greeted us as though she had known us always.
crsnk10{_}1129{_}We sat at table on the lotus-eating veranda, served by the butterfly maids, and ate strange foods and partook of a nectar called poi.
crsnk10{_}1130{_}But the dream threatened to dissolve.
crsnk10{_}1131{_}It shimmered and trembled like an iridescent bubble about to break.
crsnk10{_}1132{_}I was just glancing out at the green grass and stately trees and blossoms of hibiscus, when suddenly I felt the table move.
crsnk10{_}1133{_}The table, and the Madonna across from me, and the veranda of the lotus-eaters, the scarlet hibiscus, the greensward and the trees--all lifted and tilted before my eyes, and heaved and sank down into the trough of a monstrous sea.
crsnk10{_}1134{_}I gripped my chair convulsively and held on.
crsnk10{_}1135{_}I had a feeling that I was holding on to the dream as well as the chair.
crsnk10{_}1136{_}I should not have been surprised had the sea rushed in and drowned all that fairyland and had I found myself at the wheel of the Snark just looking up casually from the study of logarithms.
crsnk10{_}1137{_}But the dream persisted.
crsnk10{_}1138{_}I looked covertly at the Madonna and her husband.
crsnk10{_}1139{_}They evidenced no perturbation.
crsnk10{_}1140{_}The dishes had not moved upon the table.
crsnk10{_}1141{_}The hibiscus and trees and grass were still there.
crsnk10{_}1142{_}Nothing had changed.
crsnk10{_}1143{_}I partook of more nectar, and the dream was more real than ever.
crsnk10{_}1144{_}"Will you have some iced tea?"
crsnk10{_}1145{_}asked the Madonna; and then her side of the table sank down gently and I said yes to her at an angle of forty-five degrees.
crsnk10{_}1146{_}"Speaking of sharks," said her husband, "up at Niihau there was a man--"  And at that moment the table lifted and heaved, and I gazed upward at him at an angle of forty-five degrees.
crsnk10{_}1147{_}So the luncheon went on, and I was glad that I did not have to bear the affliction of watching Charmian walk.
crsnk10{_}1148{_}Suddenly, however, a mysterious word of fear broke from the lips of the lotus-eaters.
crsnk10{_}1149{_}"Ah, ah," thought I, "now the dream goes glimmering."
crsnk10{_}1150{_}I clutched the chair desperately, resolved to drag back to the reality of the Snark some tangible vestige of this lotus land.
crsnk10{_}1151{_}I felt the whole dream lurching and pulling to be gone.
crsnk10{_}1152{_}Just then the mysterious word of fear was repeated.
crsnk10{_}1153{_}It sounded like REPORTERS.
crsnk10{_}1154{_}I looked and saw three of them coming across the lawn.
crsnk10{_}1155{_}Oh, blessed reporters!
crsnk10{_}1156{_}Then the dream was indisputably real after all.
crsnk10{_}1157{_}I glanced out across the shining water and saw the Snark at anchor, and I remembered that I had sailed in her from San Francisco to Hawaii, and that this was Pearl Harbour, and that even then I was acknowledging introductions and saying, in reply to the first question, "Yes, we had delightful weather all the way down."
crsnk10{_}1158{_}CHAPTER VI--A ROYAL SPORT    That is what it is, a royal sport for the natural kings of earth.
crsnk10{_}1159{_}The grass grows right down to the water at Waikiki Beach, and within fifty feet of the everlasting sea.
crsnk10{_}1160{_}The trees also grow down to the salty edge of things, and one sits in their shade and looks seaward at a majestic surf thundering in on the beach to one's very feet.
crsnk10{_}1161{_}Half a mile out, where is the reef, the white-headed combers thrust suddenly skyward out of the placid turquoise-blue and come rolling in to shore.
crsnk10{_}1162{_}One after another they come, a mile long, with smoking crests, the white battalions of the infinite army of the sea.
crsnk10{_}1163{_}And one sits and listens to the perpetual roar, and watches the unending procession, and feels tiny and fragile before this tremendous force expressing itself in fury and foam and sound.
crsnk10{_}1164{_}Indeed, one feels microscopically small, and the thought that one may wrestle with this sea raises in one's imagination a thrill of apprehension, almost of fear.
crsnk10{_}1165{_}Why, they are a mile long, these bull-mouthed monsters, and they weigh a thousand tons, and they charge in to shore faster than a man can run.
crsnk10{_}1166{_}What chance?
crsnk10{_}1167{_}No chance at all, is the verdict of the shrinking ego; and one sits, and looks, and listens, and thinks the grass and the shade are a pretty good place in which to be.
crsnk10{_}1168{_}And suddenly, out there where a big smoker lifts skyward, rising like a sea-god from out of the welter of spume and churning white, on the giddy, toppling, overhanging and downfalling, precarious crest appears the dark head of a man.
crsnk10{_}1169{_}Swiftly he rises through the rushing white.
crsnk10{_}1170{_}His black shoulders, his chest, his loins, his limbs--all is abruptly projected on one's vision.
crsnk10{_}1171{_}Where but the moment before was only the wide desolation and invincible roar, is now a man, erect, full-statured, not struggling frantically in that wild movement, not buried and crushed and buffeted by those mighty monsters, but standing above them all, calm and superb, poised on the giddy summit, his feet buried in the churning foam, the salt smoke rising to his knees, and all the rest of him in the free air and flashing sunlight, and he is flying through the air, flying forward, flying fast as the surge on which he stands.
crsnk10{_}1172{_}He is a Mercury--a brown Mercury.
crsnk10{_}1173{_}His heels are winged, and in them is the swiftness of the sea.
crsnk10{_}1174{_}In truth, from out of the sea he has leaped upon the back of the sea, and he is riding the sea that roars and bellows and cannot shake him from its back.
crsnk10{_}1175{_}But no frantic outreaching and balancing is his.
crsnk10{_}1176{_}He is impassive, motionless as a statue carved suddenly by some miracle out of the sea's depth from which he rose.
crsnk10{_}1177{_}And straight on toward shore he flies on his winged heels and the white crest of the breaker.
crsnk10{_}1178{_}There is a wild burst of foam, a long tumultuous rushing sound as the breaker falls futile and spent on the beach at your feet; and there, at your feet steps calmly ashore a Kanaka, burnt, golden and brown by the tropic sun.
crsnk10{_}1179{_}Several minutes ago he was a speck a quarter of a mile away.
crsnk10{_}1180{_}He has "bitted the bull-mouthed breaker" and ridden it in, and the pride in the feat shows in the carriage of his magnificent body as he glances for a moment carelessly at you who sit in the shade of the shore.
crsnk10{_}1181{_}He is a Kanaka--and more, he is a man, a member of the kingly species that has mastered matter and the brutes and lorded it over creation.
crsnk10{_}1182{_}And one sits and thinks of Tristram's last wrestle with the sea on that fatal morning; and one thinks further, to the fact that that Kanaka has done what Tristram never did, and that he knows a joy of the sea that Tristram never knew.
crsnk10{_}1183{_}And still further one thinks.
crsnk10{_}1184{_}It is all very well, sitting here in cool shade of the beach, but you are a man, one of the kingly species, and what that Kanaka can do, you can do yourself.
crsnk10{_}1185{_}Go to.
crsnk10{_}1186{_}Strip off your clothes that are a nuisance in this mellow clime.
crsnk10{_}1187{_}Get in and wrestle with the sea; wing your heels with the skill and power that reside in you; bit the sea's breakers, master them, and ride upon their backs as a king should.
crsnk10{_}1188{_}And that is how it came about that I tackled surf-riding.
crsnk10{_}1189{_}And now that I have tackled it, more than ever do I hold it to be a royal sport.
crsnk10{_}1190{_}But first let me explain the physics of it.
crsnk10{_}1191{_}A wave is a communicated agitation.
crsnk10{_}1192{_}The water that composes the body of a wave does not move.
crsnk10{_}1193{_}If it did, when a stone is thrown into a pond and the ripples spread away in an ever widening circle, there would appear at the centre an ever increasing hole.
crsnk10{_}1194{_}No, the water that composes the body of a wave is stationary.
crsnk10{_}1195{_}Thus, you may watch a particular portion of the ocean's surface and you will see the sane water rise and fall a thousand times to the agitation communicated by a thousand successive waves.
crsnk10{_}1196{_}Now imagine this communicated agitation moving shoreward.
crsnk10{_}1197{_}As the bottom shoals, the lower portion of the wave strikes land first and is stopped.
crsnk10{_}1198{_}But water is fluid, and the upper portion has not struck anything, wherefore it keeps on communicating its agitation, keeps on going.
crsnk10{_}1199{_}And when the top of the wave keeps on going, while the bottom of it lags behind, something is bound to happen.
crsnk10{_}1200{_}The bottom of the wave drops out from under and the top of the wave falls over, forward, and down, curling and cresting and roaring as it does so.
crsnk10{_}1201{_}It is the bottom of a wave striking against the top of the land that is the cause of all surfs.
crsnk10{_}1202{_}But the transformation from a smooth undulation to a breaker is not abrupt except where the bottom shoals abruptly.
crsnk10{_}1203{_}Say the bottom shoals gradually for from quarter of a mile to a mile, then an equal distance will be occupied by the transformation.
crsnk10{_}1204{_}Such a bottom is that off the beach of Waikiki, and it produces a splendid surf- riding surf.
crsnk10{_}1205{_}One leaps upon the back of a breaker just as it begins to break, and stays on it as it continues to break all the way in to shore.
crsnk10{_}1206{_}And now to the particular physics of surf-riding.
crsnk10{_}1207{_}Get out on a flat board, six feet long, two feet wide, and roughly oval in shape.
crsnk10{_}1208{_}Lie down upon it like a small boy on a coaster and paddle with your hands out to deep water, where the waves begin to crest.
crsnk10{_}1209{_}Lie out there quietly on the board.
crsnk10{_}1210{_}Sea after sea breaks before, behind, and under and over you, and rushes in to shore, leaving you behind.
crsnk10{_}1211{_}When a wave crests, it gets steeper.
crsnk10{_}1212{_}Imagine yourself, on your hoard, on the face of that steep slope.
crsnk10{_}1213{_}If it stood still, you would slide down just as a boy slides down a hill on his coaster.
crsnk10{_}1214{_}"But," you object, "the wave doesn't stand still."
crsnk10{_}1215{_}Very true, but the water composing the wave stands still, and there you have the secret.
crsnk10{_}1216{_}If ever you start sliding down the face of that wave, you'll keep on sliding and you'll never reach the bottom.
crsnk10{_}1217{_}Please don't laugh.
crsnk10{_}1218{_}The face of that wave may be only six feet, yet you can slide down it a quarter of a mile, or half a mile, and not reach the bottom.
crsnk10{_}1219{_}For, see, since a wave is only a communicated agitation or impetus, and since the water that composes a wave is changing every instant, new water is rising into the wave as fast as the wave travels.
crsnk10{_}1220{_}You slide down this new water, and yet remain in your old position on the wave, sliding down the still newer water that is rising and forming the wave.
crsnk10{_}1221{_}You slide precisely as fast as the wave travels.
crsnk10{_}1222{_}If it travels fifteen miles an hour, you slide fifteen miles an hour.
crsnk10{_}1223{_}Between you and shore stretches a quarter of mile of water.
crsnk10{_}1224{_}As the wave travels, this water obligingly heaps itself into the wave, gravity does the rest, and down you go, sliding the whole length of it.
crsnk10{_}1225{_}If you still cherish the notion, while sliding, that the water is moving with you, thrust your arms into it and attempt to paddle; you will find that you have to be remarkably quick to get a stroke, for that water is dropping astern just as fast as you are rushing ahead.
crsnk10{_}1226{_}And now for another phase of the physics of surf-riding.
crsnk10{_}1227{_}All rules have their exceptions.
crsnk10{_}1228{_}It is true that the water in a wave does not travel forward.
crsnk10{_}1229{_}But there is what may be called the send of the sea.
crsnk10{_}1230{_}The water in the overtoppling crest does move forward, as you will speedily realize if you are slapped in the face by it, or if you are caught under it and are pounded by one mighty blow down under the surface panting and gasping for half a minute.
crsnk10{_}1231{_}The water in the top of a wave rests upon the water in the bottom of the wave.
crsnk10{_}1232{_}But when the bottom of the wave strikes the land, it stops, while the top goes on.
crsnk10{_}1233{_}It no longer has the bottom of the wave to hold it up.
crsnk10{_}1234{_}Where was solid water beneath it, is now air, and for the first time it feels the grip of gravity, and down it falls, at the same time being torn asunder from the lagging bottom of the wave and flung forward.
crsnk10{_}1235{_}And it is because of this that riding a surf-board is something more than a mere placid sliding down a hill.
crsnk10{_}1236{_}In truth, one is caught up and hurled shoreward as by some Titan's hand.
crsnk10{_}1237{_}I deserted the cool shade, put on a swimming suit, and got hold of a surf-board.
crsnk10{_}1238{_}It was too small a board.
crsnk10{_}1239{_}But I didn't know, and nobody told me.
crsnk10{_}1240{_}I joined some little Kanaka boys in shallow water, where the breakers were well spent and small--a regular kindergarten school.
crsnk10{_}1241{_}I watched the little Kanaka boys.
crsnk10{_}1242{_}When a likely-looking breaker came along, they flopped upon their stomachs on their boards, kicked like mad with their feet, and rode the breaker in to the beach.
crsnk10{_}1243{_}I tried to emulate them.
crsnk10{_}1244{_}I watched them, tried to do everything that they did, and failed utterly.
crsnk10{_}1245{_}The breaker swept past, and I was not on it.
crsnk10{_}1246{_}I tried again and again.
crsnk10{_}1247{_}I kicked twice as madly as they did, and failed.
crsnk10{_}1248{_}Half a dozen would be around.
crsnk10{_}1249{_}We would all leap on our boards in front of a good breaker.
crsnk10{_}1250{_}Away our feet would churn like the stern-wheels of river steamboats, and away the little rascals would scoot while I remained in disgrace behind.
crsnk10{_}1251{_}I tried for a solid hour, and not one wave could I persuade to boost me shoreward.
crsnk10{_}1252{_}And then arrived a friend, Alexander Hume Ford, a globe trotter by profession, bent ever on the pursuit of sensation.
crsnk10{_}1253{_}And he had found it at Waikiki.
crsnk10{_}1254{_}Heading for Australia, he had stopped off for a week to find out if there were any thrills in surf-riding, and he had become wedded to it.
crsnk10{_}1255{_}He had been at it every day for a month and could not yet see any symptoms of the fascination lessening on him.
crsnk10{_}1256{_}He spoke with authority.
crsnk10{_}1257{_}"Get off that board," he said.
crsnk10{_}1258{_}"Chuck it away at once.
crsnk10{_}1259{_}Look at the way you're trying to ride it.
crsnk10{_}1260{_}If ever the nose of that board hits bottom, you'll be disembowelled.
crsnk10{_}1261{_}Here, take my board.
crsnk10{_}1262{_}It's a man's size."
crsnk10{_}1263{_}I am always humble when confronted by knowledge.
crsnk10{_}1264{_}Ford knew.
crsnk10{_}1265{_}He showed me how properly to mount his board.
crsnk10{_}1266{_}Then he waited for a good breaker, gave me a shove at the right moment, and started me in.
crsnk10{_}1267{_}Ah, delicious moment when I felt that breaker grip and fling me.
crsnk10{_}1268{_}On I dashed, a hundred and fifty feet, and subsided with the breaker on the sand.
crsnk10{_}1269{_}From that moment I was lost.
crsnk10{_}1270{_}I waded back to Ford with his board.
crsnk10{_}1271{_}It was a large one, several inches thick, and weighed all of seventy-five pounds.
crsnk10{_}1272{_}He gave me advice, much of it.
crsnk10{_}1273{_}He had had no one to teach him, and all that he had laboriously learned in several weeks he communicated to me in half an hour.
crsnk10{_}1274{_}I really learned by proxy.
crsnk10{_}1275{_}And inside of half an hour I was able to start myself and ride in.
crsnk10{_}1276{_}I did it time after time, and Ford applauded and advised.
crsnk10{_}1277{_}For instance, he told me to get just so far forward on the board and no farther.
crsnk10{_}1278{_}But I must have got some farther, for as I came charging in to land, that miserable board poked its nose down to bottom, stopped abruptly, and turned a somersault, at the same time violently severing our relations.
crsnk10{_}1279{_}I was tossed through the air like a chip and buried ignominiously under the downfalling breaker.
crsnk10{_}1280{_}And I realized that if it hadn't been for Ford, I'd have been disembowelled.
crsnk10{_}1281{_}That particular risk is part of the sport, Ford says.
crsnk10{_}1282{_}Maybe he'll have it happen to him before he leaves Waikiki, and then, I feel confident, his yearning for sensation will be satisfied for a time.
crsnk10{_}1283{_}When all is said and done, it is my steadfast belief that homicide is worse than suicide, especially if, in the former case, it is a woman.
crsnk10{_}1284{_}Ford saved me from being a homicide.
crsnk10{_}1285{_}"Imagine your legs are a rudder," he said.
crsnk10{_}1286{_}"Hold them close together, and steer with them."
crsnk10{_}1287{_}A few minutes later I came charging in on a comber.
crsnk10{_}1288{_}As I neared the beach, there, in the water, up to her waist, dead in front of me, appeared a woman.
crsnk10{_}1289{_}How was I to stop that comber on whose back I was?
crsnk10{_}1290{_}It looked like a dead woman.
crsnk10{_}1291{_}The board weighed seventy-five pounds, I weighed a hundred and sixty-five.
crsnk10{_}1292{_}The added weight had a velocity of fifteen miles per hour.
crsnk10{_}1293{_}The board and I constituted a projectile.
crsnk10{_}1294{_}I leave it to the physicists to figure out the force of the impact upon that poor, tender woman.
crsnk10{_}1295{_}And then I remembered my guardian angel, Ford.
crsnk10{_}1296{_}"Steer with your legs!"
crsnk10{_}1297{_}rang through my brain.
crsnk10{_}1298{_}I steered with my legs, I steered sharply, abruptly, with all my legs and with all my might.
crsnk10{_}1299{_}The board sheered around broadside on the crest.
crsnk10{_}1300{_}Many things happened simultaneously.
crsnk10{_}1301{_}The wave gave me a passing buffet, a light tap as the taps of waves go, but a tap sufficient to knock me off the board and smash me down through the rushing water to bottom, with which I came in violent collision and upon which I was rolled over and over.
crsnk10{_}1302{_}I got my head out for a breath of air and then gained my feet.
crsnk10{_}1303{_}There stood the woman before me.
crsnk10{_}1304{_}I felt like a hero.
crsnk10{_}1305{_}I had saved her life.
crsnk10{_}1306{_}And she laughed at me.
crsnk10{_}1307{_}It was not hysteria.
crsnk10{_}1308{_}She had never dreamed of her danger.
crsnk10{_}1309{_}Anyway, I solaced myself, it was not I but Ford that saved her, and I didn't have to feel like a hero.
crsnk10{_}1310{_}And besides, that leg-steering was great.
crsnk10{_}1311{_}In a few minutes more of practice I was able to thread my way in and out past several bathers and to remain on top my breaker instead of going under it.
crsnk10{_}1312{_}"To-morrow," Ford said, "I am going to take you out into the blue water."
crsnk10{_}1313{_}I looked seaward where he pointed, and saw the great smoking combers that made the breakers I had been riding look like ripples.
crsnk10{_}1314{_}I don't know what I might have said had I not recollected just then that I was one of a kingly species.
crsnk10{_}1315{_}So all that I did say was, "All right, I'll tackle them to-morrow."
crsnk10{_}1316{_}The water that rolls in on Waikiki Beach is just the same as the water that laves the shores of all the Hawaiian Islands; and in ways, especially from the swimmer's standpoint, it is wonderful water.
crsnk10{_}1317{_}It is cool enough to be comfortable, while it is warm enough to permit a swimmer to stay in all day without experiencing a chill.
crsnk10{_}1318{_}Under the sun or the stars, at high noon or at midnight, in midwinter or in midsummer, it does not matter when, it is always the same temperature--not too warm, not too cold, just right.
crsnk10{_}1319{_}It is wonderful water, salt as old ocean itself, pure and crystal-clear.
crsnk10{_}1320{_}When the nature of the water is considered, it is not so remarkable after all that the Kanakas are one of the most expert of swimming races.
crsnk10{_}1321{_}So it was, next morning, when Ford came along, that I plunged into the wonderful water for a swim of indeterminate length.
crsnk10{_}1322{_}Astride of our surf-boards, or, rather, flat down upon them on our stomachs, we paddled out through the kindergarten where the little Kanaka boys were at play.
crsnk10{_}1323{_}Soon we were out in deep water where the big smokers came roaring in.
crsnk10{_}1324{_}The mere struggle with them, facing them and paddling seaward over them and through them, was sport enough in itself.
crsnk10{_}1325{_}One had to have his wits about him, for it was a battle in which mighty blows were struck, on one side, and in which cunning was used on the other side--a struggle between insensate force and intelligence.
crsnk10{_}1326{_}I soon learned a bit.
crsnk10{_}1327{_}When a breaker curled over my head, for a swift instant I could see the light of day through its emerald body; then down would go my head, and I would clutch the board with all my strength.
crsnk10{_}1328{_}Then would come the blow, and to the onlooker on shore I would be blotted out.
crsnk10{_}1329{_}In reality the board and I have passed through the crest and emerged in the respite of the other side.
crsnk10{_}1330{_}I should not recommend those smashing blows to an invalid or delicate person.
crsnk10{_}1331{_}There is weight behind them, and the impact of the driven water is like a sandblast.
crsnk10{_}1332{_}Sometimes one passes through half a dozen combers in quick succession, and it is just about that time that he is liable to discover new merits in the stable land and new reasons for being on shore.
crsnk10{_}1333{_}Out there in the midst of such a succession of big smoky ones, a third man was added to our party, one Freeth.
crsnk10{_}1334{_}Shaking the water from my eyes as I emerged from one wave and peered ahead to see what the next one looked like, I saw him tearing in on the back of it, standing upright on his board, carelessly poised, a young god bronzed with sunburn.
crsnk10{_}1335{_}We went through the wave on the back of which he rode.
crsnk10{_}1336{_}Ford called to him.
crsnk10{_}1337{_}He turned an airspring from his wave, rescued his board from its maw, paddled over to us and joined Ford in showing me things.
crsnk10{_}1338{_}One thing in particular I learned from Freeth, namely, how to encounter the occasional breaker of exceptional size that rolled in.
crsnk10{_}1339{_}Such breakers were really ferocious, and it was unsafe to meet them on top of the board.
crsnk10{_}1340{_}But Freeth showed me, so that whenever I saw one of that calibre rolling down on me, I slid off the rear end of the board and dropped down beneath the surface, my arms over my head and holding the board.
crsnk10{_}1341{_}Thus, if the wave ripped the board out of my hands and tried to strike me with it (a common trick of such waves), there would be a cushion of water a foot or more in depth, between my head and the blow.
crsnk10{_}1342{_}When the wave passed, I climbed upon the board and paddled on.
crsnk10{_}1343{_}Many men have been terribly injured, I learn, by being struck by their boards.
crsnk10{_}1344{_}The whole method of surf-riding and surf-fighting, learned, is one of non-resistance.
crsnk10{_}1345{_}Dodge the blow that is struck at you.
crsnk10{_}1346{_}Dive through the wave that is trying to slap you in the face.
crsnk10{_}1347{_}Sink down, feet first, deep under the surface, and let the big smoker that is trying to smash you go by far overhead.
crsnk10{_}1348{_}Never be rigid.
crsnk10{_}1349{_}Relax.
crsnk10{_}1350{_}Yield yourself to the waters that are ripping and tearing at you.
crsnk10{_}1351{_}When the undertow catches you and drags you seaward along the bottom, don't struggle against it.
crsnk10{_}1352{_}If you do, you are liable to be drowned, for it is stronger than you.
crsnk10{_}1353{_}Yield yourself to that undertow.
crsnk10{_}1354{_}Swim with it, not against it, and you will find the pressure removed.
crsnk10{_}1355{_}And, swimming with it, fooling it so that it does not hold you, swim upward at the same time.
crsnk10{_}1356{_}It will be no trouble at all to reach the surface.
crsnk10{_}1357{_}The man who wants to learn surf-riding must be a strong swimmer, and he must be used to going under the water.
crsnk10{_}1358{_}After that, fair strength and common-sense are all that is required.
crsnk10{_}1359{_}The force of the big comber is rather unexpected.
crsnk10{_}1360{_}There are mix-ups in which board and rider are torn apart and separated by several hundred feet.
crsnk10{_}1361{_}The surf-rider must take care of himself.
crsnk10{_}1362{_}No matter how many riders swim out with him, he cannot depend upon any of them for aid.
crsnk10{_}1363{_}The fancied security I had in the presence of Ford and Freeth made me forget that it was my first swim out in deep water among the big ones.
crsnk10{_}1364{_}I recollected, however, and rather suddenly, for a big wave came in, and away went the two men on its back all the way to shore.
crsnk10{_}1365{_}I could have been drowned a dozen different ways before they got back to me.
crsnk10{_}1366{_}One slides down the face of a breaker on his surf-board, but he has to get started to sliding.
crsnk10{_}1367{_}Board and rider must be moving shoreward at a good rate before the wave overtakes them.
crsnk10{_}1368{_}When you see the wave coming that you want to ride in, you turn tail to it and paddle shoreward with all your strength, using what is called the windmill stroke.
crsnk10{_}1369{_}This is a sort of spurt performed immediately in front of the wave.
crsnk10{_}1370{_}If the board is going fast enough, the wave accelerates it, and the board begins its quarter-of-a-mile slide.
crsnk10{_}1371{_}I shall never forget the first big wave I caught out there in the deep water.
crsnk10{_}1372{_}I saw it coming, turned my back on it and paddled for dear life.
crsnk10{_}1373{_}Faster and faster my board went, till it seemed my arms would drop off.
crsnk10{_}1374{_}What was happening behind me I could not tell.
crsnk10{_}1375{_}One cannot look behind and paddle the windmill stroke.
crsnk10{_}1376{_}I heard the crest of the wave hissing and churning, and then my board was lifted and flung forward.
crsnk10{_}1377{_}I scarcely knew what happened the first half- minute.
crsnk10{_}1378{_}Though I kept my eyes open, I could not see anything, for I was buried in the rushing white of the crest.
crsnk10{_}1379{_}But I did not mind.
crsnk10{_}1380{_}I was chiefly conscious of ecstatic bliss at having caught the wave.
crsnk10{_}1381{_}At the end, of the half-minute, however, I began to see things, and to breathe.
crsnk10{_}1382{_}I saw that three feet of the nose of my board was clear out of water and riding on the air.
crsnk10{_}1383{_}I shifted my weight forward, and made the nose come down.
crsnk10{_}1384{_}Then I lay, quite at rest in the midst of the wild movement, and watched the shore and the bathers on the beach grow distinct.
crsnk10{_}1385{_}I didn't cover quite a quarter of a mile on that wave, because, to prevent the board from diving, I shifted my weight back, but shifted it too far and fell down the rear slope of the wave.
crsnk10{_}1386{_}It was my second day at surf-riding, and I was quite proud of myself.
crsnk10{_}1387{_}I stayed out there four hours, and when it was over, I was resolved that on the morrow I'd come in standing up.
crsnk10{_}1388{_}But that resolution paved a distant place.
crsnk10{_}1389{_}On the morrow I was in bed.
crsnk10{_}1390{_}I was not sick, but I was very unhappy, and I was in bed.
crsnk10{_}1391{_}When describing the wonderful water of Hawaii I forgot to describe the wonderful sun of Hawaii.
crsnk10{_}1392{_}It is a tropic sun, and, furthermore, in the first part of June, it is an overhead sun.
crsnk10{_}1393{_}It is also an insidious, deceitful sun.
crsnk10{_}1394{_}For the first time in my life I was sunburned unawares.
crsnk10{_}1395{_}My arms, shoulders, and back had been burned many times in the past and were tough; but not so my legs.
crsnk10{_}1396{_}And for four hours I had exposed the tender backs of my legs, at right- angles, to that perpendicular Hawaiian sun.
crsnk10{_}1397{_}It was not until after I got ashore that I discovered the sun had touched me.
crsnk10{_}1398{_}Sunburn at first is merely warm; after that it grows intense and the blisters come out.
crsnk10{_}1399{_}Also, the joints, where the skin wrinkles, refuse to bend.
crsnk10{_}1400{_}That is why I spent the next day in bed.
crsnk10{_}1401{_}I couldn't walk.
crsnk10{_}1402{_}And that is why, to-day, I am writing this in bed.
crsnk10{_}1403{_}It is easier to than not to.
crsnk10{_}1404{_}But to-morrow, ah, to-morrow, I shall be out in that wonderful water, and I shall come in standing up, even as Ford and Freeth.
crsnk10{_}1405{_}And if I fail to-morrow, I shall do it the next day, or the next.
crsnk10{_}1406{_}Upon one thing I am resolved:  the Snark shall not sail from Honolulu until I, too, wing my heels with the swiftness of the sea, and become a sun-burned, skin-peeling Mercury.
crsnk10{_}1407{_}CHAPTER VII--THE LEPERS OF MOLOKAI    When the Snark sailed along the windward coast of Molokai, on her way to Honolulu, I looked at the chart, then pointed to a low-lying peninsula backed by a tremendous cliff varying from two to four thousand feet in height, and said:  "The pit of hell, the most cursed place on earth."
crsnk10{_}1408{_}I should have been shocked, if, at that moment, I could have caught a vision of myself a month later, ashore in the most cursed place on earth and having a disgracefully good time along with eight hundred of the lepers who were likewise having a good time.
crsnk10{_}1409{_}Their good time was not disgraceful; but mine was, for in the midst of so much misery it was not meet for me to have a good time.
crsnk10{_}1410{_}That is the way I felt about it, and my only excuse is that I couldn't help having a good time.
crsnk10{_}1411{_}For instance, in the afternoon of the Fourth of July all the lepers gathered at the race-track for the sports.
crsnk10{_}1412{_}I had wandered away from the Superintendent and the physicians in order to get a snapshot of the finish of one of the races.
crsnk10{_}1413{_}It was an interesting race, and partisanship ran high.
crsnk10{_}1414{_}Three horses were entered, one ridden by a Chinese, one by an Hawaiian, and one by a Portuguese boy.
crsnk10{_}1415{_}All three riders were lepers; so were the judges and the crowd.
crsnk10{_}1416{_}The race was twice around the track.
crsnk10{_}1417{_}The Chinese and the Hawaiian got away together and rode neck and neck, the Portuguese boy toiling along two hundred feet behind.
crsnk10{_}1418{_}Around they went in the same positions.
crsnk10{_}1419{_}Halfway around on the second and final lap the Chinese pulled away and got one length ahead of the Hawaiian.
crsnk10{_}1420{_}At the same time the Portuguese boy was beginning to crawl up.
crsnk10{_}1421{_}But it looked hopeless.
crsnk10{_}1422{_}The crowd went wild.
crsnk10{_}1423{_}All the lepers were passionate lovers of horseflesh.
crsnk10{_}1424{_}The Portuguese boy crawled nearer and nearer.
crsnk10{_}1425{_}I went wild, too.
crsnk10{_}1426{_}They were on the home stretch.
crsnk10{_}1427{_}The Portuguese boy passed the Hawaiian.
crsnk10{_}1428{_}There was a thunder of hoofs, a rush of the three horses bunched together, the jockeys plying their whips, and every last onlooker bursting his throat, or hers, with shouts and yells.
crsnk10{_}1429{_}Nearer, nearer, inch by inch, the Portuguese boy crept up, and passed, yes, passed, winning by a head from the Chinese.
crsnk10{_}1430{_}I came to myself in a group of lepers.
crsnk10{_}1431{_}They were yelling, tossing their hats, and dancing around like fiends.
crsnk10{_}1432{_}So was I.
crsnk10{_}1433{_}When I came to I was waving my hat and murmuring ecstatically:  "By golly, the boy wins!
crsnk10{_}1434{_}The boy wins!"
crsnk10{_}1435{_}I tried to check myself.
crsnk10{_}1436{_}I assured myself that I was witnessing one of the horrors of Molokai, and that it was shameful for me, under such circumstances, to be so light-hearted and light-headed.
crsnk10{_}1437{_}But it was no use.
crsnk10{_}1438{_}The next event was a donkey-race, and it was just starting; so was the fun.
crsnk10{_}1439{_}The last donkey in was to win the race, and what complicated the affair was that no rider rode his own donkey.
crsnk10{_}1440{_}They rode one another's donkeys, the result of which was that each man strove to make the donkey he rode beat his own donkey ridden by some one else, Naturally, only men possessing very slow or extremely obstreperous donkeys had entered them for the race.
crsnk10{_}1441{_}One donkey had been trained to tuck in its legs and lie down whenever its rider touched its sides with his heels.
crsnk10{_}1442{_}Some donkeys strove to turn around and come back; others developed a penchant for the side of the track, where they stuck their heads over the railing and stopped; while all of them dawdled.
crsnk10{_}1443{_}Halfway around the track one donkey got into an argument with its rider.
crsnk10{_}1444{_}When all the rest of the donkeys had crossed the wire, that particular donkey was still arguing.
crsnk10{_}1445{_}He won the race, though his rider lost it and came in on foot.
crsnk10{_}1446{_}And all the while nearly a thousand lepers were laughing uproariously at the fun.
crsnk10{_}1447{_}Anybody in my place would have joined with them in having a good time.
crsnk10{_}1448{_}All the foregoing is by way of preamble to the statement that the horrors of Molokai, as they have been painted in the past, do not exist.
crsnk10{_}1449{_}The Settlement has been written up repeatedly by sensationalists, and usually by sensationalists who have never laid eyes on it.
crsnk10{_}1450{_}Of course, leprosy is leprosy, and it is a terrible thing; but so much that is lurid has been written about Molokai that neither the lepers, nor those who devote their lives to them, have received a fair deal.
crsnk10{_}1451{_}Here is a case in point.
crsnk10{_}1452{_}A newspaper writer, who, of course, had never been near the Settlement, vividly described Superintendent McVeigh, crouching in a grass hut and being besieged nightly by starving lepers on their knees, wailing for food.
crsnk10{_}1453{_}This hair-raising account was copied by the press all over the United States and was the cause of many indignant and protesting editorials.
crsnk10{_}1454{_}Well, I lived and slept for five days in Mr. McVeigh's "grass hut" (which was a comfortable wooden cottage, by the way; and there isn't a grass house in the whole Settlement), and I heard the lepers wailing for food--only the wailing was peculiarly harmonious and rhythmic, and it was accompanied by the music of stringed instruments, violins, guitars, ukuleles, and banjos.
crsnk10{_}1455{_}Also, the wailing was of various sorts.
crsnk10{_}1456{_}The leper brass band wailed, and two singing societies wailed, and lastly a quintet of excellent voices wailed.
crsnk10{_}1457{_}So much for a lie that should never have been printed.
crsnk10{_}1458{_}The wailing was the serenade which the glee clubs always give Mr. McVeigh when he returns from a trip to Honolulu.
crsnk10{_}1459{_}Leprosy is not so contagious as is imagined.
crsnk10{_}1460{_}I went for a week's visit to the Settlement, and I took my wife along--all of which would not have happened had we had any apprehension of contracting the disease.
crsnk10{_}1461{_}Nor did we wear long, gauntleted gloves and keep apart from the lepers.
crsnk10{_}1462{_}On the contrary, we mingled freely with them, and before we left, knew scores of them by sight and name.
crsnk10{_}1463{_}The precautions of simple cleanliness seem to be all that is necessary.
crsnk10{_}1464{_}On returning to their own houses, after having been among and handling lepers, the non-lepers, such as the physicians and the superintendent, merely wash their faces and hands with mildly antiseptic soap and change their coats.
crsnk10{_}1465{_}That a leper is unclean, however, should be insisted upon; and the segregation of lepers, from what little is known of the disease, should be rigidly maintained.
crsnk10{_}1466{_}On the other hand, the awful horror with which the leper has been regarded in the past, and the frightful treatment he has received, have been unnecessary and cruel.
crsnk10{_}1467{_}In order to dispel some of the popular misapprehensions of leprosy, I want to tell something of the relations between the lepers and non-lepers as I observed them at Molokai.
crsnk10{_}1468{_}On the morning after our arrival Charmian and I attended a shoot of the Kalaupapa Rifle Club, and caught our first glimpse of the democracy of affliction and alleviation that obtains.
crsnk10{_}1469{_}The club was just beginning a prize shoot for a cup put up by Mr. McVeigh, who is also a member of the club, as also are Dr. Goodhue and Dr. Hollmann, the resident physicians (who, by the way, live in the Settlement with their wives).
crsnk10{_}1470{_}All about us, in the shooting booth, were the lepers.
crsnk10{_}1471{_}Lepers and non-lepers were using the same guns, and all were rubbing shoulders in the confined space.
crsnk10{_}1472{_}The majority of the lepers were Hawaiians.
crsnk10{_}1473{_}Sitting beside me on a bench was a Norwegian.
crsnk10{_}1474{_}Directly in front of me, in the stand, was an American, a veteran of the Civil War, who had fought on the Confederate side.
crsnk10{_}1475{_}He was sixty- five years of age, but that did not prevent him from running up a good score.
crsnk10{_}1476{_}Strapping Hawaiian policemen, lepers, khaki-clad, were also shooting, as were Portuguese, Chinese, and kokuas--the latter are native helpers in the Settlement who are non-lepers.
crsnk10{_}1477{_}And on the afternoon that Charmian and I climbed the two-thousand-foot pali and looked our last upon the Settlement, the superintendent, the doctors, and the mixture of nationalities and of diseased and non- diseased were all engaged in an exciting baseball game.
crsnk10{_}1478{_}Not so was the leper and his greatly misunderstood and feared disease treated during the middle ages in Europe.
crsnk10{_}1479{_}At that time the leper was considered legally and politically dead.
crsnk10{_}1480{_}He was placed in a funeral procession and led to the church, where the burial service was read over him by the officiating clergyman.
crsnk10{_}1481{_}Then a spadeful of earth was dropped upon his chest and he was dead-living dead.
crsnk10{_}1482{_}While this rigorous treatment was largely unnecessary, nevertheless, one thing was learned by it.
crsnk10{_}1483{_}Leprosy was unknown in Europe until it was introduced by the returning Crusaders, whereupon it spread slowly until it had seized upon large numbers of the people.
crsnk10{_}1484{_}Obviously, it was a disease that could be contracted by contact.
crsnk10{_}1485{_}It was a contagion, and it was equally obvious that it could be eradicated by segregation.
crsnk10{_}1486{_}Terrible and monstrous as was the treatment of the leper in those days, the great lesson of segregation was learned.
crsnk10{_}1487{_}By its means leprosy was stamped out.
crsnk10{_}1488{_}And by the same means leprosy is even now decreasing in the Hawaiian Islands.
crsnk10{_}1489{_}But the segregation of the lepers on Molokai is not the horrible nightmare that has been so often exploited by YELLOW writers.
crsnk10{_}1490{_}In the first place, the leper is not torn ruthlessly from his family.
crsnk10{_}1491{_}When a suspect is discovered, he is invited by the Board of Health to come to the Kalihi receiving station at Honolulu.
crsnk10{_}1492{_}His fare and all expenses are paid for him.
crsnk10{_}1493{_}He is first passed upon by microscopical examination by the bacteriologist of the Board of Health.
crsnk10{_}1494{_}If the bacillus leprae is found, the patient is examined by the Board of Examining Physicians, five in number.
crsnk10{_}1495{_}If found by them to be a leper, he is so declared, which finding is later officially confirmed by the Board of Health, and the leper is ordered straight to Molokai.
crsnk10{_}1496{_}Furthermore, during the thorough trial that is given his case, the patient has the right to be represented by a physician whom he can select and employ for himself.
crsnk10{_}1497{_}Nor, after having been declared a leper, is the patient immediately rushed off to Molokai.
crsnk10{_}1498{_}He is given ample time, weeks, and even months, sometimes, during which he stays at Kalihi and winds up or arranges all his business affairs.
crsnk10{_}1499{_}At Molokai, in turn, he may be visited by his relatives, business agents, etc., though they are not permitted to eat and sleep in his house.
crsnk10{_}1500{_}Visitors' houses, kept "clean," are maintained for this purpose.
crsnk10{_}1501{_}I saw an illustration of the thorough trial given the suspect, when I visited Kalihi with Mr. Pinkham, president of the Board of Health.
crsnk10{_}1502{_}The suspect was an Hawaiian, seventy years of age, who for thirty- four years had worked in Honolulu as a pressman in a printing office.
crsnk10{_}1503{_}The bacteriologist had decided that he was a leper, the Examining Board had been unable to make up its mind, and that day all had come out to Kalihi to make another examination.
crsnk10{_}1504{_}When at Molokai, the declared leper has the privilege of re- examination, and patients are continually coming back to Honolulu for that purpose.
crsnk10{_}1505{_}The steamer that took me to Molokai had on board two returning lepers, both young women, one of whom had come to Honolulu to settle up some property she owned, and the other had come to Honolulu to see her sick mother.
crsnk10{_}1506{_}Both had remained at Kalihi for a month.
crsnk10{_}1507{_}The Settlement of Molokai enjoys a far more delightful climate than even Honolulu, being situated on the windward side of the island in the path of the fresh north-east trades.
crsnk10{_}1508{_}The scenery is magnificent; on one side is the blue sea, on the other the wonderful wall of the pali, receding here and there into beautiful mountain valleys.
crsnk10{_}1509{_}Everywhere are grassy pastures over which roam the hundreds of horses which are owned by the lepers.
crsnk10{_}1510{_}Some of them have their own carts, rigs, and traps.
crsnk10{_}1511{_}In the little harbour of Kalaupapa lie fishing boats and a steam launch, all of which are privately owned and operated by lepers.
crsnk10{_}1512{_}Their bounds upon the sea are, of course, determined:  otherwise no restriction is put upon their sea-faring.
crsnk10{_}1513{_}Their fish they sell to the Board of Health, and the money they receive is their own.
crsnk10{_}1514{_}While I was there, one night's catch was four thousand pounds.
crsnk10{_}1515{_}And as these men fish, others farm.
crsnk10{_}1516{_}All trades are followed.
crsnk10{_}1517{_}One leper, a pure Hawaiian, is the boss painter.
crsnk10{_}1518{_}He employs eight men, and takes contracts for painting buildings from the Board of Health.
crsnk10{_}1519{_}He is a member of the Kalaupapa Rifle Club, where I met him, and I must confess that he was far better dressed than I.
crsnk10{_}1520{_}Another man, similarly situated, is the boss carpenter.
crsnk10{_}1521{_}Then, in addition to the Board of Health store, there are little privately owned stores, where those with shopkeeper's souls may exercise their peculiar instincts.
crsnk10{_}1522{_}The Assistant Superintendent, Mr. Waiamau, a finely educated and able man, is a pure Hawaiian and a leper.
crsnk10{_}1523{_}Mr. Bartlett, who is the present storekeeper, is an American who was in business in Honolulu before he was struck down by the disease.
crsnk10{_}1524{_}All that these men earn is that much in their own pockets.
crsnk10{_}1525{_}If they do not work, they are taken care of anyway by the territory, given food, shelter, clothes, and medical attendance.
