crsnk10{_}2133{_}When hauled aboard, numerous remora were clinging to his shell, and out of the hollows at the roots of his flippers crawled several large crabs.
crsnk10{_}2134{_}It did not take the crew of the Snark longer than the next meal to reach the unanimous conclusion that it would willingly put the Snark about any time for a turtle.
crsnk10{_}2135{_}But it is the dolphin that is the king of deep-sea fishes.
crsnk10{_}2136{_}Never is his colour twice quite the same.
crsnk10{_}2137{_}Swimming in the sea, an ethereal creature of palest azure, he displays in that one guise a miracle of colour.
crsnk10{_}2138{_}But it is nothing compared with the displays of which he is capable.
crsnk10{_}2139{_}At one time he will appear green--pale green, deep green, phosphorescent green; at another time blue--deep blue, electric blue, all the spectrum of blue.
crsnk10{_}2140{_}Catch him on a hook, and he turns to gold, yellow gold, all gold.
crsnk10{_}2141{_}Haul him on deck, and he excels the spectrum, passing through inconceivable shades of blues, greens, and yellows, and then, suddenly, turning a ghostly white, in the midst of which are bright blue spots, and you suddenly discover that he is speckled like a trout.
crsnk10{_}2142{_}Then back from white he goes, through all the range of colours, finally turning to a mother-of-pearl.
crsnk10{_}2143{_}For those who are devoted to fishing, I can recommend no finer sport than catching dolphin.
crsnk10{_}2144{_}Of course, it must be done on a thin line with reel and pole.
crsnk10{_}2145{_}A No.
crsnk10{_}2146{_}7, O'Shaughnessy tarpon hook is just the thing, baited with an entire flying-fish.
crsnk10{_}2147{_}Like the bonita, the dolphin's fare consists of flying-fish, and he strikes like lightning at the bait.
crsnk10{_}2148{_}The first warning is when the reel screeches and you see the line smoking out at right angles to the boat.
crsnk10{_}2149{_}Before you have time to entertain anxiety concerning the length of your line, the fish rises into the air in a succession of leaps.
crsnk10{_}2150{_}Since he is quite certain to be four feet long or over, the sport of landing so gamey a fish can be realized.
crsnk10{_}2151{_}When hooked, he invariably turns golden.
crsnk10{_}2152{_}The idea of the series of leaps is to rid himself of the hook, and the man who has made the strike must be of iron or decadent if his heart does not beat with an extra flutter when he beholds such gorgeous fish, glittering in golden mail and shaking itself like a stallion in each mid-air leap.
crsnk10{_}2153{_}'Ware slack!
crsnk10{_}2154{_}If you don't, on one of those leaps the hook will be flung out and twenty feet away.
crsnk10{_}2155{_}No slack, and away he will go on another run, culminating in another series of leaps.
crsnk10{_}2156{_}About this time one begins to worry over the line, and to wish that he had had nine hundred feet on the reel originally instead of six hundred.
crsnk10{_}2157{_}With careful playing the line can be saved, and after an hour of keen excitement the fish can be brought to gaff.
crsnk10{_}2158{_}One such dolphin I landed on the Snark measured four feet and seven inches.
crsnk10{_}2159{_}Hermann caught dolphins more prosaically.
crsnk10{_}2160{_}A hand-line and a chunk of shark-meat were all he needed.
crsnk10{_}2161{_}His hand-line was very thick, but on more than one occasion it parted and lost the fish.
crsnk10{_}2162{_}One day a dolphin got away with a lure of Hermann's manufacture, to which were lashed four O'Shaughnessy hooks.
crsnk10{_}2163{_}Within an hour the same dolphin was landed with the rod, and on dissecting him the four hooks were recovered.
crsnk10{_}2164{_}The dolphins, which remained with us over a month, deserted us north of the line, and not one was seen during the remainder of the traverse.
crsnk10{_}2165{_}So the days passed.
crsnk10{_}2166{_}There was so much to be done that time never dragged.
crsnk10{_}2167{_}Had there been little to do, time could not have dragged with such wonderful seascapes and cloudscapes--dawns that were like burning imperial cities under rainbows that arched nearly to the zenith; sunsets that bathed the purple sea in rivers of rose- coloured light, flowing from a sun whose diverging, heaven-climbing rays were of the purest blue.
crsnk10{_}2168{_}Overside, in the heat of the day, the sea was an azure satiny fabric, in the depths of which the sunshine focussed in funnels of light.
crsnk10{_}2169{_}Astern, deep down, when there was a breeze, bubbled a procession of milky-turquoise ghosts--the foam flung down by the hull of the Snark each time she floundered against a sea.
crsnk10{_}2170{_}At night the wake was phosphorescent fire, where the medusa slime resented our passing bulk, while far down could be observed the unceasing flight of comets, with long, undulating, nebulous tails--caused by the passage of the bonitas through the resentful medusa slime.
crsnk10{_}2171{_}And now and again, from out of the darkness on either hand, just under the surface, larger phosphorescent organisms flashed up like electric lights, marking collisions with the careless bonitas skurrying ahead to the good hunting just beyond our bowsprit.
crsnk10{_}2172{_}We made our easting, worked down through the doldrums, and caught a fresh breeze out of south-by-west.
crsnk10{_}2173{_}Hauled up by the wind, on such a slant, we would fetch past the Marquesas far away to the westward.
crsnk10{_}2174{_}But the next day, on Tuesday, November 26, in the thick of a heavy squall, the wind shifted suddenly to the southeast.
crsnk10{_}2175{_}It was the trade at last.
crsnk10{_}2176{_}There were no more squalls, naught but fine weather, a fair wind, and a whirling log, with sheets slacked off and with spinnaker and mainsail swaying and bellying on either side.
crsnk10{_}2177{_}The trade backed more and more, until it blew out of the northeast, while we steered a steady course to the southwest.
crsnk10{_}2178{_}Ten days of this, and on the morning of December 6, at five o'clock, we sighted land "just where it ought to have been," dead ahead.
crsnk10{_}2179{_}We passed to leeward of Ua-huka, skirted the southern edge of Nuka-hiva, and that night, in driving squalls and inky darkness, fought our way in to an anchorage in the narrow bay of Taiohae.
crsnk10{_}2180{_}The anchor rumbled down to the blatting of wild goats on the cliffs, and the air we breathed was heavy with the perfume of flowers.
crsnk10{_}2181{_}The traverse was accomplished.
crsnk10{_}2182{_}Sixty days from land to land, across a lonely sea above whose horizons never rise the straining sails of ships.
crsnk10{_}2183{_}CHAPTER X--TYPEE    To the eastward Ua-huka was being blotted out by an evening rain- squall that was fast overtaking the Snark.
crsnk10{_}2184{_}But that little craft, her big spinnaker filled by the southeast trade, was making a good race of it.
crsnk10{_}2185{_}Cape Martin, the southeasternmost point of Nuku-hiva, was abeam, and Comptroller Bay was opening up as we fled past its wide entrance, where Sail Rock, for all the world like the spritsail of a Columbia River salmon-boat, was making brave weather of it in the smashing southeast swell.
crsnk10{_}2186{_}"What do you make that out to be?"
crsnk10{_}2187{_}I asked Hermann, at the wheel.
crsnk10{_}2188{_}"A fishing-boat, sir," he answered after careful scrutiny.
crsnk10{_}2189{_}Yet on the chart it was plainly marked, "Sail Rock."
crsnk10{_}2190{_}But we were more interested in the recesses of Comptroller Bay, where our eyes eagerly sought out the three bights of land and centred on the midmost one, where the gathering twilight showed the dim walls of a valley extending inland.
crsnk10{_}2191{_}How often we had pored over the chart and centred always on that midmost bight and on the valley it opened--the Valley of Typee.
crsnk10{_}2192{_}"Taipi" the chart spelled it, and spelled it correctly, but I prefer "Typee," and I shall always spell it "Typee."
crsnk10{_}2193{_}When I was a little boy, I read a book spelled in that manner--Herman Melville's "Typee"; and many long hours I dreamed over its pages.
crsnk10{_}2194{_}Nor was it all dreaming.
crsnk10{_}2195{_}I resolved there and then, mightily, come what would, that when I had gained strength and years, I, too, would voyage to Typee.
crsnk10{_}2196{_}For the wonder of the world was penetrating to my tiny consciousness--the wonder that was to lead me to many lands, and that leads and never pails.
crsnk10{_}2197{_}The years passed, but Typee was not forgotten.
crsnk10{_}2198{_}Returned to San Francisco from a seven months' cruise in the North Pacific, I decided the time had come.
crsnk10{_}2199{_}The brig Galilee was sailing for the Marquesas, but her crew was complete and I, who was an able-seaman before the mast and young enough to be overweeningly proud of it, was willing to condescend to ship as cabin-boy in order to make the pilgrimage to Typee.
crsnk10{_}2200{_}Of course, the Galilee would have sailed from the Marquesas without me, for I was bent on finding another Fayaway and another Kory-Kory.
crsnk10{_}2201{_}I doubt that the captain read desertion in my eye.
crsnk10{_}2202{_}Perhaps even the berth of cabin-boy was already filled.
crsnk10{_}2203{_}At any rate, I did not get it.
crsnk10{_}2204{_}Then came the rush of years, filled brimming with projects, achievements, and failures; but Typee was not forgotten, and here I was now, gazing at its misty outlines till the squall swooped down and the Snark dashed on into the driving smother.
crsnk10{_}2205{_}Ahead, we caught a glimpse and took the compass bearing of Sentinel Rock, wreathed with pounding surf.
crsnk10{_}2206{_}Then it, too, was effaced by the rain and darkness.
crsnk10{_}2207{_}We steered straight for it, trusting to hear the sound of breakers in time to sheer clear.
crsnk10{_}2208{_}We had to steer for it.
crsnk10{_}2209{_}We had naught but a compass bearing with which to orientate ourselves, and if we missed Sentinel Rock, we missed Taiohae Bay, and we would have to throw the Snark up to the wind and lie off and on the whole night--no pleasant prospect for voyagers weary from a sixty days' traverse of the vast Pacific solitude, and land-hungry, and fruit- hungry, and hungry with an appetite of years for the sweet vale of Typee.
crsnk10{_}2210{_}Abruptly, with a roar of sound, Sentinel Rock loomed through the rain dead ahead.
crsnk10{_}2211{_}We altered our course, and, with mainsail and spinnaker bellying to the squall, drove past.
crsnk10{_}2212{_}Under the lea of the rock the wind dropped us, and we rolled in an absolute calm.
crsnk10{_}2213{_}Then a puff of air struck us, right in our teeth, out of Taiohae Bay.
crsnk10{_}2214{_}It was in spinnaker, up mizzen, all sheets by the wind, and we were moving slowly ahead, heaving the lead and straining our eyes for the fixed red light on the ruined fort that would give us our bearings to anchorage.
crsnk10{_}2215{_}The air was light and baffling, now east, now west, now north, now south; while from either hand came the roar of unseen breakers.
crsnk10{_}2216{_}From the looming cliffs arose the blatting of wild goats, and overhead the first stars were peeping mistily through the ragged train of the passing squall.
crsnk10{_}2217{_}At the end of two hours, having come a mile into the bay, we dropped anchor in eleven fathoms.
crsnk10{_}2218{_}And so we came to Taiohae.
crsnk10{_}2219{_}In the morning we awoke in fairyland.
crsnk10{_}2220{_}The Snark rested in a placid harbour that nestled in a vast amphitheatre, the towering, vine-clad walls of which seemed to rise directly from the water.
crsnk10{_}2221{_}Far up, to the east, we glimpsed the thin line of a trail, visible in one place, where it scoured across the face of the wall.
crsnk10{_}2222{_}"The path by which Toby escaped from Typee!"
crsnk10{_}2223{_}we cried.
crsnk10{_}2224{_}We were not long in getting ashore and astride horses, though the consummation of our pilgrimage had to be deferred for a day.
crsnk10{_}2225{_}Two months at sea, bare-footed all the time, without space in which to exercise one's limbs, is not the best preliminary to leather shoes and walking.
crsnk10{_}2226{_}Besides, the land had to cease its nauseous rolling before we could feel fit for riding goat-like horses over giddy trails.
crsnk10{_}2227{_}So we took a short ride to break in, and crawled through thick jungle to make the acquaintance of a venerable moss-grown idol, where had foregathered a German trader and a Norwegian captain to estimate the weight of said idol, and to speculate upon depreciation in value caused by sawing him in half.
crsnk10{_}2228{_}They treated the old fellow sacrilegiously, digging their knives into him to see how hard he was and how deep his mossy mantle, and commanding him to rise up and save them trouble by walking down to the ship himself.
crsnk10{_}2229{_}In lieu of which, nineteen Kanakas slung him on a frame of timbers and toted him to the ship, where, battened down under hatches, even now he is cleaving the South Pacific Hornward and toward Europe--the ultimate abiding-place for all good heathen idols, save for the few in America and one in particular who grins beside me as I write, and who, barring shipwreck, will grin somewhere in my neighbourhood until I die.
crsnk10{_}2230{_}And he will win out.
crsnk10{_}2231{_}He will be grinning when I am dust.
crsnk10{_}2232{_}Also, as a preliminary, we attended a feast, where one Taiara Tamarii, the son of an Hawaiian sailor who deserted from a whaleship, commemorated the death of his Marquesan mother by roasting fourteen whole hogs and inviting in the village.
crsnk10{_}2233{_}So we came along, welcomed by a native herald, a young girl, who stood on a great rock and chanted the information that the banquet was made perfect by our presence--which information she extended impartially to every arrival.
crsnk10{_}2234{_}Scarcely were we seated, however, when she changed her tune, while the company manifested intense excitement.
crsnk10{_}2235{_}Her cries became eager and piercing.
crsnk10{_}2236{_}From a distance came answering cries, in men's voices, which blended into a wild, barbaric chant that sounded incredibly savage, smacking of blood and war.
crsnk10{_}2237{_}Then, through vistas of tropical foliage appeared a procession of savages, naked save for gaudy loin-cloths.
crsnk10{_}2238{_}They advanced slowly, uttering deep guttural cries of triumph and exaltation.
crsnk10{_}2239{_}Slung from young saplings carried on their shoulders were mysterious objects of considerable weight, hidden from view by wrappings of green leaves.
crsnk10{_}2240{_}Nothing but pigs, innocently fat and roasted to a turn, were inside those wrappings, but the men were carrying them into camp in imitation of old times when they carried in "long-pig."
crsnk10{_}2241{_}Now long- pig is not pig.
crsnk10{_}2242{_}Long-pig is the Polynesian euphemism for human flesh; and these descendants of man-eaters, a king's son at their head, brought in the pigs to table as of old their grandfathers had brought in their slain enemies.
crsnk10{_}2243{_}Every now and then the procession halted in order that the bearers should have every advantage in uttering particularly ferocious shouts of victory, of contempt for their enemies, and of gustatory desire.
crsnk10{_}2244{_}So Melville, two generations ago, witnessed the bodies of slain Happar warriors, wrapped in palm-leaves, carried to banquet at the Ti.
crsnk10{_}2245{_}At another time, at the Ti, he "observed a curiously carved vessel of wood," and on looking into it his eyes "fell upon the disordered members of a human skeleton, the bones still fresh with moisture, and with particles of flesh clinging to them here and there."
crsnk10{_}2246{_}Cannibalism has often been regarded as a fairy story by ultracivilized men who dislike, perhaps, the notion that their own savage forebears have somewhere in the past been addicted to similar practices.
crsnk10{_}2247{_}Captain Cook was rather sceptical upon the subject, until, one day, in a harbour of New Zealand, he deliberately tested the matter.
crsnk10{_}2248{_}A native happened to have brought on board, for sale, a nice, sun-dried head.
crsnk10{_}2249{_}At Cook's orders strips of the flesh were cut away and handed to the native, who greedily devoured them.
crsnk10{_}2250{_}To say the least, Captain Cook was a rather thorough-going empiricist.
crsnk10{_}2251{_}At any rate, by that act he supplied one ascertained fact of which science had been badly in need.
crsnk10{_}2252{_}Little did he dream of the existence of a certain group of islands, thousands of miles away, where in subsequent days there would arise a curious suit at law, when an old chief of Maui would be charged with defamation of character because he persisted in asserting that his body was the living repository of Captain Cook's great toe.
crsnk10{_}2253{_}It is said that the plaintiffs failed to prove that the old chief was not the tomb of the navigator's great toe, and that the suit was dismissed.
crsnk10{_}2254{_}I suppose I shall not have the chance in these degenerate days to see any long-pig eaten, but at least I am already the possessor of a duly certified Marquesan calabash, oblong in shape, curiously carved, over a century old, from which has been drunk the blood of two shipmasters.
crsnk10{_}2255{_}One of those captains was a mean man.
crsnk10{_}2256{_}He sold a decrepit whale-boat, as good as new what of the fresh white paint, to a Marquesan chief.
crsnk10{_}2257{_}But no sooner had the captain sailed away than the whale-boat dropped to pieces.
crsnk10{_}2258{_}It was his fortune, some time afterwards, to be wrecked, of all places, on that particular island.
crsnk10{_}2259{_}The Marquesan chief was ignorant of rebates and discounts; but he had a primitive sense of equity and an equally primitive conception of the economy of nature, and he balanced the account by eating the man who had cheated him.
crsnk10{_}2260{_}We started in the cool dawn for Typee, astride ferocious little stallions that pawed and screamed and bit and fought one another quite oblivious of the fragile humans on their backs and of the slippery boulders, loose rocks, and yawning gorges.
crsnk10{_}2261{_}The way led up an ancient road through a jungle of hau trees.
crsnk10{_}2262{_}On every side were the vestiges of a one-time dense population.
crsnk10{_}2263{_}Wherever the eye could penetrate the thick growth, glimpses were caught of stone walls and of stone foundations, six to eight feet in height, built solidly throughout, and many yards in width and depth.
crsnk10{_}2264{_}They formed great stone platforms, upon which, at one time, there had been houses.
crsnk10{_}2265{_}But the houses and the people were gone, and huge trees sank their roots through the platforms and towered over the under-running jungle.
crsnk10{_}2266{_}These foundations are called pae-paes--the pi-pis of Melville, who spelled phonetically.
crsnk10{_}2267{_}The Marquesans of the present generation lack the energy to hoist and place such huge stones.
crsnk10{_}2268{_}Also, they lack incentive.
crsnk10{_}2269{_}There are plenty of pae-paes to go around, with a few thousand unoccupied ones left over.
crsnk10{_}2270{_}Once or twice, as we ascended the valley, we saw magnificent pae-paes bearing on their general surface pitiful little straw huts, the proportions being similar to a voting booth perched on the broad foundation of the Pyramid of Cheops.
crsnk10{_}2271{_}For the Marquesans are perishing, and, to judge from conditions at Taiohae, the one thing that retards their destruction is the infusion of fresh blood.
crsnk10{_}2272{_}A pure Marquesan is a rarity.
crsnk10{_}2273{_}They seem to be all half-breeds and strange conglomerations of dozens of different races.
crsnk10{_}2274{_}Nineteen able labourers are all the trader at Taiohae can muster for the loading of copra on shipboard, and in their veins runs the blood of English, American, Dane, German, French, Corsican, Spanish, Portuguese, Chinese, Hawaiian, Paumotan, Tahitian, and Easter Islander.
crsnk10{_}2275{_}There are more races than there are persons, but it is a wreckage of races at best.
crsnk10{_}2276{_}Life faints and stumbles and gasps itself away.
crsnk10{_}2277{_}In this warm, equable clime--a truly terrestrial paradise--where are never extremes of temperature and where the air is like balm, kept ever pure by the ozone-laden southeast trade, asthma, phthisis, and tuberculosis flourish as luxuriantly as the vegetation.
crsnk10{_}2278{_}Everywhere, from the few grass huts, arises the racking cough or exhausted groan of wasted lungs.
crsnk10{_}2279{_}Other horrible diseases prosper as well, but the most deadly of all are those that attack the lungs.
crsnk10{_}2280{_}There is a form of consumption called "galloping," which is especially dreaded.
crsnk10{_}2281{_}In two months' time it reduces the strongest man to a skeleton under a grave-cloth.
crsnk10{_}2282{_}In valley after valley the last inhabitant has passed and the fertile soil has relapsed to jungle.
crsnk10{_}2283{_}In Melville's day the valley of Hapaa (spelled by him "Happar") was peopled by a strong and warlike tribe.
crsnk10{_}2284{_}A generation later, it contained but two hundred persons.
crsnk10{_}2285{_}To-day it is an untenanted, howling, tropical wilderness.
crsnk10{_}2286{_}We climbed higher and higher in the valley, our unshod stallions picking their steps on the disintegrating trail, which led in and out through the abandoned pae-paes and insatiable jungle.
crsnk10{_}2287{_}The sight of red mountain apples, the ohias, familiar to us from Hawaii, caused a native to be sent climbing after them.
crsnk10{_}2288{_}And again he climbed for cocoa-nuts.
crsnk10{_}2289{_}I have drunk the cocoanuts of Jamaica and of Hawaii, but I never knew how delicious such draught could be till I drank it here in the Marquesas.
crsnk10{_}2290{_}Occasionally we rode under wild limes and oranges--great trees which had survived the wilderness longer than the motes of humans who had cultivated them.
crsnk10{_}2291{_}We rode through endless thickets of yellow-pollened cassi--if riding it could be called; for those fragrant thickets were inhabited by wasps.
crsnk10{_}2292{_}And such wasps!
crsnk10{_}2293{_}Great yellow fellows the size of small canary birds, darting through the air with behind them drifting a bunch of legs a couple of inches long.
crsnk10{_}2294{_}A stallion abruptly stands on his forelegs and thrusts his hind legs skyward.
crsnk10{_}2295{_}He withdraws them from the sky long enough to make one wild jump ahead, and then returns them to their index position.
crsnk10{_}2296{_}It is nothing.
crsnk10{_}2297{_}His thick hide has merely been punctured by a flaming lance of wasp virility.
crsnk10{_}2298{_}Then a second and a third stallion, and all the stallions, begin to cavort on their forelegs over the precipitous landscape.
crsnk10{_}2299{_}Swat!
crsnk10{_}2300{_}A white-hot poniard penetrates my cheek.
crsnk10{_}2301{_}Swat again!!
crsnk10{_}2302{_}I am stabbed in the neck.
crsnk10{_}2303{_}I am bringing up the rear and getting more than my share.
crsnk10{_}2304{_}There is no retreat, and the plunging horses ahead, on a precarious trail, promise little safety.
crsnk10{_}2305{_}My horse overruns Charmian's horse, and that sensitive creature, fresh-stung at the psychological moment, planks one of his hoofs into my horse and the other hoof into me.
crsnk10{_}2306{_}I thank my stars that he is not steel-shod, and half-arise from the saddle at the impact of another flaming dagger.
crsnk10{_}2307{_}I am certainly getting more than my share, and so is my poor horse, whose pain and panic are only exceeded by mine.
crsnk10{_}2308{_}"Get out of the way!
crsnk10{_}2309{_}I'm coming!"
crsnk10{_}2310{_}I shout, frantically dashing my cap at the winged vipers around me.
crsnk10{_}2311{_}On one side of the trail the landscape rises straight up.
crsnk10{_}2312{_}On the other side it sinks straight down.
crsnk10{_}2313{_}The only way to get out of my way is to keep on going.
crsnk10{_}2314{_}How that string of horses kept their feet is a miracle; but they dashed ahead, over-running one another, galloping, trotting, stumbling, jumping, scrambling, and kicking methodically skyward every time a wasp landed on them.
crsnk10{_}2315{_}After a while we drew breath and counted our injuries.
crsnk10{_}2316{_}And this happened not once, nor twice, but time after time.
crsnk10{_}2317{_}Strange to say, it never grew monotonous.
crsnk10{_}2318{_}I know that I, for one, came through each brush with the undiminished zest of a man flying from sudden death.
crsnk10{_}2319{_}No; the pilgrim from Taiohae to Typee will never suffer from ennui on the way.
crsnk10{_}2320{_}At last we arose above the vexation of wasps.
crsnk10{_}2321{_}It was a matter of altitude, however, rather than of fortitude.
crsnk10{_}2322{_}All about us lay the jagged back-bones of ranges, as far as the eye could see, thrusting their pinnacles into the trade-wind clouds.
crsnk10{_}2323{_}Under us, from the way we had come, the Snark lay like a tiny toy on the calm water of Taiohae Bay.
crsnk10{_}2324{_}Ahead we could see the inshore indentation of Comptroller Bay.
crsnk10{_}2325{_}We dropped down a thousand feet, and Typee lay beneath us.
crsnk10{_}2326{_}"Had a glimpse of the gardens of paradise been revealed to me I could scarcely have been more ravished with the sight"--so said Melville on the moment of his first view of the valley.
crsnk10{_}2327{_}He saw a garden.
crsnk10{_}2328{_}We saw a wilderness.
crsnk10{_}2329{_}Where were the hundred groves of the breadfruit tree he saw?
crsnk10{_}2330{_}We saw jungle, nothing but jungle, with the exception of two grass huts and several clumps of cocoanuts breaking the primordial green mantle.
crsnk10{_}2331{_}Where was the Ti of Mehevi, the bachelors' hall, the palace where women were taboo, and where he ruled with his lesser chieftains, keeping the half-dozen dusty and torpid ancients to remind them of the valorous past?
crsnk10{_}2332{_}From the swift stream no sounds arose of maids and matrons pounding tapa.
crsnk10{_}2333{_}And where was the hut that old Narheyo eternally builded?
crsnk10{_}2334{_}In vain I looked for him perched ninety feet from the ground in some tall cocoanut, taking his morning smoke.
crsnk10{_}2335{_}We went down a zigzag trail under overarching, matted jungle, where great butterflies drifted by in the silence.
crsnk10{_}2336{_}No tattooed savage with club and javelin guarded the path; and when we forded the stream, we were free to roam where we pleased.
crsnk10{_}2337{_}No longer did the taboo, sacred and merciless, reign in that sweet vale.
crsnk10{_}2338{_}Nay, the taboo still did reign, a new taboo, for when we approached too near the several wretched native women, the taboo was uttered warningly.
crsnk10{_}2339{_}And it was well.
crsnk10{_}2340{_}They were lepers.
crsnk10{_}2341{_}The man who warned us was afflicted horribly with elephantiasis.
crsnk10{_}2342{_}All were suffering from lung trouble.
crsnk10{_}2343{_}The valley of Typee was the abode of death, and the dozen survivors of the tribe were gasping feebly the last painful breaths of the race.
crsnk10{_}2344{_}Certainly the battle had not been to the strong, for once the Typeans were very strong, stronger than the Happars, stronger than the Taiohaeans, stronger than all the tribes of Nuku-hiva.
crsnk10{_}2345{_}The word "typee," or, rather, "taipi," originally signified an eater of human flesh.
crsnk10{_}2346{_}But since all the Marquesans were human-flesh eaters, to be so designated was the token that the Typeans were the human-flesh eaters par excellence.
crsnk10{_}2347{_}Not alone to Nuku-hiva did the Typean reputation for bravery and ferocity extend.
crsnk10{_}2348{_}In all the islands of the Marquesas the Typeans were named with dread.
crsnk10{_}2349{_}Man could not conquer them.
crsnk10{_}2350{_}Even the French fleet that took possession of the Marquesas left the Typeans alone.
crsnk10{_}2351{_}Captain Porter, of the frigate Essex, once invaded the valley.
crsnk10{_}2352{_}His sailors and marines were reinforced by two thousand warriors of Happar and Taiohae.
crsnk10{_}2353{_}They penetrated quite a distance into the valley, but met with so fierce a resistance that they were glad to retreat and get away in their flotilla of boats and war-canoes.
crsnk10{_}2354{_}Of all inhabitants of the South Seas, the Marquesans were adjudged the strongest and the most beautiful.
crsnk10{_}2355{_}Melville said of them:  "I was especially struck by the physical strength and beauty they displayed .
crsnk10{_}2356{_}.
crsnk10{_}2357{_}.
crsnk10{_}2358{_}In beauty of form they surpassed anything I had ever seen.
crsnk10{_}2359{_}Not a single instance of natural deformity was observable in all the throng attending the revels.
crsnk10{_}2360{_}Every individual appeared free from those blemishes which sometimes mar the effect of an otherwise perfect form.
crsnk10{_}2361{_}But their physical excellence did not merely consist in an exemption from these evils; nearly every individual of the number might have been taken for a sculptor's model."
crsnk10{_}2362{_}Mendana, the discoverer of the Marquesas, described the natives as wondrously beautiful to behold.
crsnk10{_}2363{_}Figueroa, the chronicler of his voyage, said of them:  "In complexion they were nearly white; of good stature and finely formed."
crsnk10{_}2364{_}Captain Cook called the Marquesans the most splendid islanders in the South Seas.
crsnk10{_}2365{_}The men were described, as "in almost every instance of lofty stature, scarcely ever less than six feet in height."
crsnk10{_}2366{_}And now all this strength and beauty has departed, and the valley of Typee is the abode of some dozen wretched creatures, afflicted by leprosy, elephantiasis, and tuberculosis.
crsnk10{_}2367{_}Melville estimated the population at two thousand, not taking into consideration the small adjoining valley of Ho-o-u-mi.
crsnk10{_}2368{_}Life has rotted away in this wonderful garden spot, where the climate is as delightful and healthful as any to be found in the world.
crsnk10{_}2369{_}Not alone were the Typeans physically magnificent; they were pure.
crsnk10{_}2370{_}Their air did not contain the bacilli and germs and microbes of disease that fill our own air.
crsnk10{_}2371{_}And when the white men imported in their ships these various micro-organisms or disease, the Typeans crumpled up and went down before them.
crsnk10{_}2372{_}When one considers the situation, one is almost driven to the conclusion that the white race flourishes on impurity and corruption.
crsnk10{_}2373{_}Natural selection, however, gives the explanation.
crsnk10{_}2374{_}We of the white race are the survivors and the descendants of the thousands of generations of survivors in the war with the micro- organisms.
crsnk10{_}2375{_}Whenever one of us was born with a constitution peculiarly receptive to these minute enemies, such a one promptly died.
crsnk10{_}2376{_}Only those of us survived who could withstand them.
crsnk10{_}2377{_}We who are alive are the immune, the fit--the ones best constituted to live in a world of hostile micro-organisms.
crsnk10{_}2378{_}The poor Marquesans had undergone no such selection.
crsnk10{_}2379{_}They were not immune.
crsnk10{_}2380{_}And they, who had made a custom of eating their enemies, were now eaten by enemies so microscopic as to be invisible, and against whom no war of dart and javelin was possible.
crsnk10{_}2381{_}On the other hand, had there been a few hundred thousand Marquesans to begin with, there might have been sufficient survivors to lay the foundation for a new race--a regenerated race, if a plunge into a festering bath of organic poison can be called regeneration.
crsnk10{_}2382{_}We unsaddled our horses for lunch, and after we had fought the stallions apart--mine with several fresh chunks bitten out of his back--and after we had vainly fought the sand-flies, we ate bananas and tinned meats, washed down by generous draughts of cocoanut milk.
crsnk10{_}2383{_}There was little to be seen.
crsnk10{_}2384{_}The jungle had rushed back and engulfed the puny works of man.
crsnk10{_}2385{_}Here and there pai-pais were to be stumbled upon, but there were no inscriptions, no hieroglyphics, no clues to the past they attested--only dumb stones, builded and carved by hands that were forgotten dust.
crsnk10{_}2386{_}Out of the pai-pais grew great trees, jealous of the wrought work of man, splitting and scattering the stones back into the primeval chaos.
crsnk10{_}2387{_}We gave up the jungle and sought the stream with the idea of evading the sand-flies.
crsnk10{_}2388{_}Vain hope!
crsnk10{_}2389{_}To go in swimming one must take off his clothes.
crsnk10{_}2390{_}The sand-flies are aware of the fact, and they lurk by the river bank in countless myriads.
crsnk10{_}2391{_}In the native they are called the nau-nau, which is pronounced "now-now."
crsnk10{_}2392{_}They are certainly well named, for they are the insistent present.
crsnk10{_}2393{_}There is no past nor future when they fasten upon one's epidermis, and I am willing to wager that Omer Khayyam could never have written the Rubaiyat in the valley of Typee--it would have been psychologically impossible.
crsnk10{_}2394{_}I made the strategic mistake of undressing on the edge of a steep bank where I could dive in but could not climb out.
crsnk10{_}2395{_}When I was ready to dress, I had a hundred yards' walk on the bank before I could reach my clothes.
crsnk10{_}2396{_}At the first step, fully ten thousand nau-naus landed upon me.
crsnk10{_}2397{_}At the second step I was walking in a cloud.
crsnk10{_}2398{_}By the third step the sun was dimmed in the sky.
crsnk10{_}2399{_}After that I don't know what happened.
crsnk10{_}2400{_}When I arrived at my clothes, I was a maniac.
crsnk10{_}2401{_}And here enters my grand tactical error.
crsnk10{_}2402{_}There is only one rule of conduct in dealing with nau-naus.
crsnk10{_}2403{_}Never swat them.
crsnk10{_}2404{_}Whatever you do, don't swat them.
crsnk10{_}2405{_}They are so vicious that in the instant of annihilation they eject their last atom of poison into your carcass.
crsnk10{_}2406{_}You must pluck them delicately, between thumb and forefinger, and persuade them gently to remove their proboscides from your quivering flesh.
crsnk10{_}2407{_}It is like pulling teeth.
crsnk10{_}2408{_}But the difficulty was that the teeth sprouted faster than I could pull them, so I swatted, and, so doing, filled myself full with their poison.
crsnk10{_}2409{_}This was a week ago.
crsnk10{_}2410{_}At the present moment I resemble a sadly neglected smallpox convalescent.
crsnk10{_}2411{_}Ho-o-u-mi is a small valley, separated from Typee by a low ridge, and thither we started when we had knocked our indomitable and insatiable riding-animals into submission.
crsnk10{_}2412{_}As it was, Warren's mount, after a mile run, selected the most dangerous part of the trail for an exhibition that kept us all on the anxious seat for fully five minutes.
crsnk10{_}2413{_}We rode by the mouth of Typee valley and gazed down upon the beach from which Melville escaped.
crsnk10{_}2414{_}There was where the whale-boat lay on its oars close in to the surf; and there was where Karakoee, the taboo Kanaka, stood in the water and trafficked for the sailor's life.
crsnk10{_}2415{_}There, surely, was where Melville gave Fayaway the parting embrace ere he dashed for the boat.
crsnk10{_}2416{_}And there was the point of land from which Mehevi and Mow-mow and their following swam off to intercept the boat, only to have their wrists gashed by sheath-knives when they laid hold of the gunwale, though it was reserved for Mow-mow to receive the boat-hook full in the throat from Melville's hands.
crsnk10{_}2417{_}We rode on to Ho-o-u-mi.
crsnk10{_}2418{_}So closely was Melville guarded that he never dreamed of the existence of this valley, though he must continually have met its inhabitants, for they belonged to Typee.
crsnk10{_}2419{_}We rode through the same abandoned pae-paes, but as we neared the sea we found a profusion of cocoanuts, breadfruit trees and taro patches, and fully a dozen grass dwellings.
crsnk10{_}2420{_}In one of these we arranged to pass the night, and preparations were immediately put on foot for a feast.
crsnk10{_}2421{_}A young pig was promptly despatched, and while he was being roasted among hot stones, and while chickens were stewing in cocoanut milk, I persuaded one of the cooks to climb an unusually tall cocoanut palm.
crsnk10{_}2422{_}The cluster of nuts at the top was fully one hundred and twenty-five feet from the ground, but that native strode up to the tree, seized it in both hands, jack-knived at the waist so that the soles of his feet rested flatly against the trunk, and then he walked right straight up without stopping.
crsnk10{_}2423{_}There were no notches in the tree.
crsnk10{_}2424{_}He had no ropes to help him.
crsnk10{_}2425{_}He merely walked up the tree, one hundred and twenty-five feet in the air, and cast down the nuts from the summit.
crsnk10{_}2426{_}Not every man there had the physical stamina for such a feat, or the lungs, rather, for most of them were coughing their lives away.
crsnk10{_}2427{_}Some of the women kept up a ceaseless moaning and groaning, so badly were their lungs wasted.
crsnk10{_}2428{_}Very few of either sex were full-blooded Marquesans.
crsnk10{_}2429{_}They were mostly half- breeds and three-quarter-breeds of French, English, Danish, and Chinese extraction.
crsnk10{_}2430{_}At the best, these infusions of fresh blood merely delayed the passing, and the results led one to wonder whether it was worth while.
crsnk10{_}2431{_}The feast was served on a broad pae-pae, the rear portion of which was occupied by the house in which we were to sleep.
crsnk10{_}2432{_}The first course was raw fish and poi-poi, the latter sharp and more acrid of taste than the poi of Hawaii, which is made from taro.
crsnk10{_}2433{_}The poi-poi of the Marquesas is made from breadfruit.
crsnk10{_}2434{_}The ripe fruit, after the core is removed, is placed in a calabash and pounded with a stone pestle into a stiff, sticky paste.
crsnk10{_}2435{_}In this stage of the process, wrapped in leaves, it can be buried in the ground, where it will keep for years.
crsnk10{_}2436{_}Before it can be eaten, however, further processes are necessary.
crsnk10{_}2437{_}A leaf-covered package is placed among hot stones, like the pig, and thoroughly baked.
crsnk10{_}2438{_}After that it is mixed with cold water and thinned out--not thin enough to run, but thin enough to be eaten by sticking one's first and second fingers into it.
crsnk10{_}2439{_}On close acquaintance it proves a pleasant and most healthful food.
crsnk10{_}2440{_}And breadfruit, ripe and well boiled or roasted!
crsnk10{_}2441{_}It is delicious.
crsnk10{_}2442{_}Breadfruit and taro are kingly vegetables, the pair of them, though the former is patently a misnomer and more resembles a sweet potato than anything else, though it is not mealy like a sweet potato, nor is it so sweet.
crsnk10{_}2443{_}The feast ended, we watched the moon rise over Typee.
crsnk10{_}2444{_}The air was like balm, faintly scented with the breath of flowers.
crsnk10{_}2445{_}It was a magic night, deathly still, without the slightest breeze to stir the foliage; and one caught one's breath and felt the pang that is almost hurt, so exquisite was the beauty of it.
crsnk10{_}2446{_}Faint and far could be heard the thin thunder of the surf upon the beach.
crsnk10{_}2447{_}There were no beds; and we drowsed and slept wherever we thought the floor softest.
crsnk10{_}2448{_}Near by, a woman panted and moaned in her sleep, and all about us the dying islanders coughed in the night.
crsnk10{_}2449{_}CHAPTER XI--THE NATURE MAN    I first met him on Market Street in San Francisco.
crsnk10{_}2450{_}It was a wet and drizzly afternoon, and he was striding along, clad solely in a pair of abbreviated knee-trousers and an abbreviated shirt, his bare feet going slick-slick through the pavement-slush.
crsnk10{_}2451{_}At his heels trooped a score of excited gamins.
crsnk10{_}2452{_}Every head--and there were thousands-- turned to glance curiously at him as he went by.
crsnk10{_}2453{_}And I turned, too.
crsnk10{_}2454{_}Never had I seen such lovely sunburn.
crsnk10{_}2455{_}He was all sunburn, of the sort a blond takes on when his skin does not peel.
crsnk10{_}2456{_}His long yellow hair was burnt, so was his beard, which sprang from a soil unploughed by any razor.
crsnk10{_}2457{_}He was a tawny man, a golden-tawny man, all glowing and radiant with the sun.
crsnk10{_}2458{_}Another prophet, thought I, come up to town with a message that will save the world.
crsnk10{_}2459{_}A few weeks later I was with some friends in their bungalow in the Piedmont hills overlooking San Francisco Bay.
crsnk10{_}2460{_}"We've got him, we've got him," they barked.
crsnk10{_}2461{_}"We caught him up a tree; but he's all right now, he'll feed from the hand.
crsnk10{_}2462{_}Come on and see him."
crsnk10{_}2463{_}So I accompanied them up a dizzy hill, and in a rickety shack in the midst of a eucalyptus grove found my sunburned prophet of the city pavements.
crsnk10{_}2464{_}He hastened to meet us, arriving in the whirl and blur of a handspring.
crsnk10{_}2465{_}He did not shake hands with us; instead, his greeting took the form of stunts.
crsnk10{_}2466{_}He turned more handsprings.
crsnk10{_}2467{_}He twisted his body sinuously, like a snake, until, having sufficiently limbered up, he bent from the hips, and, with legs straight and knees touching, beat a tattoo on the ground with the palms of his hands.
crsnk10{_}2468{_}He whirligigged and pirouetted, dancing and cavorting round like an inebriated ape.
crsnk10{_}2469{_}All the sun-warmth of his ardent life beamed in his face.
crsnk10{_}2470{_}I am so happy, was the song without words he sang.
crsnk10{_}2471{_}He sang it all evening, ringing the changes on it with an endless variety of stunts.
crsnk10{_}2472{_}"A fool!
crsnk10{_}2473{_}a fool!
crsnk10{_}2474{_}I met a fool in the forest!"
crsnk10{_}2475{_}thought I, and a worthy fool he proved.
crsnk10{_}2476{_}Between handsprings and whirligigs he delivered his message that would save the world.
crsnk10{_}2477{_}It was twofold.
crsnk10{_}2478{_}First, let suffering humanity strip off its clothing and run wild in the mountains and valleys; and, second, let the very miserable world adopt phonetic spelling.
crsnk10{_}2479{_}I caught a glimpse of the great social problems being settled by the city populations swarming naked over the landscape, to the popping of shot-guns, the barking of ranch-dogs, and countless assaults with pitchforks wielded by irate farmers.
crsnk10{_}2480{_}The years passed, and, one sunny morning, the Snark poked her nose into a narrow opening in a reef that smoked with the crashing impact of the trade-wind swell, and beat slowly up Papeete harbour.
crsnk10{_}2481{_}Coming off to us was a boat, flying a yellow flag.
crsnk10{_}2482{_}We knew it contained the port doctor.
crsnk10{_}2483{_}But quite a distance off, in its wake, was a tiny out rigger canoe that puzzled us.
crsnk10{_}2484{_}It was flying a red flag.
crsnk10{_}2485{_}I studied it through the glasses, fearing that it marked some hidden danger to navigation, some recent wreck or some buoy or beacon that had been swept away.
crsnk10{_}2486{_}Then the doctor came on board.
crsnk10{_}2487{_}After he had examined the state of our health and been assured that we had no live rats hidden away in the Snark, I asked him the meaning of the red flag.
crsnk10{_}2488{_}"Oh, that is Darling," was the answer.
crsnk10{_}2489{_}And then Darling, Ernest Darling flying the red flag that is indicative of the brotherhood of man, hailed us.
crsnk10{_}2490{_}"Hello, Jack!"
crsnk10{_}2491{_}he called.
crsnk10{_}2492{_}"Hello, Charmian!
crsnk10{_}2493{_}He paddled swiftly nearer, and I saw that he was the tawny prophet of the Piedmont hills.
crsnk10{_}2494{_}He came over the side, a sun-god clad in a scarlet loin-cloth, with presents of Arcady and greeting in both his hands--a bottle of golden honey and a leaf-basket filled WITH great golden mangoes, golden bananas specked with freckles of deeper gold, golden pine-apples and golden limes, and juicy oranges minted from the same precious ore of sun and soil.
crsnk10{_}2495{_}And in this fashion under the southern sky, I met once more Darling, the Nature Man.
crsnk10{_}2496{_}Tahiti is one of the most beautiful spots in the world, inhabited by thieves and robbers and liars, also by several honest and truthful men and women.
crsnk10{_}2497{_}Wherefore, because of the blight cast upon Tahiti's wonderful beauty by the spidery human vermin that infest it, I am minded to write, not of Tahiti, but of the Nature Man.
crsnk10{_}2498{_}He, at least, is refreshing and wholesome.
crsnk10{_}2499{_}The spirit that emanates from him is so gentle and sweet that it would harm nothing, hurt nobody's feelings save the feelings of a predatory and plutocratic capitalist.
crsnk10{_}2500{_}"What does this red flag mean?"
crsnk10{_}2501{_}I asked.
crsnk10{_}2502{_}"Socialism, of course."
crsnk10{_}2503{_}"Yes, yes, I know that," I went on; "but what does it mean in your hands?"
crsnk10{_}2504{_}"Why, that I've found my message."
crsnk10{_}2505{_}"And that you are delivering it to Tahiti?"
crsnk10{_}2506{_}I demanded incredulously.
crsnk10{_}2507{_}"Sure," he answered simply; and later on I found that he was, too.
crsnk10{_}2508{_}When we dropped anchor, lowered a small boat into the water, and started ashore, the Nature Man joined us.
crsnk10{_}2509{_}Now, thought I, I shall be pestered to death by this crank.
crsnk10{_}2510{_}Waking or sleeping I shall never be quit of him until I sail away from here.
crsnk10{_}2511{_}But never in my life was I more mistaken.
crsnk10{_}2512{_}I took a house and went to live and work in it, and the Nature Man never came near me.
crsnk10{_}2513{_}He was waiting for the invitation.
crsnk10{_}2514{_}In the meantime he went aboard the Snark and took possession of her library, delighted by the quantity of scientific books, and shocked, as I learned afterwards, by the inordinate amount of fiction.
crsnk10{_}2515{_}The Nature Man never wastes time on fiction.
crsnk10{_}2516{_}After a week or so, my conscience smote me, and I invited him to dinner at a downtown hotel.
crsnk10{_}2517{_}He arrived, looking unwontedly stiff and uncomfortable in a cotton jacket.
crsnk10{_}2518{_}When invited to peel it off, he beamed his gratitude and joy, and did so, revealing his sun-gold skin, from waist to shoulder, covered only by a piece of fish-net of coarse twine and large of mesh.
crsnk10{_}2519{_}A scarlet loin-cloth completed his costume.
crsnk10{_}2520{_}I began my acquaintance with him that night, and during my long stay in Tahiti that acquaintance ripened into friendship.
crsnk10{_}2521{_}"So you write books," he said, one day when, tired and sweaty, I finished my morning's work.
crsnk10{_}2522{_}"I, too, write books," he announced.
crsnk10{_}2523{_}Aha, thought I, now at last is he going to pester me with his literary efforts.
crsnk10{_}2524{_}My soul was in revolt.
crsnk10{_}2525{_}I had not come all the way to the South Seas to be a literary bureau.
crsnk10{_}2526{_}"This is the book I write," he explained, smashing himself a resounding blow on the chest with his clenched fist.
crsnk10{_}2527{_}"The gorilla in the African jungle pounds his chest till the noise of it can be heard half a mile away."
crsnk10{_}2528{_}"A pretty good chest," quoth I, admiringly; "it would even make a gorilla envious."
crsnk10{_}2529{_}And then, and later, I learned the details of the marvellous book Ernest Darling had written.
crsnk10{_}2530{_}Twelve years ago he lay close to death.
crsnk10{_}2531{_}He weighed but ninety pounds, and was too weak to speak.
crsnk10{_}2532{_}The doctors had given him up.
crsnk10{_}2533{_}His father, a practising physician, had given him up.
crsnk10{_}2534{_}Consultations with other physicians had been held upon him.
crsnk10{_}2535{_}There was no hope for him.
crsnk10{_}2536{_}Overstudy (as a school- teacher and as a university student) and two successive attacks of pneumonia were responsible for his breakdown.
crsnk10{_}2537{_}Day by day he was losing strength.
crsnk10{_}2538{_}He could extract no nutrition from the heavy foods they gave him; nor could pellets and powders help his stomach to do the work of digestion.
crsnk10{_}2539{_}Not only was he a physical wreck, but he was a mental wreck.
crsnk10{_}2540{_}His mind was overwrought.
crsnk10{_}2541{_}He was sick and tired of medicine, and he was sick and tired of persons.
crsnk10{_}2542{_}Human speech jarred upon him.
crsnk10{_}2543{_}Human attentions drove him frantic.
crsnk10{_}2544{_}The thought came to him that since he was going to die, he might as well die in the open, away from all the bother and irritation.
crsnk10{_}2545{_}And behind this idea lurked a sneaking idea that perhaps he would not die after all if only he could escape from the heavy foods, the medicines, and the well-intentioned persons who made him frantic.
crsnk10{_}2546{_}So Ernest Darling, a bag of bones and a death's-head, a perambulating corpse, with just the dimmest flutter of life in it to make it perambulate, turned his back upon men and the habitations of men and dragged himself for five miles through the brush, away from the city of Portland, Oregon.
crsnk10{_}2547{_}Of course he was crazy.
crsnk10{_}2548{_}Only a lunatic would drag himself out of his death-bed.
crsnk10{_}2549{_}But in the brush, Darling found what he was looking for--rest.
crsnk10{_}2550{_}Nobody bothered him with beefsteaks and pork.
crsnk10{_}2551{_}No physicians lacerated his tired nerves by feeling his pulse, nor tormented his tired stomach with pellets and powders.
crsnk10{_}2552{_}He began to feel soothed.
crsnk10{_}2553{_}The sun was shining warm, and he basked in it.
crsnk10{_}2554{_}He had the feeling that the sun shine was an elixir of health.
crsnk10{_}2555{_}Then it seemed to him that his whole wasted wreck of a body was crying for the sun.
crsnk10{_}2556{_}He stripped off his clothes and bathed in the sunshine.
crsnk10{_}2557{_}He felt better.
crsnk10{_}2558{_}It had done him good--the first relief in weary months of pain.
crsnk10{_}2559{_}As he grew better, he sat up and began to take notice.
crsnk10{_}2560{_}All about him were the birds fluttering and chirping, the squirrels chattering and playing.
crsnk10{_}2561{_}He envied them their health and spirits, their happy, care-free existence.
crsnk10{_}2562{_}That he should contrast their condition with his was inevitable; and that he should question why they were splendidly vigorous while he was a feeble, dying wraith of a man, was likewise inevitable.
crsnk10{_}2563{_}His conclusion was the very obvious one, namely, that they lived naturally, while he lived most unnaturally therefore, if he intended to live, he must return to nature.
crsnk10{_}2564{_}Alone, there in the brush, he worked out his problem and began to apply it.
crsnk10{_}2565{_}He stripped off his clothing and leaped and gambolled about, running on all fours, climbing trees; in short, doing physical stunts,--and all the time soaking in the sunshine.
crsnk10{_}2566{_}He imitated the animals.
crsnk10{_}2567{_}He built a nest of dry leaves and grasses in which to sleep at night, covering it over with bark as a protection against the early fall rains.
crsnk10{_}2568{_}"Here is a beautiful exercise," he told me, once, flapping his arms mightily against his sides; "I learned it from watching the roosters crow."
crsnk10{_}2569{_}Another time I remarked the loud, sucking intake with which he drank cocoanut-milk.
crsnk10{_}2570{_}He explained that he had noticed the cows drinking that way and concluded there must be something in it.
crsnk10{_}2571{_}He tried it and found it good, and thereafter he drank only in that fashion.
crsnk10{_}2572{_}He noted that the squirrels lived on fruits and nuts.
crsnk10{_}2573{_}He started on a fruit-and-nut diet, helped out by bread, and he grew stronger and put on weight.
crsnk10{_}2574{_}For three months he continued his primordial existence in the brush, and then the heavy Oregon rains drove him back to the habitations of men.
crsnk10{_}2575{_}Not in three months could a ninety- pound survivor of two attacks of pneumonia develop sufficient ruggedness to live through an Oregon winter in the open.
crsnk10{_}2576{_}He had accomplished much, but he had been driven in.
crsnk10{_}2577{_}There was no place to go but back to his father's house, and there, living in close rooms with lungs that panted for all the air of the open sky, he was brought down by a third attack of pneumonia.
crsnk10{_}2578{_}He grew weaker even than before.
crsnk10{_}2579{_}In that tottering tabernacle of flesh, his brain collapsed.
crsnk10{_}2580{_}He lay like a corpse, too weak to stand the fatigue of speaking, too irritated and tired in his miserable brain to care to listen to the speech of others.
crsnk10{_}2581{_}The only act of will of which he was capable was to stick his fingers in his ears and resolutely to refuse to hear a single word that was spoken to him.
crsnk10{_}2582{_}They sent for the insanity experts.
crsnk10{_}2583{_}He was adjudged insane, and also the verdict was given that he would not live a month.
crsnk10{_}2584{_}By one such mental expert he was carted off to a sanatorium on Mt.
crsnk10{_}2585{_}Tabor.
crsnk10{_}2586{_}Here, when they learned that he was harmless, they gave him his own way.
crsnk10{_}2587{_}They no longer dictated as to the food he ate, so he resumed his fruits and nuts--olive oil, peanut butter, and bananas the chief articles of his diet.
crsnk10{_}2588{_}As he regained his strength he made up his mind to live thenceforth his own life.
crsnk10{_}2589{_}If he lived like others, according to social conventions, he would surely die.
crsnk10{_}2590{_}And he did not want to die.
crsnk10{_}2591{_}The fear of death was one of the strongest factors in the genesis of the Nature Man.
crsnk10{_}2592{_}To live, he must have a natural diet, the open air, and the blessed sunshine.
crsnk10{_}2593{_}Now an Oregon winter has no inducements for those who wish to return to Nature, so Darling started out in search of a climate.
crsnk10{_}2594{_}He mounted a bicycle and headed south for the sunlands.
crsnk10{_}2595{_}Stanford University claimed him for a year.
crsnk10{_}2596{_}Here he studied and worked his way, attending lectures in as scant garb as the authorities would allow and applying as much as possible the principles of living that he had learned in squirrel-town.
crsnk10{_}2597{_}His favourite method of study was to go off in the hills back of the University, and there to strip off his clothes and lie on the grass, soaking in sunshine and health at the same time that he soaked in knowledge.
crsnk10{_}2598{_}But Central California has her winters, and the quest for a Nature Man's climate drew him on.
crsnk10{_}2599{_}He tried Los Angeles and Southern California, being arrested a few times and brought before the insanity commissions because, forsooth, his mode of life was not modelled after the mode of life of his fellow-men.
crsnk10{_}2600{_}He tried Hawaii, where, unable to prove him insane, the authorities deported him.
crsnk10{_}2601{_}It was not exactly a deportation.
crsnk10{_}2602{_}He could have remained by serving a year in prison.
crsnk10{_}2603{_}They gave him his choice.
crsnk10{_}2604{_}Now prison is death to the Nature Man, who thrives only in the open air and in God's sunshine.
crsnk10{_}2605{_}The authorities of Hawaii are not to be blamed.
crsnk10{_}2606{_}Darling was an undesirable citizen.
crsnk10{_}2607{_}Any man is undesirable who disagrees with one.
crsnk10{_}2608{_}And that any man should disagree to the extent Darling did in his philosophy of the simple life is ample vindication of the Hawaiian authorities verdict of his undesirableness.
crsnk10{_}2609{_}So Darling went thence in search of a climate which would not only be desirable, but wherein he would not be undesirable.
crsnk10{_}2610{_}And he found it in Tahiti, the garden-spot of garden-spots.
crsnk10{_}2611{_}And so it was, according to the narrative as given, that he wrote the pages of his book.
crsnk10{_}2612{_}He wears only a loin-cloth and a sleeveless fish-net shirt.
crsnk10{_}2613{_}His stripped weight is one hundred and sixty-five pounds.
crsnk10{_}2614{_}His health is perfect.
crsnk10{_}2615{_}His eyesight, that at one time was considered ruined, is excellent.
crsnk10{_}2616{_}The lungs that were practically destroyed by three attacks of pneumonia have not only recovered, but are stronger than ever before.
crsnk10{_}2617{_}I shall never forget the first time, while talking to me, that he squashed a mosquito.
crsnk10{_}2618{_}The stinging pest had settled in the middle of his back between his shoulders.
crsnk10{_}2619{_}Without interrupting the flow of conversation, without dropping even a syllable, his clenched fist shot up in the air, curved backward, and smote his back between the shoulders, killing the mosquito and making his frame resound like a bass drum.
crsnk10{_}2620{_}It reminded me of nothing so much as of horses kicking the woodwork in their stalls.
crsnk10{_}2621{_}"The gorilla in the African jungle pounds his chest until the noise of it can be heard half a mile away," he will announce suddenly, and thereat beat a hair-raising, devil's tattoo on his own chest.
crsnk10{_}2622{_}One day he noticed a set of boxing-gloves hanging on the wall, and promptly his eyes brightened.
crsnk10{_}2623{_}"Do you box?"
crsnk10{_}2624{_}I asked.
crsnk10{_}2625{_}"I used to give lessons in boxing when I was at Stanford," was the reply.
crsnk10{_}2626{_}And there and then we stripped and put on the gloves.
crsnk10{_}2627{_}Bang!
crsnk10{_}2628{_}a long, gorilla arm flashed out, landing the gloved end on my nose.
crsnk10{_}2629{_}Biff!
crsnk10{_}2630{_}he caught me, in a duck, on the side of the head nearly knocking me over sidewise.
crsnk10{_}2631{_}I carried the lump raised by that blow for a week.
crsnk10{_}2632{_}I ducked under a straight left, and landed a straight right on his stomach.
crsnk10{_}2633{_}It was a fearful blow.
crsnk10{_}2634{_}The whole weight of my body was behind it, and his body had been met as it lunged forward.
crsnk10{_}2635{_}I looked for him to crumple up and go down.
crsnk10{_}2636{_}Instead of which his face beamed approval, and he said, "That was beautiful."
crsnk10{_}2637{_}The next instant I was covering up and striving to protect myself from a hurricane of hooks, jolts, and uppercuts.
crsnk10{_}2638{_}Then I watched my chance and drove in for the solar plexus.
crsnk10{_}2639{_}I hit the mark.
crsnk10{_}2640{_}The Nature Man dropped his arms, gasped, and sat down suddenly.
crsnk10{_}2641{_}"I'll be all right," he said.
crsnk10{_}2642{_}"Just wait a moment."
crsnk10{_}2643{_}And inside thirty seconds he was on his feet--ay, and returning the compliment, for he hooked me in the solar plexus, and I gasped, dropped my hands, and sat down just a trifle more suddenly than he had.
crsnk10{_}2644{_}All of which I submit as evidence that the man I boxed with was a totally different man from the poor, ninety-pound weight of eight years before, who, given up by physicians and alienists, lay gasping his life away in a closed room in Portland, Oregon.
crsnk10{_}2645{_}The book that Ernest Darling has written is a good book, and the binding is good, too.
crsnk10{_}2646{_}Hawaii has wailed for years her need for desirable immigrants.
crsnk10{_}2647{_}She has spent much time, and thought, and money, in importing desirable citizens, and she has, as yet, nothing much to show for it.
crsnk10{_}2648{_}Yet Hawaii deported the Nature Man.
crsnk10{_}2649{_}She refused to give him a chance.
crsnk10{_}2650{_}So it is, to chasten Hawaii's proud spirit, that I take this opportunity to show her what she has lost in the Nature Man.
crsnk10{_}2651{_}When he arrived in Tahiti, he proceeded to seek out a piece of land on which to grow the food he ate.
crsnk10{_}2652{_}But land was difficult to find--that is, inexpensive land.
crsnk10{_}2653{_}The Nature Man was not rolling in wealth.
crsnk10{_}2654{_}He spent weeks in wandering over the steep hills, until, high up the mountain, where clustered several tiny canyons, he found eighty acres of brush-jungle which were apparently unrecorded as the property of any one.
crsnk10{_}2655{_}The government officials told him that if he would clear the land and till it for thirty years he would be given a title for it.
crsnk10{_}2656{_}Immediately he set to work.
crsnk10{_}2657{_}And never was there such work.
crsnk10{_}2658{_}Nobody farmed that high up.
crsnk10{_}2659{_}The land was covered with matted jungle and overrun by wild pigs and countless rats.
crsnk10{_}2660{_}The view of Papeete and the sea was magnificent, but the outlook was not encouraging.
crsnk10{_}2661{_}He spent weeks in building a road in order to make the plantation accessible.
crsnk10{_}2662{_}The pigs and the rats ate up whatever he planted as fast as it sprouted.
crsnk10{_}2663{_}He shot the pigs and trapped the rats.
crsnk10{_}2664{_}Of the latter, in two weeks he caught fifteen hundred.
crsnk10{_}2665{_}Everything had to be carried up on his back.
crsnk10{_}2666{_}He usually did his packhorse work at night.
crsnk10{_}2667{_}Gradually he began to win out.
crsnk10{_}2668{_}A grass-walled house was built.
crsnk10{_}2669{_}On the fertile, volcanic soil he had wrested from the jungle and jungle beasts were growing five hundred cocoanut trees, five hundred papaia trees, three hundred mango trees, many breadfruit trees and alligator-pear trees, to say nothing of vines, bushes, and vegetables.
crsnk10{_}2670{_}He developed the drip of the hills in the canyons and worked out an efficient irrigation scheme, ditching the water from canyon to canyon and paralleling the ditches at different altitudes.
crsnk10{_}2671{_}His narrow canyons became botanical gardens.
crsnk10{_}2672{_}The arid shoulders of the hills, where formerly the blazing sun had parched the jungle and beaten it close to earth, blossomed into trees and shrubs and flowers.
crsnk10{_}2673{_}Not only had the Nature Man become self-supporting, but he was now a prosperous agriculturist with produce to sell to the city- dwellers of Papeete.
crsnk10{_}2674{_}Then it was discovered that his land, which the government officials had informed him was without an owner, really had an owner, and that deeds, descriptions, etc., were on record.
crsnk10{_}2675{_}All his work bade fare to be lost.
crsnk10{_}2676{_}The land had been valueless when he took it up, and the owner, a large landholder, was unaware of the extent to which the Nature Man had developed it.
crsnk10{_}2677{_}A just price was agreed upon, and Darling's deed was officially filed.
crsnk10{_}2678{_}Next came a more crushing blow.
crsnk10{_}2679{_}Darling's access to market was destroyed.
crsnk10{_}2680{_}The road he had built was fenced across by triple barb- wire fences.
crsnk10{_}2681{_}It was one of those jumbles in human affairs that is so common in this absurdest of social systems.
crsnk10{_}2682{_}Behind it was the fine hand of the same conservative element that haled the Nature Man before the Insanity Commission in Los Angeles and that deported him from Hawaii.
crsnk10{_}2683{_}It is so hard for self-satisfied men to understand any man whose satisfactions are fundamentally different.
crsnk10{_}2684{_}It seems clear that the officials have connived with the conservative element, for to this day the road the Nature Man built is closed; nothing has been done about it, while an adamant unwillingness to do anything about it is evidenced on every hand.
crsnk10{_}2685{_}But the Nature Man dances and sings along his way.
crsnk10{_}2686{_}He does not sit up nights thinking about the wrong which has been done him; he leaves the worrying to the doers of the wrong.
crsnk10{_}2687{_}He has no time for bitterness.
crsnk10{_}2688{_}He believes he is in the world for the purpose of being happy, and he has not a moment to waste in any other pursuit.
crsnk10{_}2689{_}The road to his plantation is blocked.
crsnk10{_}2690{_}He cannot build a new road, for there is no ground on which he can build it.
crsnk10{_}2691{_}The government has restricted him to a wild-pig trail which runs precipitously up the mountain.
crsnk10{_}2692{_}I climbed the trail with him, and we had to climb with hands and feet in order to get up.
crsnk10{_}2693{_}Nor can that wild-pig trail be made into a road by any amount of toil less than that of an engineer, a steam-engine, and a steel cable.
crsnk10{_}2694{_}But what does the Nature Man care?
crsnk10{_}2695{_}In his gentle ethics the evil men do him he requites with goodness.
crsnk10{_}2696{_}And who shall say he is not happier than they?
crsnk10{_}2697{_}"Never mind their pesky road," he said to me as we dragged ourselves up a shelf of rock and sat down, panting, to rest.
crsnk10{_}2698{_}"I'll get an air machine soon and fool them.
crsnk10{_}2699{_}I'm clearing a level space for a landing stage for the airships, and next time you come to Tahiti you will alight right at my door."
crsnk10{_}2700{_}Yes, the Nature Man has some strange ideas besides that of the gorilla pounding his chest in the African jungle.
crsnk10{_}2701{_}The Nature Man has ideas about levitation.
crsnk10{_}2702{_}"Yes, sir," he said to me, "levitation is not impossible.
crsnk10{_}2703{_}And think of the glory of it--lifting one's self from the ground by an act of will.
crsnk10{_}2704{_}Think of it!
crsnk10{_}2705{_}The astronomers tell us that our whole solar system is dying; that, barring accidents, it will all be so cold that no life can live upon it.
crsnk10{_}2706{_}Very well.
crsnk10{_}2707{_}In that day all men will be accomplished levitationists, and they will leave this perishing planet and seek more hospitable worlds.
crsnk10{_}2708{_}How can levitation be accomplished?
crsnk10{_}2709{_}By progressive fasts.
crsnk10{_}2710{_}Yes, I have tried them, and toward the end I could feel myself actually getting lighter."
crsnk10{_}2711{_}The man is a maniac, thought I.
crsnk10{_}2712{_}"Of course," he added, "these are only theories of mine.
crsnk10{_}2713{_}I like to speculate upon the glorious future of man.
crsnk10{_}2714{_}Levitation may not be possible, but I like to think of it as possible."
crsnk10{_}2715{_}One evening, when he yawned, I asked him how much sleep he allowed himself.
crsnk10{_}2716{_}"Seven hours," was the answer.
crsnk10{_}2717{_}"But in ten years I'll be sleeping only six hours, and in twenty years only five hours.
crsnk10{_}2718{_}You see, I shall cut off an hour's sleep every ten years."
crsnk10{_}2719{_}"Then when you are a hundred you won't be sleeping at all," I interjected.
crsnk10{_}2720{_}"Just that.
crsnk10{_}2721{_}Exactly that.
crsnk10{_}2722{_}When I am a hundred I shall not require sleep.
crsnk10{_}2723{_}Also, I shall be living on air.
crsnk10{_}2724{_}There are plants that live on air, you know."
crsnk10{_}2725{_}"But has any man ever succeeded in doing it?"
crsnk10{_}2726{_}He shook his head.
crsnk10{_}2727{_}"I never heard of him if he did.
crsnk10{_}2728{_}But it is only a theory of mine, this living on air.
crsnk10{_}2729{_}It would be fine, wouldn't it?
crsnk10{_}2730{_}Of course it may be impossible--most likely it is.
crsnk10{_}2731{_}You see, I am not unpractical.
crsnk10{_}2732{_}I never forget the present.
crsnk10{_}2733{_}When I soar ahead into the future, I always leave a string by which to find my way back again."
crsnk10{_}2734{_}I fear me the Nature Man is a joker.
crsnk10{_}2735{_}At any rate he lives the simple life.
crsnk10{_}2736{_}His laundry bill cannot be large.
crsnk10{_}2737{_}Up on his plantation he lives on fruit the labour cost of which, in cash, he estimates at five cents a day.
crsnk10{_}2738{_}At present, because of his obstructed road and because he is head over heels in the propaganda of socialism, he is living in town, where his expenses, including rent, are twenty-five cents a day.
crsnk10{_}2739{_}In order to pay those expenses he is running a night school for Chinese.
crsnk10{_}2740{_}The Nature Man is not bigoted.
crsnk10{_}2741{_}When there is nothing better to eat than meat, he eats meat, as, for instance, when in jail or on shipboard and the nuts and fruits give out.
crsnk10{_}2742{_}Nor does he seem to crystallize into anything except sunburn.
crsnk10{_}2743{_}"Drop anchor anywhere and the anchor will drag--that is, if your soul is a limitless, fathomless sea, and not dog-pound," he quoted to me, then added:  "You see, my anchor is always dragging.
crsnk10{_}2744{_}I live for human health and progress, and I strive to drag my anchor always in that direction.
crsnk10{_}2745{_}To me, the two are identical.
crsnk10{_}2746{_}Dragging anchor is what has saved me.
crsnk10{_}2747{_}My anchor did not hold me to my death-bed.
crsnk10{_}2748{_}I dragged anchor into the brush and fooled the doctors.
crsnk10{_}2749{_}When I recovered health and strength, I started, by preaching and by example, to teach the people to become nature men and nature women.
crsnk10{_}2750{_}But they had deaf ears.
crsnk10{_}2751{_}Then, on the steamer coming to Tahiti, a quarter-master expounded socialism to me.
crsnk10{_}2752{_}He showed me that an economic square deal was necessary before men and women could live naturally.
crsnk10{_}2753{_}So I dragged anchor once more, and now I am working for the co-operative commonwealth.
crsnk10{_}2754{_}When that arrives, it will be easy to bring about nature living.
crsnk10{_}2755{_}"I had a dream last night," he went on thoughtfully, his face slowly breaking into a glow.
crsnk10{_}2756{_}"It seemed that twenty-five nature men and nature women had just arrived on the steamer from California, and that I was starting to go with them up the wild-pig trail to the plantation."
crsnk10{_}2757{_}Ah, me, Ernest Darling, sun-worshipper and nature man, there are times when I am compelled to envy you and your carefree existence.
crsnk10{_}2758{_}I see you now, dancing up the steps and cutting antics on the veranda; your hair dripping from a plunge in the salt sea, your eyes sparkling, your sun-gilded body flashing, your chest resounding to the devil's own tattoo as you chant:  "The gorilla in the African jungle pounds his chest until the noise of it can be heard half a mile away."
crsnk10{_}2759{_}And I shall see you always as I saw you that last day, when the Snark poked her nose once more through the passage in the smoking reef, outward bound, and I waved good-bye to those on shore.
crsnk10{_}2760{_}Not least in goodwill and affection was the wave I gave to the golden sun-god in the scarlet loin-cloth, standing upright in his tiny outrigger canoe.
crsnk10{_}2761{_}CHAPTER XII--THE HIGH SEAT OF ABUNDANCE    On the arrival of strangers, every man endeavoured to obtain one as a friend and carry him off to his own habitation, where he is treated with the greatest kindness by the inhabitants of the district; they place him on a high seat and feed him with abundance of the finest food.--Polynesian Researches.
crsnk10{_}2762{_}The Snark was lying at anchor at Raiatea, just off the village of Uturoa.
crsnk10{_}2763{_}She had arrived the night before, after dark, and we were preparing to pay our first visit ashore.
crsnk10{_}2764{_}Early in the morning I had noticed a tiny outrigger canoe, with an impossible spritsail, skimming the surface of the lagoon.
crsnk10{_}2765{_}The canoe itself was coffin- shaped, a mere dugout, fourteen feet long, a scant twelve inches wide, and maybe twenty-four inches deep.
crsnk10{_}2766{_}It had no lines, except in so far that it was sharp at both ends.
crsnk10{_}2767{_}Its sides were perpendicular.
crsnk10{_}2768{_}Shorn of the outrigger, it would have capsized of itself inside a tenth of a second.
crsnk10{_}2769{_}It was the outrigger that kept it right side up.
crsnk10{_}2770{_}I have said that the sail was impossible.
crsnk10{_}2771{_}It was.
crsnk10{_}2772{_}It was one of those things, not that you have to see to believe, but that you cannot believe after you have seen it.
crsnk10{_}2773{_}The hoist of it and the length of its boom were sufficiently appalling; but, not content with that, its artificer had given it a tremendous head.
crsnk10{_}2774{_}So large was the head that no common sprit could carry the strain of it in an ordinary breeze.
crsnk10{_}2775{_}So a spar had been lashed to the canoe, projecting aft over the water.
crsnk10{_}2776{_}To this had been made fast a sprit guy:  thus, the foot of the sail was held by the main-sheet, and the peak by the guy to the sprit.
crsnk10{_}2777{_}It was not a mere boat, not a mere canoe, but a sailing machine.
crsnk10{_}2778{_}And the man in it sailed it by his weight and his nerve--principally by the latter.
crsnk10{_}2779{_}I watched the canoe beat up from leeward and run in toward the village, its sole occupant far out on the outrigger and luffing up and spilling the wind in the puffs.
crsnk10{_}2780{_}"Well, I know one thing," I announced; "I don't leave Raiatea till I have a ride in that canoe."
crsnk10{_}2781{_}A few minutes later Warren called down the companionway, "Here's that canoe you were talking about."
crsnk10{_}2782{_}Promptly I dashed on deck and gave greeting to its owner, a tall, slender Polynesian, ingenuous of face, and with clear, sparkling, intelligent eyes.
crsnk10{_}2783{_}He was clad in a scarlet loin-cloth and a straw hat.
crsnk10{_}2784{_}In his hands were presents--a fish, a bunch of greens, and several enormous yams.
crsnk10{_}2785{_}All of which acknowledged by smiles (which are coinage still in isolated spots of Polynesia) and by frequent repetitions of mauruuru (which is the Tahitian "thank you"), I proceeded to make signs that I desired to go for a sail in his canoe.
crsnk10{_}2786{_}His face lighted with pleasure and he uttered the single word, "Tahaa," turning at the same time and pointing to the lofty, cloud- draped peaks of an island three miles away--the island of Tahaa.
crsnk10{_}2787{_}It was fair wind over, but a head-beat back.
crsnk10{_}2788{_}Now I did not want to go to Tahaa.
crsnk10{_}2789{_}I had letters to deliver in Raiatea, and officials to see, and there was Charmian down below getting ready to go ashore.
crsnk10{_}2790{_}By insistent signs I indicated that I desired no more than a short sail on the lagoon.
crsnk10{_}2791{_}Quick was the disappointment in his face, yet smiling was the acquiescence.
crsnk10{_}2792{_}"Come on for a sail," I called below to Charmian.
crsnk10{_}2793{_}"But put on your swimming suit.
crsnk10{_}2794{_}It's going to be wet."
crsnk10{_}2795{_}It wasn't real.
crsnk10{_}2796{_}It was a dream.
crsnk10{_}2797{_}That canoe slid over the water like a streak of silver.
crsnk10{_}2798{_}I climbed out on the outrigger and supplied the weight to hold her down, while Tehei (pronounced Tayhayee) supplied the nerve.
crsnk10{_}2799{_}He, too, in the puffs, climbed part way out on the outrigger, at the same time steering with both hands on a large paddle and holding the mainsheet with his foot.
crsnk10{_}2800{_}"Ready about!"
crsnk10{_}2801{_}he called.
crsnk10{_}2802{_}I carefully shifted my weight inboard in order to maintain the equilibrium as the sail emptied.
crsnk10{_}2803{_}"Hard a-lee!"
crsnk10{_}2804{_}he called, shooting her into the wind.
crsnk10{_}2805{_}I slid out on the opposite side over the water on a spar lashed across the canoe, and we were full and away on the other tack.
crsnk10{_}2806{_}"All right," said Tehei.
crsnk10{_}2807{_}Those three phrases, "Ready about," "Hard a-lee," and "All right," comprised Tehei's English vocabulary and led me to suspect that at some time he had been one of a Kanaka crew under an American captain.
crsnk10{_}2808{_}Between the puffs I made signs to him and repeatedly and interrogatively uttered the word SAILOR.
crsnk10{_}2809{_}Then I tried it in atrocious French.
crsnk10{_}2810{_}MARIN conveyed no meaning to him; nor did MATELOT.
crsnk10{_}2811{_}Either my French was bad, or else he was not up in it.
crsnk10{_}2812{_}I have since concluded that both conjectures were correct.
crsnk10{_}2813{_}Finally, I began naming over the adjacent islands.
crsnk10{_}2814{_}He nodded that he had been to them.
crsnk10{_}2815{_}By the time my quest reached Tahiti, he caught my drift.
crsnk10{_}2816{_}His thought-processes were almost visible, and it was a joy to watch him think.
crsnk10{_}2817{_}He nodded his head vigorously.
crsnk10{_}2818{_}Yes, he had been to Tahiti, and he added himself names of islands such as Tikihau, Rangiroa, and Fakarava, thus proving that he had sailed as far as the Paumotus--undoubtedly one of the crew of a trading schooner.
crsnk10{_}2819{_}After our short sail, when he had returned on board, he by signs inquired the destination of the Snark, and when I had mentioned Samoa, Fiji, New Guinea, France, England, and California in their geographical sequence, he said "Samoa," and by gestures intimated that he wanted to go along.
crsnk10{_}2820{_}Whereupon I was hard put to explain that there was no room for him.
crsnk10{_}2821{_}"Petit bateau" finally solved it, and again the disappointment in his face was accompanied by smiling acquiescence, and promptly came the renewed invitation to accompany him to Tahaa.
crsnk10{_}2822{_}Charmian and I looked at each other.
crsnk10{_}2823{_}The exhilaration of the ride we had taken was still upon us.
crsnk10{_}2824{_}Forgotten were the letters to Raiatea, the officials we had to visit.
crsnk10{_}2825{_}Shoes, a shirt, a pair of trousers, cigarettes matches, and a book to read were hastily crammed into a biscuit tin and wrapped in a rubber blanket, and we were over the side and into the canoe.
crsnk10{_}2826{_}"When shall we look for you?"
crsnk10{_}2827{_}Warren called, as the wind filled the sail and sent Tehei and me scurrying out on the outrigger.
crsnk10{_}2828{_}"I don't know," I answered.
crsnk10{_}2829{_}"When we get back, as near as I can figure it."
crsnk10{_}2830{_}And away we went.
crsnk10{_}2831{_}The wind had increased, and with slacked sheets we ran off before it.
crsnk10{_}2832{_}The freeboard of the canoe was no more than two and a half inches, and the little waves continually lapped over the side.
crsnk10{_}2833{_}This required bailing.
crsnk10{_}2834{_}Now bailing is one of the principal functions of the vahine.
crsnk10{_}2835{_}Vahine is the Tahitian for woman, and Charmian being the only vahine aboard, the bailing fell appropriately to her.
crsnk10{_}2836{_}Tehei and I could not very well do it, the both of us being perched part way out on the outrigger and busied with keeping the canoe bottom-side down.
crsnk10{_}2837{_}So Charmian bailed, with a wooden scoop of primitive design, and so well did she do it that there were occasions when she could rest off almost half the time.
crsnk10{_}2838{_}Raiatea and Tahaa are unique in that they lie inside the same encircling reef.
crsnk10{_}2839{_}Both are volcanic islands, ragged of sky-line, with heaven-aspiring peaks and minarets.
crsnk10{_}2840{_}Since Raiatea is thirty miles in circumference, and Tahaa fifteen miles, some idea may be gained of the magnitude of the reef that encloses them.
crsnk10{_}2841{_}Between them and the reef stretches from one to two miles of water, forming a beautiful lagoon.
