crsnk10{_}4421{_}Out of the seven of us all told Tehei is the only one who has escaped; but his sufferings from nostalgia are worse than fever.
crsnk10{_}4422{_}Nakata, as usual, followed instructions faithfully, so that by the end of his third attack he could take a two hours' sweat, consume thirty or forty grains of quinine, and be weak but all right at the end of twenty-four hours.
crsnk10{_}4423{_}Wada and Henry, however, were tougher patients with which to deal.
crsnk10{_}4424{_}In the first place, Wada got in a bad funk.
crsnk10{_}4425{_}He was of the firm conviction that his star had set and that the Solomons would receive his bones.
crsnk10{_}4426{_}He saw that life about him was cheap.
crsnk10{_}4427{_}At Penduffryn he saw the ravages of dysentery, and, unfortunately for him, he saw one victim carried out on a strip of galvanized sheet-iron and dumped without coffin or funeral into a hole in the ground.
crsnk10{_}4428{_}Everybody had fever, everybody had dysentery, everybody had everything.
crsnk10{_}4429{_}Death was common.
crsnk10{_}4430{_}Here to-day and gone to-morrow--and Wada forgot all about to-day and made up his mind that to-morrow had come.
crsnk10{_}4431{_}He was careless of his ulcers, neglected to sublimate them, and by uncontrolled scratching spread them all over his body.
crsnk10{_}4432{_}Nor would he follow instructions with fever, and, as a result, would be down five days at a time, when a day would have been sufficient.
crsnk10{_}4433{_}Henry, who is a strapping giant of a man, was just as bad.
crsnk10{_}4434{_}He refused point blank to take quinine, on the ground that years before he had had fever and that the pills the doctor gave him were of different size and colour from the quinine tablets I offered him.
crsnk10{_}4435{_}So Henry joined Wada.
crsnk10{_}4436{_}But I fooled the pair of them, and dosed them with their own medicine, which was faith-cure.
crsnk10{_}4437{_}They had faith in their funk that they were going to die.
crsnk10{_}4438{_}I slammed a lot of quinine down their throats and took their temperature.
crsnk10{_}4439{_}It was the first time I had used my medicine-chest thermometer, and I quickly discovered that it was worthless, that it had been produced for profit and not for service.
crsnk10{_}4440{_}If I had let on to my two patients that the thermometer did not work, there would have been two funerals in short order.
crsnk10{_}4441{_}Their temperature I swear was 105 degrees.
crsnk10{_}4442{_}I solemnly made one and then the other smoke the thermometer, allowed an expression of satisfaction to irradiate my countenance, and joyfully told them that their temperature was 94 degrees.
crsnk10{_}4443{_}Then I slammed more quinine down their throats, told them that any sickness or weakness they might experience would be due to the quinine, and left them to get well.
crsnk10{_}4444{_}And they did get well, Wada in spite of himself.
crsnk10{_}4445{_}If a man can die through a misapprehension, is there any immorality in making him live through a misapprehension?
crsnk10{_}4446{_}Commend me the white race when it comes to grit and surviving.
crsnk10{_}4447{_}One of our two Japanese and both our Tahitians funked and had to be slapped on the back and cheered up and dragged along by main strength toward life.
crsnk10{_}4448{_}Charmian and Martin took their afflictions cheerfully, made the least of them, and moved with calm certitude along the way of life.
crsnk10{_}4449{_}When Wada and Henry were convinced that they were going to die, the funeral atmosphere was too much for Tehei, who prayed dolorously and cried for hours at a time.
crsnk10{_}4450{_}Martin, on the other hand, cursed and got well, and Charmian groaned and made plans for what she was going to do when she got well again.
crsnk10{_}4451{_}Charmian had been raised a vegetarian and a sanitarian.
crsnk10{_}4452{_}Her Aunt Netta, who brought her up and who lived in a healthful climate, did not believe in drugs.
crsnk10{_}4453{_}Neither did Charmian.
crsnk10{_}4454{_}Besides, drugs disagreed with her.
crsnk10{_}4455{_}Their effects were worse than the ills they were supposed to alleviate.
crsnk10{_}4456{_}But she listened to the argument in favour of quinine, accepted it as the lesser evil, and in consequence had shorter, less painful, and less frequent attacks of fever.
crsnk10{_}4457{_}We encountered a Mr. Caulfeild, a missionary, whose two predecessors had died after less than six months' residence in the Solomons.
crsnk10{_}4458{_}Like them he had been a firm believer in homeopathy, until after his first fever, whereupon, unlike them, he made a grand slide back to allopathy and quinine, catching fever and carrying on his Gospel work.
crsnk10{_}4459{_}But poor Wada!
crsnk10{_}4460{_}The straw that broke the cook's back was when Charmian and I took him along on a cruise to the cannibal island of Malaita, in a small yacht, on the deck of which the captain had been murdered half a year before.
crsnk10{_}4461{_}Kai-kai means to eat, and Wada was sure he was going to be kai-kai'd.
crsnk10{_}4462{_}We went about heavily armed, our vigilance was unremitting, and when we went for a bath in the mouth of a fresh-water stream, black boys, armed with rifles, did sentry duty about us.
crsnk10{_}4463{_}We encountered English war vessels burning and shelling villages in punishment for murders.
crsnk10{_}4464{_}Natives with prices on their heads sought shelter on board of us.
crsnk10{_}4465{_}Murder stalked abroad in the land.
crsnk10{_}4466{_}In out-of-they-way places we received warnings from friendly savages of impending attacks.
crsnk10{_}4467{_}Our vessel owed two heads to Malaita, which were liable to be collected any time.
crsnk10{_}4468{_}Then to cap it all, we were wrecked on a reef, and with rifles in one hand warned the canoes of wreckers off while with the other hand we toiled to save the ship.
crsnk10{_}4469{_}All of which was too much for Wada, who went daffy, and who finally quitted the Snark on the island of Ysabel, going ashore for good in a driving rain-storm, between two attacks of fever, while threatened with pneumonia.
crsnk10{_}4470{_}If he escapes being kai- kai'd, and if he can survive sores and fever which are riotous ashore, he can expect, if he is reasonably lucky, to get away from that place to the adjacent island in anywhere from six to eight weeks.
crsnk10{_}4471{_}He never did think much of my medicine, despite the fact that I successfully and at the first trail pulled two aching teeth for him.
crsnk10{_}4472{_}The Snark has been a hospital for months, and I confess that we are getting used to it.
crsnk10{_}4473{_}At Meringe Lagoon, where we careened and cleaned the Snark's copper, there were times when only one man of us was able to go into the water, while the three white men on the plantation ashore were all down with fever.
crsnk10{_}4474{_}At the moment of writing this we are lost at sea somewhere northeast of Ysabel and trying vainly to find Lord Howe Island, which is an atoll that cannot be sighted unless one is on top of it.
crsnk10{_}4475{_}The chronometer has gone wrong.
crsnk10{_}4476{_}The sun does not shine anyway, nor can I get a star observation at night, and we have had nothing but squalls and rain for days and days.
crsnk10{_}4477{_}The cook is gone.
crsnk10{_}4478{_}Nakata, who has been trying to be both cook and cabin boy, is down on his back with fever.
crsnk10{_}4479{_}Martin is just up from fever, and going down again.
crsnk10{_}4480{_}Charmian, whose fever has become periodical, is looking up in her date book to find when the next attack will be.
crsnk10{_}4481{_}Henry has begun to eat quinine in an expectant mood.
crsnk10{_}4482{_}And, since my attacks hit me with the suddenness of bludgeon-blows I do not know from moment to moment when I shall be brought down.
crsnk10{_}4483{_}By a mistake we gave our last flour away to some white men who did not have any flour.
crsnk10{_}4484{_}We don't know when we'll make land.
crsnk10{_}4485{_}Our Solomon sores are worse than ever, and more numerous.
crsnk10{_}4486{_}The corrosive sublimate was accidentally left ashore at Penduffryn; the peroxide of hydrogen is exhausted; and I am experimenting with boracic acid, lysol, and antiphlogystine.
crsnk10{_}4487{_}At any rate, if I fail in becoming a reputable M.D., it won't be from lack of practice.
crsnk10{_}4488{_}P.S.
crsnk10{_}4489{_}It is now two weeks since the foregoing was written, and Tehei, the only immune on board has been down ten days with far severer fever than any of us and is still down.
crsnk10{_}4490{_}His temperature has been repeatedly as high as 104, and his pulse 115.
crsnk10{_}4491{_}P.S.
crsnk10{_}4492{_}At sea, between Tasman atoll and Manning Straits.
crsnk10{_}4493{_}Tehei's attack developed into black water fever--the severest form of malarial fever, which, the doctor-book assures me, is due to some outside infection as well.
crsnk10{_}4494{_}Having pulled him through his fever, I am now at my wit's end, for he has lost his wits altogether.
crsnk10{_}4495{_}I am rather recent in practice to take up the cure of insanity.
crsnk10{_}4496{_}This makes the second lunacy case on this short voyage.
crsnk10{_}4497{_}P.S.
crsnk10{_}4498{_}Some day I shall write a book (for the profession), and entitle it, "Around the World on the Hospital Ship Snark."
crsnk10{_}4499{_}Even our pets have not escaped.
crsnk10{_}4500{_}We sailed from Meringe Lagoon with two, an Irish terrier and a white cockatoo.
crsnk10{_}4501{_}The terrier fell down the cabin companionway and lamed its nigh hind leg, then repeated the manoeuvre and lamed its off fore leg.
crsnk10{_}4502{_}At the present moment it has but two legs to walk on.
crsnk10{_}4503{_}Fortunately, they are on opposite sides and ends, so that she can still dot and carry two.
crsnk10{_}4504{_}The cockatoo was crushed under the cabin skylight and had to be killed.
crsnk10{_}4505{_}This was our first funeral--though for that matter, the several chickens we had, and which would have made welcome broth for the convalescents, flew overboard and were drowned.
crsnk10{_}4506{_}Only the cockroaches flourish.
crsnk10{_}4507{_}Neither illness nor accident ever befalls them, and they grow larger and more carnivorous day by day, gnawing our finger-nails and toe-nails while we sleep.
crsnk10{_}4508{_}P.S.
crsnk10{_}4509{_}Charmian is having another bout with fever.
crsnk10{_}4510{_}Martin, in despair, has taken to horse-doctoring his yaws with bluestone and to blessing the Solomons.
crsnk10{_}4511{_}As for me, in addition to navigating, doctoring, and writing short stories, I am far from well.
crsnk10{_}4512{_}With the exception of the insanity cases, I'm the worst off on board.
crsnk10{_}4513{_}I shall catch the next steamer to Australia and go on the operating table.
crsnk10{_}4514{_}Among my minor afflictions, I may mention a new and mysterious one.
crsnk10{_}4515{_}For the past week my hands have been swelling as with dropsy.
crsnk10{_}4516{_}It is only by a painful effort that I can close them.
crsnk10{_}4517{_}A pull on a rope is excruciating.
crsnk10{_}4518{_}The sensations are like those that accompany severe chilblains.
crsnk10{_}4519{_}Also, the skin is peeling off both hands at an alarming rate, besides which the new skin underneath is growing hard and thick.
crsnk10{_}4520{_}The doctor-book fails to mention this disease.
crsnk10{_}4521{_}Nobody knows what it is.
crsnk10{_}4522{_}P.S.
crsnk10{_}4523{_}Well, anyway, I've cured the chronometer.
crsnk10{_}4524{_}After knocking about the sea for eight squally, rainy days, most of the time hove to, I succeeded in catching a partial observation of the sun at midday.
crsnk10{_}4525{_}From this I worked up my latitude, then headed by log to the latitude of Lord Howe, and ran both that latitude and the island down together.
crsnk10{_}4526{_}Here I tested the chronometer by longitude sights and found it something like three minutes out.
crsnk10{_}4527{_}Since each minute is equivalent to fifteen miles, the total error can be appreciated.
crsnk10{_}4528{_}By repeated observations at Lord Howe I rated the chronometer, finding it to have a daily losing error of seven-tenths of a second.
crsnk10{_}4529{_}Now it happens that a year ago, when we sailed from Hawaii, that selfsame chronometer had that selfsame losing error of seven-tenths of a second.
crsnk10{_}4530{_}Since that error was faithfully added every day, and since that error, as proved by my observations at Lord Howe, has not changed, then what under the sun made that chronometer all of a sudden accelerate and catch up with itself three minutes?
crsnk10{_}4531{_}Can such things be?
crsnk10{_}4532{_}Expert watchmakers say no; but I say that they have never done any expert watch-making and watch-rating in the Solomons.
crsnk10{_}4533{_}That it is the climate is my only diagnosis.
crsnk10{_}4534{_}At any rate, I have successfully doctored the chronometer, even if I have failed with the lunacy cases and with Martin's yaws.
crsnk10{_}4535{_}P.S.
crsnk10{_}4536{_}Martin has just tried burnt alum, and is blessing the Solomons more fervently than ever.
crsnk10{_}4537{_}P.S.
crsnk10{_}4538{_}Between Manning Straits and Pavuvu Islands.
crsnk10{_}4539{_}Henry has developed rheumatism in his back, ten skins have peeled off my hands and the eleventh is now peeling, while Tehei is more lunatic than ever and day and night prays God not to kill him.
crsnk10{_}4540{_}Also, Nakata and I are slashing away at fever again.
crsnk10{_}4541{_}And finally up to date, Nakata last evening had an attack of ptomaine poisoning, and we spent half the night pulling him through.
crsnk10{_}4542{_}BACK WORD    The Snark was forty-three feet on the water-line and fifty-five over all, with fifteen feet beam (tumble-home sides) and seven feet eight inches draught.
crsnk10{_}4543{_}She was ketch-rigged, carrying flying-jib, jib, fore-staysail, main-sail, mizzen, and spinnaker.
crsnk10{_}4544{_}There were six feet of head-room below, and she was crown-decked and flush-decked.
crsnk10{_}4545{_}There were four alleged WATER-TIGHT compartments.
crsnk10{_}4546{_}A seventy-horse power auxiliary gas-engine sporadically furnished locomotion at an approximate cost of twenty dollars per mile.
crsnk10{_}4547{_}A five-horse power engine ran the pumps when it was in order, and on two occasions proved capable of furnishing juice for the search-light.
crsnk10{_}4548{_}The storage batteries worked four or five times in the course of two years.
crsnk10{_}4549{_}The fourteen-foot launch was rumoured to work at times, but it invariably broke down whenever I stepped on board.
crsnk10{_}4550{_}But the Snark sailed.
crsnk10{_}4551{_}It was the only way she could get anywhere.
crsnk10{_}4552{_}She sailed for two years, and never touched rock, reef, nor shoal.
crsnk10{_}4553{_}She had no inside ballast, her iron keel weighed five tons, but her deep draught and high freeboard made her very stiff.
crsnk10{_}4554{_}Caught under full sail in tropic squalls, she buried her rail and deck many times, but stubbornly refused to turn turtle.
crsnk10{_}4555{_}She steered easily, and she could run day and night, without steering, close-by, full- and-by, and with the wind abeam.
crsnk10{_}4556{_}With the wind on her quarter and the sails properly trimmed, she steered herself within two points, and with the wind almost astern she required scarcely three points for self-steering.
crsnk10{_}4557{_}The Snark was partly built in San Francisco.
crsnk10{_}4558{_}The morning her iron keel was to be cast was the morning of the great earthquake.
crsnk10{_}4559{_}Then came anarchy.
crsnk10{_}4560{_}Six months overdue in the building, I sailed the shell of her to Hawaii to be finished, the engine lashed to the bottom, building materials lashed on deck.
crsnk10{_}4561{_}Had I remained in San Francisco for completion, I'd still be there.
crsnk10{_}4562{_}As it was, partly built, she cost four times what she ought to have cost.
crsnk10{_}4563{_}The Snark was born unfortunately.
crsnk10{_}4564{_}She was libelled in San Francisco, had her cheques protested as fraudulent in Hawaii, and was fined for breach of quarantine in the Solomons.
crsnk10{_}4565{_}To save themselves, the newspapers could not tell the truth about her.
crsnk10{_}4566{_}When I discharged an incompetent captain, they said I had beaten him to a pulp.
crsnk10{_}4567{_}When one young man returned home to continue at college, it was reported that I was a regular Wolf Larsen, and that my whole crew had deserted because I had beaten it to a pulp.
crsnk10{_}4568{_}In fact the only blow struck on the Snark was when the cook was manhandled by a captain who had shipped with me under false pretences, and whom I discharged in Fiji.
crsnk10{_}4569{_}Also, Charmian and I boxed for exercise; but neither of us was seriously maimed.
crsnk10{_}4570{_}The voyage was our idea of a good time.
crsnk10{_}4571{_}I built the Snark and paid for it, and for all expenses.
crsnk10{_}4572{_}I contracted to write thirty-five thousand words descriptive of the trip for a magazine which was to pay me the same rate I received for stories written at home.
crsnk10{_}4573{_}Promptly the magazine advertised that it was sending me especially around the world for itself.
crsnk10{_}4574{_}It was a wealthy magazine.
crsnk10{_}4575{_}And every man who had business dealings with the Snark charged three prices because forsooth the magazine could afford it.
crsnk10{_}4576{_}Down in the uttermost South Sea isle this myth obtained, and I paid accordingly.
crsnk10{_}4577{_}To this day everybody believes that the magazine paid for everything and that I made a fortune out of the voyage.
crsnk10{_}4578{_}It is hard, after such advertising, to hammer it into the human understanding that the whole voyage was done for the fun of it.
crsnk10{_}4579{_}I went to Australia to go into hospital, where I spent five weeks.
crsnk10{_}4580{_}I spent five months miserably sick in hotels.
crsnk10{_}4581{_}The mysterious malady that afflicted my hands was too much for the Australian specialists.
crsnk10{_}4582{_}It was unknown in the literature of medicine.
crsnk10{_}4583{_}No case like it had ever been reported.
crsnk10{_}4584{_}It extended from my hands to my feet so that at times I was as helpless as a child.
crsnk10{_}4585{_}On occasion my hands were twice their natural size, with seven dead and dying skins peeling off at the same time.
crsnk10{_}4586{_}There were times when my toe-nails, in twenty-four hours, grew as thick as they were long.
crsnk10{_}4587{_}After filing them off, inside another twenty-four hours they were as thick as before.
crsnk10{_}4588{_}The Australian specialists agreed that the malady was non-parasitic, and that, therefore, it must be nervous.
crsnk10{_}4589{_}It did not mend, and it was impossible for me to continue the voyage.
crsnk10{_}4590{_}The only way I could have continued it would have been by being lashed in my bunk, for in my helpless condition, unable to clutch with my hands, I could not have moved about on a small rolling boat.
crsnk10{_}4591{_}Also, I said to myself that while there were many boats and many voyages, I had but one pair of hands and one set of toe-nails.
crsnk10{_}4592{_}Still further, I reasoned that in my own climate of California I had always maintained a stable nervous equilibrium.
crsnk10{_}4593{_}So back I came.
crsnk10{_}4594{_}Since my return I have completely recovered.
crsnk10{_}4595{_}And I have found out what was the matter with me.
crsnk10{_}4596{_}I encountered a book by Lieutenant- Colonel Charles E. Woodruff of the United States Army entitled "Effects of Tropical Light on White Men."
crsnk10{_}4597{_}Then I knew.
crsnk10{_}4598{_}Later, I met Colonel Woodruff, and learned that he had been similarly afflicted.
crsnk10{_}4599{_}Himself an Army surgeon, seventeen Army surgeons sat on his case in the Philippines, and, like the Australian specialists, confessed themselves beaten.
crsnk10{_}4600{_}In brief, I had a strong predisposition toward the tissue-destructiveness of tropical light.
crsnk10{_}4601{_}I was being torn to pieces by the ultra-violet rays just as many experimenters with the X-ray have been torn to pieces.
crsnk10{_}4602{_}In passing, I may mention that among the other afflictions that jointly compelled the abandonment of the voyage, was one that is variously called the healthy man's disease, European Leprosy, and Biblical Leprosy.
crsnk10{_}4603{_}Unlike True Leprosy, nothing is known of this mysterious malady.
crsnk10{_}4604{_}No doctor has ever claimed a cure for a case of it, though spontaneous cures are recorded.
crsnk10{_}4605{_}It comes, they know not how.
crsnk10{_}4606{_}It is, they know not what.
crsnk10{_}4607{_}It goes, they know not why.
crsnk10{_}4608{_}Without the use of drugs, merely by living in the wholesome California climate, my silvery skin vanished.
crsnk10{_}4609{_}The only hope the doctors had held out to me was a spontaneous cure, and such a cure was mine.
crsnk10{_}4610{_}A last word:  the test of the voyage.
crsnk10{_}4611{_}It is easy enough for me or any man to say that it was enjoyable.
crsnk10{_}4612{_}But there is a better witness, the one woman who made it from beginning to end.
crsnk10{_}4613{_}In hospital when I broke the news to Charmian that I must go back to California, the tears welled into her eyes.
crsnk10{_}4614{_}For two days she was wrecked and broken by the knowledge that the happy, happy voyage was abandoned.
